Resolving Apparent Conflict Between Hadiths: Tarjih with Quran and Ijma
Defending author's sequence using tarjīḥ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi tarjih to resolve apparent conflict between two hadiths by prioritizing external evidences such as the Quran and ijma.

Core Idea
When two hadiths conflict, Hanafis use Quran and ijma as external preponderators.

This passage defends the author's arrangement of placing tasmiyah before tahmid. Some objected that this contradicts the intended equality. The commentator explains that two hadiths appear to conflict, so one must be given precedence using external evidences. The Hanafi method of tarjih favors the Quran and ijma, both of which place tasmiyah first.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent conflict (ta'āruḍ)
Two hadiths exist: one commands beginning with tasmiyah, the other with tahmid. They cannot both be acted upon simultaneously.
2
Recognize the need for tarjīḥ
Since both cannot be followed, one must be preferred. The Hanafi rule is to use external evidences (Quran, ijma, etc.) to give preference.
3
Apply tarjīḥ using Quran and ijma
The Quran always begins with bismillah before alhamdulillah, and the consensus of the ummah is to do the same. Therefore, tasmiyah is given precedence over tahmid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دفع ہے اس اشکال کا کہ مصنف نے ترتیب ذکری کے اندر تسمیہ کو مقدم ذکر کیا ہے اور محمد کو مؤخراً یہ تو تسویہ کی جو قصد کی تھی اس کے خلاف ہے تو اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے کہا کہ لان النصين متعارضان ظاهرا یعنی دونوں حدیثیں ظاہرا آپس میں متعارض ہیں کیونکہ ایک حدیث ابتداء بالتسمیہ کو ضروری قرار دیتی ہے اور دوسری ابتداء بالتحمید کو اور دونوں پر بیک وقت عمل کرنا مشکل ہے اذ الابتداء باحد الامرين اخر للآخر کیونکہ ایک امر کے ساتھ ابتداء دوسرے کے ساتھ ابتداء کرنے کو فوت کر دیتا ہے لہذا ہمارے لئے یہی ممکن ہے کہ ایک کو دوسرے پر مقدم کریں اس کے ساتھ ابتدار حقیقی ہو جائے گی دوسرے کے ساتھ اضافی یعنی با نسبت ماسوی الاول کے باقی رہی یہ بات کہ کس کے ساتھ ابتدا حقیقی ہونی چاہئے تو اس کو واضح کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ مصنف نے تقدیم تسمیہ کر کے اس کے ساتھ ابتدار حقیقی کی اور حمد کے ساتھ اضافی کیونکہ کتاب مجید پر عمل کرنا اسی کا متقاضی تھا کیونکہ قرآن مجید میں تسمیہ مقدم علی التحمید ہے اور اجماع امت بھی اسی پر منعقد ہے کہ وہ بھی اپنے افعال ذی بال میں تسمیہ کو مقدم علی التجميد کرتے ہیں۔ وترك العاطف یعنی جب تسمیہ اور حمد دونوں بصورت حال ہیں تو ان کے درمیان حرف عاطف کیوں استعمال نہیں کیا مثلاً فحامدا یا وحامدًا بولتا اور اس کا عطف متبو کا پر ہو جاتا جو بسملہ کی باجارہ کا متعلق ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا لئلا يشعر بالتبعية يعني حرف عطف اس چیز کی طرف مشعر ہوتا کہ ادائیگی حمد بالتبع ہے مقصود بالذات نہیں ہے کیونکہ تابعية في اللفظ تابعية في المعنیٰ پر دال ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں جو تسویه بين التسميه والتجميد مقصود تھا وہ مختل اور منتقض ہو جاتا ولا يجوزان يكون حامدا الا يعني لفظ يقول جو يقول لما وفقني کے اندر مذکور ہے اس کے فاعل سے حامدا کو حال بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
This is a response to the objection that the author mentioned tasmiyah first in the arrangement and Muhammad later—this contradicts the equality he intended. So he said: Because the two texts are apparently conflicting: one hadith requires beginning with tasmiyah, the other with tahmid, and it is difficult to act on both simultaneously, since beginning with one precludes beginning with the other. Therefore, the only option for us is to give precedence to one over the other, making it a real beginning and the other additional relative to what comes after. To clarify which should be the real beginning, the author gave precedence to tasmiyah and made the real beginning with it, and made hamd additional, because acting upon the Noble Book requires that—since in the Noble Quran tasmiyah precedes tahmid, and the consensus of the ummah is also upon this: they give precedence to tasmiyah over tahmid in their important actions. And he omitted the conjunction: Since tasmiyah and hamd are both in the accusative state, why was a conjunction not used between them, e.g., saying 'fahamidan' or 'wahamidan', with the conjunction attached to the preceding word which is related to basmalah? The answer given is: so that it does not indicate subordination—the conjunction would suggest that hamd is performed subordinately, not as the primary intention, because subordination in wording indicates subordination in meaning. In that case, the intended equality between tasmiyah and tahmid would be disturbed and invalidated. And it is not permissible to make 'hamidan' a circumstantial accusative from the agent of 'yaqul' mentioned in 'yaqulu lima waffaqani'—that is incorrect.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage, likely from a gloss (hāshiya) on Al-Tawḍīḥ, addresses an objection regarding the author's sequence: why tasmiyah (bismillah) is placed before tahmid (alhamdulillah), contradicting the intended equality? The commentator explains that two hadiths apparently conflict regarding which phrase should begin. Since acting on both simultaneously is impossible, one must be given precedence. The author chose to prioritize tasmiyah based on Quranic practice (where bismillah always precedes alhamdulillah) and the consensus of the ummah. The commentator also addresses the grammatical omission of a conjunction (wāw) between tasmiyah and tahmid: if a conjunction were used, it would imply that hamd is subordinate to tasmiyah, undermining the intentional equality. The passage further rejects the interpretation of 'hamidan' as a circumstantial accusative from the verb 'yaqul', listing multiple grammatical impediments. This is a standard Hanafi usul approach that prioritizes textual and consensus evidence when reconciling apparently conflicting reports.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'āruḍ): Apparent conflict between two textual evidences that cannot be reconciled in practice.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'bismillah' (in the name of Allah).
التحميد (al-taḥmīd): Saying 'alhamdulillah' (all praise belongs to Allah).
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): The process of giving preference to one evidence over another using external indicators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author prioritize tasmiyah over tahmid in the book introduction?
A) Because a hadith explicitly says so
B) Because the Quran and ijma support it
C) Because it is easier to pronounce
D) Because the other hadith is weak

Key Takeaway
When two hadiths appear to conflict, the Hanafi school uses tarjīḥ with external evidences like the Quran and ijma to determine precedence.

Omission of Conjunction: Preserving Equality Between Tasmiyah and Tahmid
Grammatical defense of omitted conjunction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the conjunction was omitted between tasmiyah and tahmid and identify the Hanafi usul principle that subordination in wording indicates subordination in meaning.

Core Idea
Omission of a conjunction preserves the intended equality between two phrases.

After defending the sequence, the commentator addresses a grammatical objection: why is there no conjunction between 'bismillah' and 'alhamdulillah'? The answer reveals a deep usul principle: subordination in wording (with a conjunction) implies subordination in meaning, which would contradict the author's intention of equality. Thus, the conjunction is deliberately omitted to maintain taswiyah (equality).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the grammatical question
Tasmiyah and tahmid are both in the accusative case; one expects a conjunction (waw) between them, e.g., 'fahamidan' or 'wahamidan'. The author omitted it.
2
Understand the implication of a conjunction
In Hanafi usul, using a conjunction (al-'aṭf) indicates that the second element is subordinate (tabi'ah) to the first. This would imply that tahmid is secondary to tasmiyah.
3
Realize the author's intention of equality
The author intended taswiyah (equality) between tasmiyah and tahmid. A conjunction would create subordination, violating that intention. Hence, the conjunction is omitted to preserve equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دفع ہے اس اشکال کا کہ مصنف نے ترتیب ذکری کے اندر تسمیہ کو مقدم ذکر کیا ہے اور محمد کو مؤخراً یہ تو تسویہ کی جو قصد کی تھی اس کے خلاف ہے تو اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے کہا کہ لان النصين متعارضان ظاهرا یعنی دونوں حدیثیں ظاہرا آپس میں متعارض ہیں کیونکہ ایک حدیث ابتداء بالتسمیہ کو ضروری قرار دیتی ہے اور دوسری ابتداء بالتحمید کو اور دونوں پر بیک وقت عمل کرنا مشکل ہے اذ الابتداء باحد الامرين اخر للآخر کیونکہ ایک امر کے ساتھ ابتداء دوسرے کے ساتھ ابتداء کرنے کو فوت کر دیتا ہے لہذا ہمارے لئے یہی ممکن ہے کہ ایک کو دوسرے پر مقدم کریں اس کے ساتھ ابتدار حقیقی ہو جائے گی دوسرے کے ساتھ اضافی یعنی با نسبت ماسوی الاول کے باقی رہی یہ بات کہ کس کے ساتھ ابتدا حقیقی ہونی چاہئے تو اس کو واضح کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ مصنف نے تقدیم تسمیہ کر کے اس کے ساتھ ابتدار حقیقی کی اور حمد کے ساتھ اضافی کیونکہ کتاب مجید پر عمل کرنا اسی کا متقاضی تھا کیونکہ قرآن مجید میں تسمیہ مقدم علی التحمید ہے اور اجماع امت بھی اسی پر منعقد ہے کہ وہ بھی اپنے افعال ذی بال میں تسمیہ کو مقدم علی التجميد کرتے ہیں۔ وترك العاطف یعنی جب تسمیہ اور حمد دونوں بصورت حال ہیں تو ان کے درمیان حرف عاطف کیوں استعمال نہیں کیا مثلاً فحامدا یا وحامدًا بولتا اور اس کا عطف متبو کا پر ہو جاتا جو بسملہ کی باجارہ کا متعلق ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا لئلا يشعر بالتبعية يعني حرف عطف اس چیز کی طرف مشعر ہوتا کہ ادائیگی حمد بالتبع ہے مقصود بالذات نہیں ہے کیونکہ تابعية في اللفظ تابعية في المعنیٰ پر دال ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں جو تسویه بين التسميه والتجميد مقصود تھا وہ مختل اور منتقض ہو جاتا ولا يجوزان يكون حامدا الا يعني لفظ يقول جو يقول لما وفقني کے اندر مذکور ہے اس کے فاعل سے حامدا کو حال بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
This is a response to the objection that the author mentioned tasmiyah first in the arrangement and Muhammad later—this contradicts the equality he intended. So he said: Because the two texts are apparently conflicting: one hadith requires beginning with tasmiyah, the other with tahmid, and it is difficult to act on both simultaneously, since beginning with one precludes beginning with the other. Therefore, the only option for us is to give precedence to one over the other, making it a real beginning and the other additional relative to what comes after. To clarify which should be the real beginning, the author gave precedence to tasmiyah and made the real beginning with it, and made hamd additional, because acting upon the Noble Book requires that—since in the Noble Quran tasmiyah precedes tahmid, and the consensus of the ummah is also upon this: they give precedence to tasmiyah over tahmid in their important actions. The answer given is: so that it does not indicate subordination—the conjunction would suggest that hamd is performed subordinately, not as the primary intention, because subordination in wording indicates subordination in meaning. In that case, the intended equality between tasmiyah and tahmid would be disturbed and invalidated. And it is not permissible to make 'hamidan' a circumstantial accusative from the agent of 'yaqul' mentioned in 'yaqulu lima waffaqani'—that is incorrect.

Tasamuh vs Tadmeen: Defending Author's Usage in Usul al-Fiqh
Defending author's use of 'ba' by invoking tadmeen over tasamuh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tasamuh and tadmeen and apply the Hanafi preference for tadmeen in analyzing textual irregularities.

Core Idea
Tadmeen preserves the real meaning while implying another; tasamuh is only used when tadmeen is impossible.

In usul al-fiqh, understanding how a word can carry two meanings is crucial. This lesson examines a case where a phrase appears irregular—the author uses 'ba' instead of 'lam'. Is this a mere leniency (tasamuh) or a deliberate implication (tadmeen)? The passage defends tadmeen, citing Ibn Jinni. By mastering this distinction, you will strengthen your ability to analyze linguistic nuances in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the irregular usage
Locate the phrase 'wafaqani Allah' in the Arabic text. Note that the verb 'wafaqa' normally takes 'lam', but the author used 'ba'. This is the point of contention.
The irregularity is the transitivity with 'ba' instead of 'lam'.
2
Distinguish tasamuh and tadmeen
Read the definitions in the passage: tasamuh uses a word outside its real meaning without proper connection; tadmeen implies a second meaning by indicating a deleted verb via its connector.
Tadmeen avoids combining reality and metaphor in one word.
3
Understand the Hanafi preference
Note that the author argues tadmeen is preferred whenever possible, citing Ibn Jinni's statement on its vastness. Tasamuh is only used when tadmeen is impossible.
This preference stems from linguistic precision.
4
Analyze the defense
See how the author explains that 'wafaqani' carries the real meaning of tawfiq and the implied meaning of tashrif (honoring). The 'ba' indicates the deleted verb 'sharrafani'.
This explanation removes the need to assume tasamuh.
5
Evaluate the commentator's accusation
The commentator accused the author of frequent tasamuh. The author responds that this accusation is baseless because tadmeen is a well-established mechanism in Arabic.
The practical consequence: the author's usage is valid and needs no correction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یہ مقام دعا ہے اس لئے معنی بخت مراد ہونا چاہیئے اور متعارف عند العامہ یہ ہے کہ ایسا لفظ استعمال کیا جائے جس کے دو معنیٰ ہوں اور ان میں سے کوئی ایک مطلقا مراد ہو قرب و بعد کا سوال عند العامہ نہیں تو پھر اس عبادت کا محمول علی الایہام ہونا ظاہر ہے ۔ وفقني الله التوفيق جعل الاسباب موافقة اصطلاح شریعت میں موافقت للمطلوب الخیر کی قید کی جاتی ہے اگر مطلوب شر کے اسباب مہیا اور متوافق ہو جائیں تو اصطلاح شریعت میں اسے خذلان کہتے ہیں اس لئے و فقہم اللہ کے مقابلہ میں خذ لہم اللہ کہا جاتا ہے و يعدى باللام یعنی مفعول ثانی کی طرف اس کا تعدیہ باللام ہوتا ہے نہ کہ بالیا، مصنف نے یہاں اسے متعدی بالباء کیا ہے تو یہ تعدیہ یا تو مبنی علی التسامح ہے یا علی التضمين لمعنی التشریف ای شرفنی اللہ تعالیٰ تالیف تسامح کا معنی ایک لفظ کو معنی حقیقی کے غیر میں استعمال کرنا بغیر کسی علاقہ مقبولہ کے اور بغیر قرینہ دالہ کے صرف اعتماد علی ظہورالفہم ہوتا ہے اور تضمین یہ ہوتی ہے کہ ایک لفظ ذکر کر کے اس کے ساتھ حقیقی معنیٰ مراد لیا جائے اور اس کے ساتھ ایک دوسرا معنیٰ تبعا لفظ آخرہ کے ساتھ مراد ہو جو وہ مذکور نہیں صرف اس کا متعلق اور صلہ ذکر کر کے اس محذوف پر دلالت کرائی جاتی ہے جیسے یہاں وفتنی سے حقیقی معنی توفیق کا مراد ہے لیکن اس کے تابع معنی تشریف بلفظ شرفنی بھی مراد ہے جو غیر مذکور ہے۔ اس پر صرف اس کا صلہ یعنی حرف بالا کر دلالت کرائی گئی ہے اس کا فائدہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ ایک لفظ کے ساتھ دو معنیٰ کا فائدہ حاصل ہو جاتا ہے لیکن دوسرا لفظ ضمنا مراد ضرور ہوتا ہے تاکہ ایک ہی لفظ کے ساتھ جمع بین الحقيقة والمجاز لازم نہ آئے ۔ کثیر ا ما يتسامح الم اس تسامح پر بلا وجہ محمول کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے جبکہ باب تضمین بہت وسیع ہے کما قال ابن جینی " لو نقلت تضمینات العرب لاجتمعت مجلدات " ہاں اگر کہیں تضمین نہ ہو سکے تو مجبور ا تسامح پر محمول کیا جائے گا لہذا شارح کا تسامح بالكثرة کا الزام على المصنف بلاوجہ ہے
This is a place of supplication, therefore the meaning intended should be 'good fortune'. The common convention is that a word with two meanings is used and one of them is absolutely intended; the question of proximity and distance does not exist among the common people. So it is clear that this worship is carried on the meaning of equivocation (al-iham). 'And may Allah grant me success (wafaqani Allah)' making causes suitable. In the terminology of Shari'ah, suitability is restricted to the desired good. If the causes for desired evil become prepared and suitable, in the terminology of Shari'ah it is called khidhlan (abandonment). Therefore, in contrast to 'wafaqahum Allah', it is said 'khadhalahum Allah'. It is transitive with lam, meaning its transitivity to the second object is with lam, not with ba. The author has made it transitive with ba here, so this transitivity is either based on tasamuh (leniency) or on tadmeen (implication) for the meaning of tashrif (honoring), i.e., 'sharrafani Allah ta'ala bi al-ta'lif'. Tasamuh means using a word for other than its real meaning without an accepted connection and without an indicating context, only relying on the apparent understanding. Tadmeen is that a word is mentioned, its real meaning is intended, and along with it a second meaning is intended followingly with another word that is not mentioned; only its object and connector are mentioned to indicate that deleted word. For example, here, with 'wafaqani', the real meaning of tawfiq (success) is intended, but along with it the subsidiary meaning of tashrif by the word 'sharrafani' is also intended, though not mentioned. Only its connector, i.e., the letter ba, indicates it. The benefit is that two meanings are obtained with one word, but the second word is necessarily implied, so that combining reality and metaphor in one word does not become necessary. Often leniency occurs; there is no need to carry it on tasamuh without reason when the chapter of tadmeen is very vast, as Ibn Jinni said: 'If the tadmeen of the Arabs were collected, it would fill volumes.' Yes, if tadmeen cannot be done, then out of necessity it will be carried on tasamuh. Therefore, the commentator's accusation of frequent tasamuh against the author is baseless.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis defending the author's peculiar usage of the transitive preposition 'ba' instead of the expected 'lam' in the phrase 'wafaqani Allah'. The commentator argues that this is not an instance of tasamuh (linguistic leniency) but rather tadmeen (implication), where the verb 'wafaqani' simultaneously carries the meaning of 'sharrafani' (to honor), and the 'ba' indicates the implied verb. The passage clarifies both usul terms: tasamuh is using a word outside its real meaning without a valid link or context, while tadmeen involves intending a second meaning along with the first by implying another verb, thus avoiding combining literal and figurative meanings in one word. The commentator supports this by citing Ibn Jinni's statement on the expansiveness of tadmeen in Arabic, and concludes that the commentator's criticism of the author for frequent tasamuh is unfounded.

Key Terms
تسامح (tasamuh): Using a word in a non-real meaning without an accepted connection or indicating context, solely relying on apparent understanding.
تضمين (tadmeen): Implying a second meaning along with the real meaning of a word by indicating a deleted verb through its object or connector.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when should a linguistic usage be explained by tadmeen rather than tasamuh?
A) When the usage is irregular and no other explanation exists.
B) When tadmeen is possible, even if the implied word is not mentioned.
C) Only when the commentator explicitly allows it.
D) When the usage is metaphorical and the context is clear.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, tadmeen is the preferred explanation for irregular prepositional usage, and tasamuh is only used when tadmeen is impossible.

The Linguistic Nature of 'الكلم' and the Generality of Indefinite Plurals
Linguistic and usul analysis of 'الكلم الطيب' as ism jins and the function of 'من محامد'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the word 'كلم' as an ism jins and apply the Hanafi position that an indefinite plural can achieve generality when qualified by a general attribute.

Core Idea
The word 'كلم' is ism jins, singular in form, plural in meaning; its indefinite plural 'محامد' gains generality via a general attribute.

In this lesson, we analyse the linguistic structure of the Qur'anic phrase 'الكلم الطيب' as interpreted by Sadr al-Shariah and his commentator. The passage clarifies that 'كلم' is not a true plural but a generic noun, and it explains how the indefinite plural 'من محامد' functions as a circumstantial adjunct that specifies the type of good words. Understanding this analysis is fundamental for Hanafi usul al-fiqh, as it affects how indefinite nouns are treated in deriving legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Analyse the metaphorical meaning of 'الصعود'
Notice that the text interprets 'الصعود' in the phrase 'صعود إلى الله' metaphorically as attention to high rank, not physical ascent, because Allah is beyond space and direction. This reflects the Hanafi theological principle of tanzih.
2
Classify 'كلم' linguistically
Compare 'كلم' to 'تمر' as a generic noun (ism jins). Note that both are singular in form but plural in meaning. Evidence: the masculine adjective 'الطيب' and the measure 'فعل' (with kasrah) not being a plural pattern.
The text provides two examples: 'نخل منقعر' (masculine adjective) and 'نخل خاوية' (feminine adjective) to show flexibility.
3
Identify the syntactic function of 'من محامد'
The commentator explicitly states that 'من محامد' is a hal (circumstantial adjunct) from 'الكلم الطيب'. It explains what kind of good words are meant, removing the ambiguity of 'الكلم'.
The text cites the hadith 'فحيا بها وجه الرحمن' as a proof that the good words are praises.
4
Resolve the objection about indefinite plural's generality
The objector argues: 'الكلم' is definite and general (due to lam al-istighraq), so how can an indefinite plural 'محامد' explain it? The commentator gives two answers: (1) the indefinite becomes general when qualified by a general attribute (وصف عام), and (2) the indefinite form here is for multitude (التنكير للتكثير), which implies generality.
The first answer is more explicit and is supported by the example 'امرأة كوفية'.
5
Evaluate the two justifications in Hanafi usul
Understand that the second justification ('التنكير للتكثير') is a separate usul principle that indefinite plurals can indicate generality when used for multitude. This is relevant for commands like 'اعتق رقبة' if 'رقبة' is considered indefinite plural.
The text accepts both as valid, showing flexibility in Hanafi methodology.

And 'الصعود' means movement from a lower place to something higher in spatial and directional position. Since here the ascension is to Allah who is free from spatiality and directions, it is used metaphorically for attention to a high rank or status. 'والكلم من الكلمة' means that the relationship of 'كلم' to 'كلمة' is like the relationship of 'تمر' to 'تمرة'. Just as 'تمر' is a generic noun for 'تمرة' and the gender without 'ta' is a singular with 'ta', similarly 'كلمة' is a singular with 'ta', and 'كلم' without 'ta' is at the level of gender, applying to both few and many. In this generic sense, it is called a plural, but in word form it is singular and in meaning plural. Considering the word aspect, its modifier can be masculine, like 'نخل منقعر', and considering the meaning aspect, its modifier can be feminine, like 'نخل خاوية', because the feminine adjective is used for non-rational plurals. The state of 'كلمة' to 'نخلة' is like 'تمر' to 'تمرة'. Since the predominant usage of 'كلم' is for many, not for one or two, some have misunderstood it to be a plural of 'كلمة' and not a generic noun like 'تمر' and 'تمرة'. But the reality is as explained. The masculine modifier in 'الكلم الطيب' indicates that 'كلم' is a generic noun, singular in word and plural in meaning, because the measure 'فعل' with a kasrah on the 'ayn is not among the measures of the plural. Therefore, it cannot be considered a plural in form. So it is not appropriate to doubt that the word 'كلم' is plural like... [page 42] ...two examples were given: one 'تمر' which is a generic noun, and the other 'رکب' which is a collective noun. Both share the characteristic of being plural in meaning but not in word or form; they are singular. And the word 'كلم' is definitely like that. It is not a plural in word and form like 'نسب' and 'رتب' which are plurals of 'نسبة' and 'رتبة' respectively. 'كلم' is not like that. Therefore, the author's phrase 'إن كان جمعا' contains some offensiveness because he used 'إن' expressing doubt, which was not appropriate. To remove this offensiveness, it is explained that 'إن كان جمعا' is a conditional and its apodosis is omitted, based on his statement 'وكل جمع يفارق واحده بالتاء'. The intended meaning is: 'والكلم إن كان جمعا فهو جمع يفرق بينه وبين واحده بالتاء, وكل جمع كذلك'. So the author's purpose is that it is actually a plural in meaning and in reality a generic noun, singular in word, not plural, because the distinction between it and its singular is by 'ta', and whatever is like that is a generic noun with plural meaning. Therefore, the word 'كلم' is certainly like that. Now with this interpretation, there is no doubt or offensiveness. And it was also said in removing the offensiveness that the word 'إن' is used for doubt from the addressee who is an inquirer, based on the statement of some grammar scholars. His statement 'من محامد' is a circumstantial adjunct (hal) from 'الكلم'. That is, the author's word 'من محامد' is syntactically a hal from 'الكلم الطيب' and an explanation of it. Since 'الكلم' had some ambiguity, he explained it with 'من محامد', and the proof of the explanation is the hadith of the Prophet which is of the category of glorification and praise. 'فحيا بها وجه الرحمن' means the angel presents it as a greeting before the essence of the Most Merciful. If the person praising has no righteous deeds, this praise is not accepted in the divine court. 'والعمل الصالح' ... and he made it reach the place of acceptance. 'وانما صلح الجمع المنكر'... Because 'الكلم' is a generic noun defined by the article of inclusion (al-istighraq) which indicates generality and inclusion, while 'محامد' is an indefinite plural which according to the author does not indicate generality and inclusion, so how can it provide explanation of 'الكلم'? Two answers were given: one is that 'إن النكرة تعم' meaning when an indefinite noun is accompanied by a general attribute, then due to the generality of the attribute, the qualified indefinite noun becomes general in the sense of that attribute, like 'امرأة كوفية' includes every woman attributed to Kufa. Here also 'لا أصولها من مشاريع الخ' is a general attribute including every kind of good words. For this reason, 'محامد' also becomes general and inclusive. The second answer: 'ولأن التنكير هنا للتكثير' meaning the indefinite form here is for multitude, which is beneficial for generality and suitable for generalization. 'والمحامد جمع محمدة' meaning 'محامد' is the plural of 'محمدة' which is a mimi verbal noun and means praise, and praise is in exchange...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of the matn's phrase 'الكلم الطيب الصاعد إليه من محامد'. The commentator explains each component: first, the metaphorical meaning of 'الصعود' when applied to Allah, second, the linguistic nature of 'كلم' as a generic noun (ism jins) rather than a true plural, supported by the masculine adjective 'الطيب' and the weight 'فعل' not being a plural pattern. He then addresses an apparent doubt created by the author's use of 'إن' in 'إن كان جمعا', providing two reconciliations. The second major point is the explanation of 'من محامد' as a circumstantial adjunct (hal) that specifies the type of good words. The commentator then faces an objection: how can an indefinite plural (محامد) explain a definite generic noun (الكلم) that is general? He gives two solutions: one based on the indefinite becoming general when qualified by a general description, and the other based on the indefinite form indicating multitude (تكثير) which implies generality. The passage concludes by defining 'محامد' as the plural of 'محمدة'.

Key Terms
صعود (su'ud): Metaphorically for attention to a high rank, not physical ascension.
كلم (kalim): Generic noun (اسم جنس) for words, singular in form but plural in meaning.
محامد (mahamid): Plural of 'محمدة', meaning praises.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the grammatical function of 'من محامد' in relation to 'الكلم الطيب' according to the commentator?
A) Badal
B) Hal
C) Sifah
D) Tamyiz

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, linguistic precision matters: 'كلم' is an ism jins, and indefinite plurals can achieve generality through a general attribute or the indication of multitude.

The Singular-Form General Word: The Case of 'al-Kalim' and the Conditional Particle 'In'
Examination of the grammatical status of 'al-kalim' and resolution of an apparent doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the grammatical category of 'al-kalim' as an ism jins and apply the Hanafi usul principle that a conditional particle does not necessarily express doubt.

Core Idea
A word can be general in meaning yet singular in form—'al-kalim' is not a plural but an ism jins.

This passage begins by examining the word 'al-kalim'. Although it appears singular, it denotes a plurality of words. The original author used the phrase 'in kāna jam‘an' (if it is a plural), which might seem to express doubt. The commentator explains that this is a conditional construction with an omitted apodosis, not grammatical doubt. This lesson unpacks that analysis and the principle that the grammatical form of a word does not determine its legal generality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical nature of 'al-kalim'
Look at the comparison with 'tamr' and 'rutab'. They are singular in form but plural in meaning. 'Al-kalim' is similar.
Also known as ism jins or ism jam‘.
2
Understand the apparent doubt
The author wrote 'in kāna jam‘an' which contains the particle 'in' (if) that could imply uncertainty. But the commentator says this causes unease (ḥazāzah).
3
Analyse the commentator's resolution
The conditional 'in' is not for doubt; it introduces a hypothetical with an omitted apodosis. The full meaning is: 'If it is a plural, then it is a plural that is distinguished from its singular by tā’.' So no doubt.
This is a common grammatical device.
4
Apply the principle
Recognize that the form of a word (singular vs plural) does not affect its capacity to indicate generality in legal texts. Hanafi usul treats such words as 'āmm if the context supports it.
This is distinct from the Shafi‘i approach which may require plural form for generality.

ر اور مرکب جمع ہے دو نظیریں پیش کیں ایک تمر کی جو اسم جنس ہے اور دوسری رکب کی جو اسم جمع ہے یہ دونوں اس امر میں مشترک ہیں کہ یہ معنی جمع ہیں اور لفظا و صیغہ جمع نہیں ہیں بلکہ مفرد ہیں اور لفظ کلم یقینا ایسے ہے وانه ليس نجمع یعنی لفظ کلم لفظا اور صیغہ جمع نہیں ہے جیسے کہ نسب اور رتب لفظی حیثیت سے نسبت اور رتبہ کی جمع ہیں کلم ایسے نہیں ہیں لہذا مصنف " کی عبارت ان کان جمعا میں ایک قسم کی مزازة یعنی تنفر اور سوزش ہے کیونکہ ان شکیہ استعمال کر کے اظہار شک کیا ہے جو کہ مناسب نہ تھا مصنف " کی کلام سے دفع حزازہ کے لئے یہ توجیہ کی جاتی ہے کہ ان کان جمعا شرط ہے اور اس کی جزا محذوف ہے جس پر اس کا قول و کل جمع الزوال سے تقدیر عبارت یوں ہے و الكلم ان کان جمعا فہو جمع يفرق بينه وبين واحده بالتا، وكل جمع لفرن خلاصہ یہ کہ مصنف کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ یہ در حقیقت جمع معنی ہے اور حقیقتاً جنس ہے لفظاً مفرد ہے جمع نہیں کیونکہ اس کے اور اس کے واحد کے درمیان فرق بالتاء ہے اور جو ایسے ہو وہ اسم جنس ہو کہ معنی جمع ہوتی ہے لہذا لفظ کلم بھی یقیناً ایسے ہے اب اس توجیہ کے لحاظ سے نہ شک ہے نہ حزازة وقيل ايض في درفع الحزازة ان كلمة إن محمولة على الشك من المخاطب المتوسم بناء على قول بعض ائمة النحو قوله من محامد حال من الكلم یعنی مصنف کا قول من محامد ترکیبی لحاظ سے الکلم الطیب سے حال ہے اور اس کی تبیین ہے چونکہ الکلم میں کچھ ابہام تھا اس لئے من محامد سے اس کی تبیین کر دی اور دلیل تبیین قول نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پیش کیا جو از قسم تسبیح و تحمید ہے۔
فحيا بها وجه الرحمن وجہ سے مراد ذات ہے یعنی فرشتہ ذات رحمن کے سامنے بطور تحیہ پیش کرتا ہے اگر اس حامد کے اعمال صالحہ بالکل نہ ہوں تو یہ حمد بارگاہ الہ میں قبول نہیں ہوتا والعمل الصالح یہ فعہ الى الى مكان القبول وانما صلح الجمع المنكر ام چونکہ الکلم اسم جنس معرف بلام الاستغراق ہے جو کہ عموم واستغراق کا افادہ کرتا ہے اور محامد جمع منکر ہے جو مصنف کے نزدیک عموم و استغراق کی مفید نہیں ہے تو یہ الکلم کی تبیین کا فائدہ کیسے دے سکتی ہے تو اس کے دو جواب دیدئیے ایک یہ کہ ان النكرة تعم یعنی جب نکرہ کے ساتھ وصف عام ملحق ہو جائے تو اس وقت عموم وصف کی وجہ سے نکرہ موصوفہ مہذا الوصف عموم کا مفید ہوتا ہے جیسے امراج کو فیہ میں لفظ امرآۃ ہر اس عورت کو شامل ہے جو منسوب الی الکوفہ ہے اور یہاں بھی لا صولها من مشاريع الخ وصف عام ہے جو ہر قسم کے کلمات طیبہ کو شامل ہے اسی وجہ سے محامد بھی عام مستغرق ہو جائے گا۔ دوسرا جواب یہ دیا ولان التنکیرا یعنی یہاں لفظ محامد کی تنگیر برائے تکثیر ہے جو مفید عموم ہو کر مناسب للتعميم ہے ۔ والمحامد جمع محمدة یعنی محامد جمع ہے محمد‎ کی جو کہ مصدر میمی ہے اور معنی الحمد ہے اور حمد مقابلہ الجمیل یعنی محمود کے کسی فعل جمیل کے مقابلہ میں ثنا ء اور تعظیم باللسان کرنا خواہ محمود سے کوئی نعمت واصلہ الی الحامد ہو یا نہ ہو چونکہ حمد مختص باللسان ہے اس لئے کلم کی تبیین اس کے ساتھ بہت مناسب للمقام ہے بخلاف شکر کے کہ وہ مختص باللسان نہیں اگرچہ اس کے اندر نعمت کا ہونا شرط ہے اس لئے شکر اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ بمقابلہ نعمت تعظیم منعم کا اظہار کیا جائے خواہ یہ قول رسانی کے ساتھ ہو یا عمل ارکانی اور اعتقاد جنانی کہ ساتھ۔ من مشارع الشرع میں لفظ مشارع جمع ہے مشرعة المار کی یعنی وہ نالیاں جن کے اندر پانی جاری رہتا ہے اور شاربین وارد ہوتے رہتے ہیں۔ الشرع والشریعہ بمعنی واحد یعنی وہ دین جو اللہ تعالیٰ نے اپنے عباد کے لئے مشروع فرمایا اور اس کو واضح اور ظاہر کر دیا۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ طریقہ معہودہ جو ثابت ہے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے جعلها اى جعل الشریعہ یعنی شریعت کو مصنف نے روضات و جنات سے تشبیہ دی جو مضمر فی النفس ہے یہ استعارہ مکیہ ہوا چونکہ مشارع یعنی پانی پینے کی نالیاں بساتین و جنات کے لوازمات سے ہیں تو شریعت کے لئے ان کا اثبات بطور استعارہ تخیلیہ کے ہے یعنی جیسے روضات وجنات میں مشارع ہوتے ہیں جن پر شار بین وارد ہوتے ہیں اسی طرح شریعت مطہرہ کے لئے بھی مشارع ہیں جن پر اللہ تعالیٰ کی رحمت و رضوان کے زلال کے پیاسے وارد ہوتے رہتے ہیں۔ زلال الماء الصافی کو کہتے ہیں۔ وبهذا الطريق ال يعنى مصنف نے اپنے قول قبول القبول نمار میں بھی اسی طرح کے استعارے پیش کئے ہیں پہلے قبول سے مراد باد صبا ہے اور دوسرے قبول سے مراد قبولیت عبادت تو قبول عبادت کو تشبیہ دی جہب الریح کے ساتھ یعنی اس سمت وجہہ کے ساتھ جس سے ہوا چلتی ہے کیونکہ قبول عبادت بھی ایک مہب ہے جہاں سے الطاف رحمن اور انوار غفران چلتے ہیں اور ظاہر ہوتے ہیں اور یہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے یہ استعارہ بالکنایہ ہو اور ریح الصبا یہ مہب الریح کے لوازمات سے ہے اس کا اثبات استعارہ تخیلیہ ہوا جیسے ریح الصبا کے ساتھ ابدان کی راحت اور اغصان کو نما حاصل ہوتا ہے اسی طرح صبار حمانی اور نور مغفرت کے ساتھ سکونِ قلب اور راحتِ دل حاصل ہوتی ہے اور ریح صبا عموما ان ایام میں چلتی ہے جب لیل و نہار آپس میں برابر ہو جاتے ہیں اور مطلع شمس یعنی مشرقی سمت سے چلتی ہے اور اس کے مقابل یعنی مغربی سمت سے جو ہوا چلتی ہے اسے دیور کہتے ہیں اہلِ عرب کا خیال ہے کہ دبوری ہوا بادل کو اٹھاتی ہے اور او سپر فضا میں لے جا کہ اس کو چلاتی ہے جب بادل اونچا ہو جاتا ہے تو ہٹ جاتی ہے پھر باد صبا اس بادل کا استقبال کرتی ہے اور مختلف ٹکڑوں کو ایک دوسرے پر لگا کہ ایک ہی ٹکڑا بنا لیتی ہے پھر بارش اترتی ہے جس کے ساتھ اشجار کا نشو نما ہوتا ہے قبول ثانی مصدر ہے لیکن ہے مصادر شازہ و
And a compound plural, he presented two examples: one of tamr which is an ism jins, and the second of rutab which is an ism jam‘. Both share that they are plural in meaning but not plural in word and form; rather they are singular. And the word kalim is certainly like that, and it is not a plural (jam‘). That is, the word kalim is not plural in word and form, like nasab and rutab which are plurals of nisbah and rutbah in terms of wording; kalim is not like that. Therefore, the author’s phrase 'in kana jam‘an' contains a kind of unease (ḥazāzah) because he used the particle 'in' indicating doubt, which was not appropriate. To remove this unease from the author’s speech, this explanation is given: that 'in kana jam‘an' is a conditional, and its apodosis is omitted, upon which his saying 'wa kullu jam‘in yufarraqu baynahu wa bayna wāḥidihi bi al-tā’' is based. The intended meaning is that it is actually a plural in meaning and actually a genus (jins), singular in word, not plural, because between it and its singular the difference is by the tā’. And whatever is like that is an ism jins whose meaning is plural. Hence the word kalim is certainly like that. Now according to this explanation, there is no doubt and no unease. And it is also said in removing the unease that the word 'in' is taken to indicate doubt on the part of the addressee who hypothesizes, based on the statement of some grammarians. His statement 'min mahāmida' is a hāl from al-kalim. That is, the author’s saying 'min mahāmida' is grammatically a hāl from al-kalim al-ṭayyib and is its clarification. Since al-kalim had some ambiguity, he clarified it with 'min mahāmida', and he presented as evidence for clarification the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which is of the type of tasbīḥ and taḥmīd. 'Fa-ḥayyā bihā wajha al-raḥmān' – by 'wajh' is meant essence (dhāt), i.e., the angel presents it as a greeting before the essence of the Merciful. If this praiser has no righteous deeds at all, then this praise is not accepted in the divine court. And 'al-‘amal al-ṣāliḥ' is... to the place of acceptance. And why does the indefinite plural suffice? Since al-kalim is an ism jins defined by lām al-istighrāq which indicates generality and inclusion, and mahāmida is an indefinite plural which, according to the author, does not indicate generality and inclusion, then how can it provide clarification for al-kalim? So two answers are given: one is that the indefinite becomes general (inna al-nakirata ta‘umm) – meaning when an indefinite is joined by a general description, then due to the generality of the description, the described indefinite becomes general in that description. For example, in 'imra’atin mā fīhā', the word 'imra’atin' includes every woman who is attributed to Kufa. And here too, 'lā uṣūlahā min mashārī‘i al-khayr' is a general description that includes all kinds of good words. For this reason, mahāmida also becomes fully general. The second answer is that the indefinite form (al-tankīr) here is for multiplication (li al-takthīr), which is general and suitable for generalizing. And al-mahāmida is the plural of maḥmada, which is a mīmī maṣdar and means al-ḥamd. And ḥamd is in contrast to al-jamīl, i.e., praise and exaltation by the tongue in response to a beautiful act of the praised one, whether or not a blessing has reached the praiser from the praised one. Since ḥamd is specific to the tongue, its clarification of kalim is very suitable for the context, unlike shukr which is not specific to the tongue, although it requires the presence of a blessing. Hence shukr is defined as expressing exaltation of the benefactor in response to a blessing, whether by speech, physical action, or inner belief. 'Min mashārī‘i al-shar‘i' - the word mashārī‘ is the plural of mashra‘ah al-mār, i.e., the channels in which water flows and drinkers constantly come. Al-shar‘ and al-sharī‘ah are synonymous, i.e., the religion that Allah has legislated for His servants and made clear and apparent. In summary, the established method that is proven from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). 'Ja‘alahā' i.e., ja‘ala al-sharī‘ah – the author likened the sharī‘ah to gardens and orchards, which is implicit in the self; this is a makkiyyah metaphor. Since mashārī‘ (water channels) are among the appurtenances of gardens, their establishment for the sharī‘ah is a figurative metaphor: just as gardens have channels upon which drinkers come, similarly the pure sharī‘ah has channels upon which those thirsty for the pure water of Allah’s mercy and pleasure come. 'Zulāl' is called clear water. 'Wa bi hādhā al-ṭarīq' – the author also presented similar metaphors in his saying 'qabūl al-qabūl namār'. The first 'qabūl' means the east wind, and the second 'qabūl' means acceptance of worship. So he likened the acceptance of worship to the direction of the wind, i.e., the direction from which the wind blows, because acceptance of worship is also a direction from which the favors of the Merciful and lights of forgiveness come and appear. This simile is implicit in the self, it is a metaphor by allusion, and 'rīḥ al-ṣabā' is among the appurtenances of the wind’s direction; its establishment is a figurative metaphor. Just as with the east wind there is comfort for bodies and growth for branches, similarly with the south wind and light of forgiveness there is tranquility of heart and comfort of the self. And the east wind generally blows when night and day become equal, and it blows from the sunrise direction. The wind that blows from the opposite, westerly direction is called 'dabūr'. The Arabs believe that the dabūr wind lifts clouds and drives them across the sky; when the cloud rises high, it withdraws. Then the east wind meets the cloud and brings different pieces together making one piece, then rain falls with which trees grow. 'Qabūl thānī' is a maṣdar but it is among irregular maṣādir.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharḥ) on a text from Al-Tawḍīḥ, focusing on the definition and grammatical nature of the word 'al-kalim' (الكلم). The commentator begins by comparing 'al-kalim' to two other words: 'tamr' (dates) and 'rutab' (ripe dates). Both 'tamr' and 'rutab' are singular in form but indicate a plural meaning; they are ism jins (nouns of genus) or ism jam‘ (collective nouns). Similarly, 'al-kalim' is singular in form but denotes a plurality of words. The author of the original text used the phrase 'in kāna jam‘an' (if it is a plural), which some might perceive as expressing doubt due to the particle 'in'. The commentator resolves this by explaining that 'in' here is a conditional particle, and its apodosis is omitted; the intended meaning is that if 'al-kalim' is considered a plural, it is a plural that differs from its singular by the addition of 'tā'' (like 'kalimah' and 'kalim'). This removes any sense of unease (ḥazāzah). The passage then discusses the phrase 'min maḥāmida' (from praises) as a descriptive phrase clarifying 'al-kalim al-ṭayyib'. The commentator notes that 'al-kalim' is defined by 'alif lām al-istighrāq' (the definite article for generality), indicating all words, while 'maḥāmida' is an indefinite plural which normally does not indicate generality. To justify its clarifying role, two answers are given: (1) an indefinite noun becomes general when it is described by a general description, and here 'lā uṣūlahā min mashārī‘ al-khayr' serves as a general description; (2) the indefinite form here is for multiplication (takthīr), which implies generality. The commentator then distinguishes between 'ḥamd' (praise) and 'shukr' (thankfulness). 'Ḥamd' is praise by the tongue for a voluntary beautiful act, regardless of any benefit to the praiser, and is specific to speech. 'Shukr' is gratitude for a blessing, expressed by speech, action, or belief, and requires the presence of a blessing. The passage ends with metaphorical interpretations of 'mashārī‘ al-shar‘' (channels of the law) and 'qabūl' (acceptance), likening the sharī‘ah to gardens with flowing water and the acceptance of worship to a wind bringing comfort. The commentary follows the author's order, clarifying each point with linguistic and legal reasoning typical of Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الكلم (al-kalim): A singular noun indicating a plural meaning, similar to ism jins or ism jam‘; defined by lām al-istighrāq to denote generality of words.
محامد (maḥāmida): Indefinite plural of maḥmada (a mīmī maṣdar meaning praise); used as a descriptive phrase to clarify the generality of al-kalim.
حمد (ḥamd): Praise and exaltation by the tongue in response to a beautiful act of the one praised, irrespective of any benefit to the praiser.
شكر (shukr): Gratitude expressed by speech, action, or belief in response to a blessing from the benefactor.
مشارع (mashāri‘): Plural of mashra‘ah, meaning channels where water flows and drinkers come; used metaphorically for the sources of the sharī‘ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the commentator argue about the phrase 'in kāna jam‘an'?
A) It shows the author was uncertain about 'al-kalim' being a plural.
B) It is a conditional statement with an omitted apodosis, not expressing doubt.
C) It indicates that 'al-kalim' is definitely not a plural.
D) It is a rhetorical question.

Key Takeaway
The grammatical form of a word (singular vs plural) does not obviate its capacity for general legal meaning; apparent doubts are often resolved by grammatical analysis.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

How an Indefinite Plural Becomes General: The Case of 'Min Mahamid'
Explaining why the indefinite plural 'min maḥāmida' can clarify the general 'al-kalim'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that an indefinite noun can indicate generality when accompanied by a general description or when used for multiplication (takthīr).

Core Idea
An indefinite plural like 'maḥāmida' can clarify a general term when attached to a general description or when intended for multiplication.

The commentator tackles a problem: 'al-kalim' is defined with lām al-istighrāq (general), but it is clarified by 'min maḥāmida', an indefinite plural that normally does not indicate generality. Two answers are given: (1) the indefinite becomes general through a general accompanying description, and (2) the indefinite form is for multiplication, implying generality. This lesson explores these two rationales, central to the Hanafi usul of ‘āmm and khāṣṣ.

Guided Path
1
State the problem
How can an indefinite plural ('min maḥāmida') clarify a general noun ('al-kalim') that is defined by lām al-istighrāq?
The indefinite plural normally does not indicate generality.
2
Identify the first answer
An indefinite noun becomes general when it is described by a general description. Here, 'lā uṣūlahā min mashārī‘ al-khayr' is a general description that makes 'maḥāmida' general.
Example: 'imra’atin mā fīhā' includes every woman attributed to Kufa due to the general description.
3
Identify the second answer
The indefinite form (al-tankīr) here is for multiplication (li al-takthīr), which implies generality. The plural 'maḥāmida' is indefinite to indicate many instances of praise, thus covering all good words.
Takthīr is a recognized purpose of tankīr in Arabic.
4
Apply the principles
When analyzing a text, if an indefinite noun is accompanied by a general description or is clearly intended for multiplication, treat it as general in Hanafi usul.
This is distinct from the default rule that indefinite nouns are not general.

ر اور مرکب جمع ہے دو نظیریں پیش کیں ایک تمر کی جو اسم جنس ہے اور دوسری رکب کی جو اسم جمع ہے یہ دونوں اس امر میں مشترک ہیں کہ یہ معنی جمع ہیں اور لفظا و صیغہ جمع نہیں ہیں بلکہ مفرد ہیں اور لفظ کلم یقینا ایسے ہے وانه ليس نجمع یعنی لفظ کلم لفظا اور صیغہ جمع نہیں ہے جیسے کہ نسب اور رتب لفظی حیثیت سے نسبت اور رتبہ کی جمع ہیں کلم ایسے نہیں ہیں لہذا مصنف " کی عبارت ان کان جمعا میں ایک قسم کی مزازة یعنی تنفر اور سوزش ہے کیونکہ ان شکیہ استعمال کر کے اظہار شک کیا ہے جو کہ مناسب نہ تھا مصنف " کی کلام سے دفع حزازہ کے لئے یہ توجیہ کی جاتی ہے کہ ان کان جمعا شرط ہے اور اس کی جزا محذوف ہے جس پر اس کا قول و کل جمع الزوال سے تقدیر عبارت یوں ہے و الكلم ان کان جمعا فہو جمع يفرق بينه وبين واحده بالتا، وكل جمع لفرن خلاصہ یہ کہ مصنف کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ یہ در حقیقت جمع معنی ہے اور حقیقتاً جنس ہے لفظاً مفرد ہے جمع نہیں کیونکہ اس کے اور اس کے واحد کے درمیان فرق بالتاء ہے اور جو ایسے ہو وہ اسم جنس ہو کہ معنی جمع ہوتی ہے لہذا لفظ کلم بھی یقیناً ایسے ہے اب اس توجیہ کے لحاظ سے نہ شک ہے نہ حزازة وقيل ايض في درفع الحزازة ان كلمة إن محمولة على الشك من المخاطب المتوسم بناء على قول بعض ائمة النحو قوله من محامد حال من الكلم یعنی مصنف کا قول من محامد ترکیبی لحاظ سے الکلم الطیب سے حال ہے اور اس کی تبیین ہے چونکہ الکلم میں کچھ ابہام تھا اس لئے من محامد سے اس کی تبیین کر دی اور دلیل تبیین قول نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پیش کیا جو از قسم تسبیح و تحمید ہے۔
فحيا بها وجه الرحمن وجہ سے مراد ذات ہے یعنی فرشتہ ذات رحمن کے سامنے بطور تحیہ پیش کرتا ہے اگر اس حامد کے اعمال صالحہ بالکل نہ ہوں تو یہ حمد بارگاہ الہ میں قبول نہیں ہوتا والعمل الصالح یہ فعہ الى الى مكان القبول وانما صلح الجمع المنكر ام چونکہ الکلم اسم جنس معرف بلام الاستغراق ہے جو کہ عموم واستغراق کا افادہ کرتا ہے اور محامد جمع منکر ہے جو مصنف کے نزدیک عموم و استغراق کی مفید نہیں ہے تو یہ الکلم کی تبیین کا فائدہ کیسے دے سکتی ہے تو اس کے دو جواب دیدئیے ایک یہ کہ ان النكرة تعم یعنی جب نکرہ کے ساتھ وصف عام ملحق ہو جائے تو اس وقت عموم وصف کی وجہ سے نکرہ موصوفہ مہذا الوصف عموم کا مفید ہوتا ہے جیسے امراج کو فیہ میں لفظ امرآۃ ہر اس عورت کو شامل ہے جو منسوب الی الکوفہ ہے اور یہاں بھی لا صولها من مشاريع الخ وصف عام ہے جو ہر قسم کے کلمات طیبہ کو شامل ہے اسی وجہ سے محامد بھی عام مستغرق ہو جائے گا۔ دوسرا جواب یہ دیا ولان التنکیرا یعنی یہاں لفظ محامد کی تنگیر برائے تکثیر ہے جو مفید عموم ہو کر مناسب للتعميم ہے ۔ والمحامد جمع محمدة یعنی محامد جمع ہے محمد‎ کی جو کہ مصدر میمی ہے اور معنی الحمد ہے اور حمد مقابلہ الجمیل یعنی محمود کے کسی فعل جمیل کے مقابلہ میں ثنا ء اور تعظیم باللسان کرنا خواہ محمود سے کوئی نعمت واصلہ الی الحامد ہو یا نہ ہو چونکہ حمد مختص باللسان ہے اس لئے کلم کی تبیین اس کے ساتھ بہت مناسب للمقام ہے بخلاف شکر کے کہ وہ مختص باللسان نہیں اگرچہ اس کے اندر نعمت کا ہونا شرط ہے اس لئے شکر اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ بمقابلہ نعمت تعظیم منعم کا اظہار کیا جائے خواہ یہ قول رسانی کے ساتھ ہو یا عمل ارکانی اور اعتقاد جنانی کہ ساتھ۔ من مشارع الشرع میں لفظ مشارع جمع ہے مشرعة المار کی یعنی وہ نالیاں جن کے اندر پانی جاری رہتا ہے اور شاربین وارد ہوتے رہتے ہیں۔ الشرع والشریعہ بمعنی واحد یعنی وہ دین جو اللہ تعالیٰ نے اپنے عباد کے لئے مشروع فرمایا اور اس کو واضح اور ظاہر کر دیا۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ طریقہ معہودہ جو ثابت ہے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے جعلها اى جعل الشریعہ یعنی شریعت کو مصنف نے روضات و جنات سے تشبیہ دی جو مضمر فی النفس ہے یہ استعارہ مکیہ ہوا چونکہ مشارع یعنی پانی پینے کی نالیاں بساتین و جنات کے لوازمات سے ہیں تو شریعت کے لئے ان کا اثبات بطور استعارہ تخیلیہ کے ہے یعنی جیسے روضات وجنات میں مشارع ہوتے ہیں جن پر شار بین وارد ہوتے ہیں اسی طرح شریعت مطہرہ کے لئے بھی مشارع ہیں جن پر اللہ تعالیٰ کی رحمت و رضوان کے زلال کے پیاسے وارد ہوتے رہتے ہیں۔ زلال الماء الصافی کو کہتے ہیں۔ وبهذا الطريق ال يعنى مصنف نے اپنے قول قبول القبول نمار میں بھی اسی طرح کے استعارے پیش کئے ہیں پہلے قبول سے مراد باد صبا ہے اور دوسرے قبول سے مراد قبولیت عبادت تو قبول عبادت کو تشبیہ دی جہب الریح کے ساتھ یعنی اس سمت وجہہ کے ساتھ جس سے ہوا چلتی ہے کیونکہ قبول عبادت بھی ایک مہب ہے جہاں سے الطاف رحمن اور انوار غفران چلتے ہیں اور ظاہر ہوتے ہیں اور یہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے یہ استعارہ بالکنایہ ہو اور ریح الصبا یہ مہب الریح کے لوازمات سے ہے اس کا اثبات استعارہ تخیلیہ ہوا جیسے ریح الصبا کے ساتھ ابدان کی راحت اور اغصان کو نما حاصل ہوتا ہے اسی طرح صبار حمانی اور نور مغفرت کے ساتھ سکونِ قلب اور راحتِ دل حاصل ہوتی ہے اور ریح صبا عموما ان ایام میں چلتی ہے جب لیل و نہار آپس میں برابر ہو جاتے ہیں اور مطلع شمس یعنی مشرقی سمت سے چلتی ہے اور اس کے مقابل یعنی مغربی سمت سے جو ہوا چلتی ہے اسے دیور کہتے ہیں اہلِ عرب کا خیال ہے کہ دبوری ہوا بادل کو اٹھاتی ہے اور او سپر فضا میں لے جا کہ اس کو چلاتی ہے جب بادل اونچا ہو جاتا ہے تو ہٹ جاتی ہے پھر باد صبا اس بادل کا استقبال کرتی ہے اور مختلف ٹکڑوں کو ایک دوسرے پر لگا کہ ایک ہی ٹکڑا بنا لیتی ہے پھر بارش اترتی ہے جس کے ساتھ اشجار کا نشو نما ہوتا ہے قبول ثانی مصدر ہے لیکن ہے مصادر شازہ و
And a compound plural, he presented two examples: one of tamr which is an ism jins, and the second of rutab which is an ism jam‘. Both share that they are plural in meaning but not plural in word and form; rather they are singular. And the word kalim is certainly like that, and it is not a plural (jam‘). That is, the word kalim is not plural in word and form, like nasab and rutab which are plurals of nisbah and rutbah in terms of wording; kalim is not like that. Therefore, the author’s phrase 'in kana jam‘an' contains a kind of unease (ḥazāzah) because he used the particle 'in' indicating doubt, which was not appropriate. To remove this unease from the author’s speech, this explanation is given: that 'in kana jam‘an' is a conditional, and its apodosis is omitted, upon which his saying 'wa kullu jam‘in yufarraqu baynahu wa bayna wāḥidihi bi al-tā’' is based. The intended meaning is that it is actually a plural in meaning and actually a genus (jins), singular in word, not plural, because between it and its singular the difference is by the tā’. And whatever is like that is an ism jins whose meaning is plural. Hence the word kalim is certainly like that. Now according to this explanation, there is no doubt and no unease. And it is also said in removing the unease that the word 'in' is taken to indicate doubt on the part of the addressee who hypothesizes, based on the statement of some grammarians. His statement 'min mahāmida' is a hāl from al-kalim. That is, the author’s saying 'min mahāmida' is grammatically a hāl from al-kalim al-ṭayyib and is its clarification. Since al-kalim had some ambiguity, he clarified it with 'min mahāmida', and he presented as evidence for clarification the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which is of the type of tasbīḥ and taḥmīd. 'Fa-ḥayyā bihā wajha al-raḥmān' – by 'wajh' is meant essence (dhāt), i.e., the angel presents it as a greeting before the essence of the Merciful. If this praiser has no righteous deeds at all, then this praise is not accepted in the divine court. And 'al-‘amal al-ṣāliḥ' is... to the place of acceptance. And why does the indefinite plural suffice? Since al-kalim is an ism jins defined by lām al-istighrāq which indicates generality and inclusion, and mahāmida is an indefinite plural which, according to the author, does not indicate generality and inclusion, then how can it provide clarification for al-kalim? So two answers are given: one is that the indefinite becomes general (inna al-nakirata ta‘umm) – meaning when an indefinite is joined by a general description, then due to the generality of the description, the described indefinite becomes general in that description. For example, in 'imra’atin mā fīhā', the word 'imra’atin' includes every woman who is attributed to Kufa. And here too, 'lā uṣūlahā min mashārī‘i al-khayr' is a general description that includes all kinds of good words. For this reason, mahāmida also becomes fully general. The second answer is that the indefinite form (al-tankīr) here is for multiplication (li al-takthīr), which is general and suitable for generalizing. And al-mahāmida is the plural of maḥmada, which is a mīmī maṣdar and means al-ḥamd. And ḥamd is in contrast to al-jamīl, i.e., praise and exaltation by the tongue in response to a beautiful act of the praised one, whether or not a blessing has reached the praiser from the praised one. Since ḥamd is specific to the tongue, its clarification of kalim is very suitable for the context, unlike shukr which is not specific to the tongue, although it requires the presence of a blessing. Hence shukr is defined as expressing exaltation of the benefactor in response to a blessing, whether by speech, physical action, or inner belief. 'Min mashārī‘i al-shar‘i' - the word mashārī‘ is the plural of mashra‘ah al-mār, i.e., the channels in which water flows and drinkers constantly come. Al-shar‘ and al-sharī‘ah are synonymous, i.e., the religion that Allah has legislated for His servants and made clear and apparent. In summary, the established method that is proven from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). 'Ja‘alahā' i.e., ja‘ala al-sharī‘ah – the author likened the sharī‘ah to gardens and orchards, which is implicit in the self; this is a makkiyyah metaphor. Since mashārī‘ (water channels) are among the appurtenances of gardens, their establishment for the sharī‘ah is a figurative metaphor: just as gardens have channels upon which drinkers come, similarly the pure sharī‘ah has channels upon which those thirsty for the pure water of Allah’s mercy and pleasure come. 'Zulāl' is called clear water. 'Wa bi hādhā al-ṭarīq' – the author also presented similar metaphors in his saying 'qabūl al-qabūl namār'. The first 'qabūl' means the east wind, and the second 'qabūl' means acceptance of worship. So he likened the acceptance of worship to the direction of the wind, i.e., the direction from which the wind blows, because acceptance of worship is also a direction from which the favors of the Merciful and lights of forgiveness come and appear. This simile is implicit in the self, it is a metaphor by allusion, and 'rīḥ al-ṣabā' is among the appurtenances of the wind’s direction; its establishment is a figurative metaphor. Just as with the east wind there is comfort for bodies and growth for branches, similarly with the south wind and light of forgiveness there is tranquility of heart and comfort of the self. And the east wind generally blows when night and day become equal, and it blows from the sunrise direction. The wind that blows from the opposite, westerly direction is called 'dabūr'. The Arabs believe that the dabūr wind lifts clouds and drives them across the sky; when the cloud rises high, it withdraws. Then the east wind meets the cloud and brings different pieces together making one piece, then rain falls with which trees grow. 'Qabūl thānī' is a maṣdar but it is among irregular maṣādir.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharḥ) on a text from Al-Tawḍīḥ, focusing on the definition and grammatical nature of the word 'al-kalim' (الكلم). The commentator begins by comparing 'al-kalim' to two other words: 'tamr' (dates) and 'rutab' (ripe dates). Both 'tamr' and 'rutab' are singular in form but indicate a plural meaning; they are ism jins (nouns of genus) or ism jam‘ (collective nouns). Similarly, 'al-kalim' is singular in form but denotes a plurality of words. The author of the original text used the phrase 'in kāna jam‘an' (if it is a plural), which some might perceive as expressing doubt due to the particle 'in'. The commentator resolves this by explaining that 'in' here is a conditional particle, and its apodosis is omitted; the intended meaning is that if 'al-kalim' is considered a plural, it is a plural that differs from its singular by the addition of 'tā'' (like 'kalimah' and 'kalim'). This removes any sense of unease (ḥazāzah). The passage then discusses the phrase 'min maḥāmida' (from praises) as a descriptive phrase clarifying 'al-kalim al-ṭayyib'. The commentator notes that 'al-kalim' is defined by 'alif lām al-istighrāq' (the definite article for generality), indicating all words, while 'maḥāmida' is an indefinite plural which normally does not indicate generality. To justify its clarifying role, two answers are given: (1) an indefinite noun becomes general when it is described by a general description, and here 'lā uṣūlahā min mashārī‘ al-khayr' serves as a general description; (2) the indefinite form here is for multiplication (takthīr), which implies generality. The commentator then distinguishes between 'ḥamd' (praise) and 'shukr' (thankfulness). 'Ḥamd' is praise by the tongue for a voluntary beautiful act, regardless of any benefit to the praiser, and is specific to speech. 'Shukr' is gratitude for a blessing, expressed by speech, action, or belief, and requires the presence of a blessing. The passage ends with metaphorical interpretations of 'mashārī‘ al-shar‘' (channels of the law) and 'qabūl' (acceptance), likening the sharī‘ah to gardens with flowing water and the acceptance of worship to a wind bringing comfort. The commentary follows the author's order, clarifying each point with linguistic and legal reasoning typical of Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الكلم (al-kalim): A singular noun indicating a plural meaning, similar to ism jins or ism jam‘; defined by lām al-istighrāq to denote generality of words.
محامد (maḥāmida): Indefinite plural of maḥmada (a mīmī maṣdar meaning praise); used as a descriptive phrase to clarify the generality of al-kalim.
حمد (ḥamd): Praise and exaltation by the tongue in response to a beautiful act of the one praised, irrespective of any benefit to the praiser.
شكر (shukr): Gratitude expressed by speech, action, or belief in response to a blessing from the benefactor.
مشارع (mashāri‘): Plural of mashra‘ah, meaning channels where water flows and drinkers come; used metaphorically for the sources of the sharī‘ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two reasons given in the text for why the indefinite plural 'min maḥāmida' can clarify the general word 'al-kalim'?
A) Because the indefinite plural is always general, and because it is a mīmī maṣdar.
B) Because it is attached to a general description, and because the indefinite form indicates multiplication (takthīr).
C) Because 'al-kalim' is also indefinite, and because the Prophet (saw) used it.
D) Because it is a proper noun, and because it is preceded by 'min'.

Key Takeaway
An indefinite noun can acquire generality through a general description or through the intention of multiplication (takthīr); both are valid usul tools in the Hanafi school.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Conditions of a Valid Definition: Tard and 'Aks
Explains tard and 'aks as conditions for definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of tard and 'aks to evaluate the validity of a definition in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A valid definition must both exclude everything else (tard) and include all its instances ('aks).

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a definition is not merely a description; it must be precise. Two logical conditions ensure precision: tard (exclusivity) and 'aks (inclusivity). This lesson unpacks these conditions with classical examples, showing how a definition can fail if either condition is violated. Understanding these conditions is foundational for defining legal terms accurately.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish tard and 'aks
Identify which condition ensures exclusivity (tard) and which ensures inclusivity ('aks). Tard means the definition applies only to the defined term; 'aks means the definition covers all instances of the defined term.
2
Test a definition for tard
Check if the definition applies to any instance that is not the defined term. If it does, tard is violated (definition is too broad).
Example: defining human as 'walking animal' fails tard because it includes horses and donkeys.
3
Test a definition for 'aks
Check if all instances of the defined term are covered by the definition. If any instance is excluded, 'aks is violated (definition is too narrow).
Example: defining human as 'actually writing animal' fails 'aks because it excludes sleeping humans.
4
Analyze the definition of 'asl' from al-Muhsul
Apply both conditions to the definition of 'asl' (root) given in al-Muhsul. The passage argues it fails tard because it would include efficient, formal, and final causes, which are not called 'asl'.
This shows that even famous definitions may be invalid.
5
Summarize the role of both conditions
A valid definition must satisfy tard and 'aks simultaneously. Missing either renders the definition invalid for legal reasoning.

ہیں جیسے لفظ اصل اور فقہ اور جنس و نوع وغیرہ تو ان کی تعریف اسمی ہوتی ہے جو پیار کرتی ہے کہ یہ اسم کسی شئی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے (و شرط لكلا التعريفين الطرد) یعنی تعریف حقیقی اور تعریف اسمی دونوں کے لئے طرد شرطہ ہے طرد کا معنی بیان کرتے ہوئے مصنف نے کہا ای کل ماصدق عليه الحد صدق عليه المحدود یعنی جہاں جہاں حد صادق آئے وہاں محدود کا صادق آنا ضروری ہے اگر حد کسی مقام یہ صادق آچکی ہے اور محدود صادق نہیں آتا تو یہ حد غیر محدود پر صادق آگئی تو مانع از دخول غیر نہ ہوئی لہذا یہ تعریف مطرد نہ ہوئی والعکس یعنی تعریفات کے لئے عکس بھی شرط ہے یعنی جامع ہوتا کیونکہ عکس کا معنیٰ ہے کل ما صدق عليه المحدود صدق عليه الحد یعنی جہاں محدود صادق آئے وہاں حد ضرور صادق آئے اگر محدود صادق آچکا ہے اور حد صادق نہیں آئی تو یہ صد جامع نہ رہی تو اس کا عکس باطل ہو گیا ۔ فاذا قيل في تعريف الانسان انه حیوان ماشي لا يطرد ای لا یمنع عن دخول الغير لانه صادق على الفرس و الحمار وغير بما من الحيوانات ولوقيل حيوان كاتب بالفعل لا ينعكس یعنی اگر انسان کی تعریف حیوان کا تب بالفعل سے کی جائے تو یہ جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ جو انسان کا تب بالفعل نہیں ہیں بلکہ صرف کا تب بالقوة ہیں ان پر یہ تعریف صادق نہیں آتی ولاشك ان تعريف الاصل اسمی یعنی الاصل کی تعریف اسمی ہے میں سے مقصود یہ بیان کرنا ہے کہ لفظ اصل کسی شئی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے فالتعريف الذي ذكر في المحصول لا يطرد اى ليس بمانع عن دخول الغير لانه الى الأصل لا يطلق على الفاعل یعنی لفظ الاصل علة فاعلیہ اور علت صوریہ اور علت غائیہ پر اطلاق نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح شروط یعنی ادوات اور آلات صناعت یہ لفظ الاصل اطلاق نہیں ہوتا لیکن ان تمام اشیاء پر تعریف مذکورہ صادق آتی ہے کیونکہ یہ تمام اشیاء محتاج الیھا ہیں تو حد صادق آگئی محدود صادق نہ آیا تو غیر محدود پر صادق آئی مانع از دخول غیر نه رہی لہذا یہ تعریف اسمی صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ ھذا ما قال المصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ ۔
Such as the word 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins', and 'naw', etc. Their definition is nominal, which [explains] that this noun is coined for something. (And a condition for both definitions is tard). That is, for both real and nominal definitions, tard is a condition. The author explained the meaning of tard: 'Every instance to which the definition applies, the defined term applies.' Meaning, wherever the definition is true, the defined must be true. If the definition is true in a place but the defined is not true, then the definition applies to what is not the defined, so it does not prevent the entry of what is other. Hence this definition is not muttard (universally applicable). And 'aks (inverse) is also a condition for definitions, meaning it must be comprehensive because the meaning of 'aks is: 'Every instance to which the defined applies, the definition applies.' If the defined applies but the definition does not, then this definition is not comprehensive, so its 'aks is invalid. For example, if it is said in the definition of human that it is a walking animal, it does not prevent the entry of others because it is true of horses, donkeys, and other animals. If it is said 'a writing animal in actuality', it does not have 'aks, meaning if a human is defined as 'an animal that writes in actuality', this is not comprehensive because those humans who are not actually writing but only potentially writing are not covered by this definition. There is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is nominal, i.e., the definition of 'asl' is nominal. The intent is to state that the word 'asl' is coined for something. So the definition mentioned in al-Muhsul does not have tard, i.e., it is not a preventer of entry of what is other, because the word 'asl' is not applied to the efficient cause, nor to the formal cause, nor to the final cause. Similarly, it is not applied to conditions, i.e., instruments and tools of a craft. But all these things are covered by the mentioned definition because they are depended upon. So the definition applies, but the defined does not, so it applies to what is not the defined, and it does not prevent the entry of what is other. Therefore, this nominal definition is not correct. This is what the author said, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage discusses the two essential conditions for any valid definition in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: tard (exclusivity) and 'aks (inclusivity). Tard ensures that the definition only applies to the defined term and excludes everything else. 'Aks ensures that the definition covers all instances of the defined term. The author illustrates with examples: defining 'human' as 'walking animal' lacks tard because it includes non-humans; defining it as 'actually writing animal' lacks 'aks because it excludes non-writing humans. The passage then tests the definition of 'asl' (root) from al-Muhsul, finding it fails tard because it would incorrectly include efficient, formal, and final causes. This demonstrates that definitions must be both exclusive and comprehensive. The discussion is part of the broader Hanafi usul methodology for defining terms precisely.

Key Terms
الطرد (al-tard): A condition of definition meaning that the definition applies to every instance of the defined term and excludes all others.
العکس (al-'aks): A condition of definition meaning that every instance of the defined term is covered by the definition.
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A nominal definition that explains the meaning of a word as coined, not its real essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the condition of tard require in a definition?
A) The definition must include all instances of the defined term.
B) The definition must exclude everything that is not the defined term.
C) The definition must be based on a real quiddity.
D) The definition must use the same word as the defined.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition in Hanafi usul must simultaneously satisfy tard (exclusivity) and 'aks (inclusivity).

Real vs Nominal Definitions: Ta'rif Haqiqi and Ta'rif Ismi
Distinguishes real and nominal definitions based on quiddity types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) and a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) by analyzing whether the quiddity of the defined term has real existence or is merely conceptual, and you will be able to state the rules for definitions of non-existents and existents.

Core Idea
A real definition explains an essence; a nominal definition clarifies a term's meaning — the key is whether the quiddity has real existence.

This passage from al-Talwih unpacks one of the most foundational distinctions in Hanafi usul: the difference between defining a real quiddity (mahiyya haqiqiyya) and defining a conceptual quiddity (mahiyya i'tibariyya). Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines whether a definition can capture the essence of something or is merely clarifying a term's coinage. The commentator guides us through the two types of definitions and their conditions, with examples like 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins', and 'naw''.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of quiddities
According to the passage, quiddities are either real (mahiyya haqiqiyya) or conceptual (mahiyya i'tibariyya). Real quiddities exist independently of mental consideration; conceptual quiddities are coined by the mind.
Examples of conceptual quiddities: 'asl' (root), 'fiqh' (jurisprudence).
2
Determine when a definition is real
A definition is real when the quiddity has real existence and the definition aims to explain that essence, using essentialia, accidents, or both.
Real definitions include complete definitions (hadd tamm), incomplete definitions (hadd naqis), and descriptive definitions (rasm).
3
Determine when a definition is nominal
A definition is nominal when the aim is to clarify the meaning of the term as coined, regardless of whether the quiddity is real or conceptual.
Nominal definitions use a more famous word (e.g., 'ghadanfar' for 'asad') or a descriptive phrase (e.g., 'al-asl ma yabni 'alayhi ghayruhu').
4
Apply the rules to non-existents and existents
Non-existents have no real quiddity, so only nominal definitions apply. Existents have both real and conceptual aspects, so both types are possible depending on the aim.
The passage emphasizes that even existents can have nominal definitions when clarifying the term's conventional meaning.
5
Note the apparent objection
The passage ends with an objection that the commentator's position may contradict the author's division. This highlights the need for careful reading of the matn and shows that later Hanafi usul refines the distinction.
The objection is incomplete due to page cut-off, but it underscores the dynamic nature of usul discourse.

The commentator, may Allah have mercy on him, said in al-Talwih: 'His statement: Know that definition is either real or nominal. The quiddity either has a real existence or a conceptual existence. Quiddity is of two types: real quiddity and conceptual quiddity. Either, despite disregarding mental consideration, it has subsistence in itself or not. The first is real quiddity, i.e., established in the actual state. If this quiddity is composite, its parts are in need of each other. The second is conceptual quiddity, i.e., its existence is due to mental consideration. For example, the coiner considered several matters and coined a term for them, and those matters do not have mutual dependence. Like the word 'asl', coined for a thing that has the attribute of being that on which something else is based. Similarly, 'fiqh' is coined for specific issues; likewise 'jins', coined for a universal that is predicated in answer to 'what is it?' over multiple differing realities; and 'naw'', coined for a universal that is predicated over multiple agreeing realities. Among conceptual quiddities, examples of composites have been given, but one should not imagine that conceptual quiddities are only composites; rather, conceptual quiddities can also be simples. Moreover, the truth is that these simples are called conceptual matters, not conceptual quiddities. With this established, the thing that the coiner conceives and imagines in order to coin a term for it: either in terms of the actual state it is a real quiddity or not. In the first case, where it has a real quiddity, the coiner's conception is either the essence of the thing or its accidents, or a composition of both. In that case, defining the real quiddity of the named thing, insofar as it is a real quiddity, is a real definition. It will convey a depiction of the quiddity, i.e., it will inform of the quiddity being imagined and impressed in the mind, either by all essentialia as in the complete definition, or by some essentialia as in the incomplete definition, or by accidents, or by a combination of accidents and essentialia as in the descriptive definitions (rusum). And defining the concept of the name, i.e., if the purpose of definition is only to clarify the meaning of the name and the conception of the coiner for which the name was coined, then this is a nominal definition. Its benefit is clarification—i.e., to explain what the name was coined for using a more famous word, such as 'al-ghadanfar' for 'al-asad' (lion), or with a word that contains a detail of the meaning of the name, like 'al-asl ma yabni 'alayhi ghayruhu' (the root is that on which something else is built). So definitions of non-existents: since they have no established realities, only concepts, their definition is only nominal, because if there is no established reality, how can there be a real definition? And definitions of existents: they can be both—nominal and real—because they have concepts and realities. If only the concept is to be clarified, the definition is nominal; if the reality is to be explained, the definition is real. If you object: what the commentator said, that definitions of existents can sometimes be nominal and sometimes real, is the point of contention. Summary of the objection: the author's apparent wording contradicts this, because when dividing definitions, he said: 'either real, like the definition of real quiddities, or nominal, like the definition of conceptual quiddities.' Since conceptual quiddities... [text ends]
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Talwih on the distinction between real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) definitions. It begins by explaining two types of quiddities: real quiddities that exist independently of mental consideration, and conceptual quiddities that exist only due to mental consideration. Examples of conceptual quiddities include terms like 'asl' (root), 'fiqh' (jurisprudence), 'jins' (genus), and 'naw'' (species), each coined for a set of attributes without real mutual dependence. The commentator clarifies that conceptual quiddities can be simple or composite. The key principle: if the quiddity is real, its definition can be real, conveying the essence (complete or incomplete definition) or using accidents (descriptive definition). If the quiddity is merely conceptual, the definition is nominal, aiming to clarify the meaning of the term. For non-existents (ma'dumat), only nominal definitions are possible. For existents, both are possible depending on the aim. The passage ends with an objection regarding the apparent contradiction with the author's earlier division, suggesting that the commentator's position may conflict with the matn. This reflects the Hanafi usul tradition's precise analysis of definition types.

Key Terms
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that explains the real essence of a thing, using its essential or accidental properties, applicable when the quiddity has real existence.
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A definition that clarifies the meaning of a term as coined, without delving into the real essence.
ماہیت حقیقیہ (mahiyya haqiqiyya): A quiddity that has real existence in the actual state, independent of mental consideration.
ماہیت اعتباریہ (mahiyya i'tibariyya): A quiddity that exists only by mental consideration, coined for a set of attributes without real mutual dependence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a definition considered 'real' (haqiqi)?
A) When it defines a non-existent thing.
B) When it clarifies the meaning of a term as coined.
C) When the quiddity of the defined thing has real existence and the definition explains that essence.
D) When it uses only essential properties without accidents.

Key Takeaway
A real definition explains the essence of a quiddity with real existence; a nominal definition clarifies the meaning of a coined term, and applies to conceptual quiddities and optionally to existents.

Conditions of Definition: Tard and Aks
Explains the conditions of tard and aks for a valid definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions of tard and aks and distinguish between nominal and real definitions.

Core Idea
A valid definition must apply to all instances (tard) and only those instances (aks).

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a definition (ta'rif) is not merely a linguistic exercise; it must satisfy logical conditions to be legally operative. This lesson explains the distinction between nominal and real definitions and the key conditions of tard (comprehensiveness) and aks (exclusivity). Understanding these conditions is foundational for defining legal terms precisely.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between nominal and real definition
The commentator explains that a nominal definition answers 'what is it?' before existence is known, while a real definition describes essence after verification. Recognize that the same definition can be both if it corresponds to reality.
2
Understand tard
Tard means the definition must apply to every instance of the defined (al-mahdud). It ensures comprehensiveness: wherever the definition is found, the defined is found.
Tard corresponds to the condition of being comprehensive (jami').
3
Understand aks
Aks is taken in two senses: customary inversion (convert subject and predicate, keeping quantity) or the condition that the definition applies only to the defined (exclusivity). The passage adopts the latter: if the definition is negated, the defined is negated.
Aks corresponds to the condition of being exclusive (mani').
4
Relate tard and aks to mani' and jami'
Together, tard and aks make the definition both preventive (mani') of non-defined entries and comprehensive (jami') of all defined instances.
5
Apply to an example
The triangle example shows how a nominal definition (shape bounded by three lines) becomes real after geometric proof of existence. Check if this definition satisfies tard (all triangles) and aks (only triangles).
This illustrates the practical application of the conditions.

Source Text
