کبھی ماہیت حقیقیہ بایں حیثیت اخذ کی جاتی ہے کہ یہ مفہوم اسم ہے اور اسم کی وضع کرتے وقت یہی متعقل واضح ہے تو اس اعتبار سے اس کی تعریف یقیناً اسمی ہے یہ اسی ما کا جواب بنتی جو مفہوم اسم اور متعقل واضع کی طلب کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے یعنی ما اسمیہ شارح وهذا التعريف قد يكون الا يعني بيبي تعریف اسمی کبھی حقیقت شی کا عین ہوتی ہے یہ اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب کہ متعقل واضع عین حقیقت ہو وقد يكون غيرها یعنی کبھی تعریف بعد الدلالة على وجوده یعنی جب علم الہندسہ اس مثلث کے وجود پر دلیل پیش کر دیتا ہے تو یہی تعریف اسمی اس وقت حقیقی ہو جاتی ہے۔ قوله شرط لكلا التعريفين اى الحقيقى والاسمى الطرد والعكس المنع والجمع اما الطرد فهو یعنی طرد صدق محدود علی ما صدق علیہ الحد صدقاً کلیاً کا نام ہے یعنی ہر وہ مقام جہاں جہاں صد صادق آئے گی وہاں محدود کا صادق آنا ضروری ہے یہی مراد ہے اس قول معروف کی کلما وجد الحد وجد المحدود قبالا طراد یعنی مرد کے ساتھ حد میں منعیت آجاتی ہے حد مانع عن دخول الغیر ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ جہاں جاتا حد پہنچی تو وہاں محدود کا پہنچنا ضروری ہوا تو اس صورت میں حد غیر محدود پر صادق نہ آئی اگر طرد منتقض ہو جائے مثلاً کسی ایک مقام پر صد صادق آچکی ہے لیکن محدود وہاں موجود نہیں ہے تو لا محالہ یہ صدغیر می رود پر صادق ہوگی تو مانع عن دخول الغير نہ رہی واما العكس فاخذه از عکس سے مراد کس طرد با عتبار متفاہم عرف کے لیا گیا ہے اور وہ یہ کہ محمول کو موضوع اور موضوع کو محمول بنا لیا جائے اور کمیت سابقہ بعینها بر قرار رکھی جائے یہ عرفی عکس کلیہ کا کلیہ آئے گا جیسے کہا جاتا ہے کل انسان ضاحک و بالعکس ای کل ضاحک انسان اور کہتے ہیں کل انسان حیوان و لا عکس ای لیس کل حیوان انسانا تو یہ ہے عکس عرفی ورنہ تو عکس مجھے موجبہ کلیہ کا موجبہ جزئیہ آتا ہے وہ تو کل انسان حیوان کا صحیح آتا ہے اس لئے مصنف نے بھی اسی بنیاد پر کس کا ترجمہ کل ماصدق علیہ المحدود صدق علیہ اخذ کیا حاصل یہ کہ طرد کے اندر محدود کا حکم کلی علی الحمد کیا جاتا ہے اور عکس کے اندر حد کا حکم کلی علی المحدود ہوتا ہے وبعضهم اخذہ یعنی بعض حضرات نے عکس کو اس مشہور معنی یعنی عکس الاثبات النفی کے لحاظ سے لیا ہے تو اس لحاظ سے مکس کا مفہوم ہوگا کلما انتفى الحد انتقى المحدود یعنی جہاں حد صادق نہ آوے وہاں محدود بھی صادق نہ آوے کیونکہ اگر محدود صادق آگیا اور حد یہاں صادق نہ آئی تو جمعیت ختم ہو جائے گی یعنی صد جامع لجمیع الافراد نہ رہی بہر حال طرد اور عکس کے ساتھ تعریف مانع و جامع ہو جاتی ہے۔
Sometimes the real essence is taken in this regard that it is the concept of the name, and when coining the name, this is the clear object of coinage, so accordingly its definition is certainly a nominal definition. It answers the question 'what is it?' which is posed for the concept of the name and the object of the coinage, i.e., the nominal 'what'. This definition may sometimes be the very reality of the thing, when the object of coinage is the very reality, and sometimes it may be other than it, i.e., sometimes the nominal definition is other than reality. For this reason the scholars of the art have stated that sometimes the real and nominal definitions become united. However, there is definitely this difference: before knowledge of the existence of the thing and its affirmation, it is called nominal, and that same definition becomes real after knowledge of the existence of the thing, like the definition of triangle: 'a shape that is bounded by three sides, i.e., three lines' – in the discussions [؟] of geometry it is called a nominal definition; then after indicating its existence – i.e., when the science of geometry provides evidence for the existence of this triangle – this same nominal definition becomes real at that time. He said: The condition for both definitions, i.e., real and nominal, is tard, aks, mani', and jam'. As for tard, it means the extension of the defined term to everything to which the definition applies universally – i.e., wherever the definition applies, the defined term must necessarily apply. This is the meaning of the well-known saying: 'Whenever the definition is found, the defined is found.' Accordingly, with tard, the definition becomes mani' (preventative), i.e., it prevents entry of what is other, because when the definition reaches a place, the defined necessarily reaches there, so in that situation the definition does not apply to what is other than the defined. If tard is violated, e.g., the definition applies in a certain place but the defined is not present there, then inevitably the definition would apply to something other than the defined, so it would not be prevenient of entry of what is other. As for aks (inversion), it is taken from inversion in the sense of customary inversion, which is to make the predicate the subject and the subject the predicate while keeping the quantity exactly the same. This customary inversion will turn a universal affirmative into a universal affirmative, as is said: 'Every human is laughing', and conversely 'Every laughing being is human'. And they say 'Every human is an animal' and there is no inversion, i.e., 'Not every animal is human'. This is customary inversion; otherwise logical inversion turns a universal affirmative into a particular affirmative, and that is valid for 'Every human is an animal'. For this reason the author, on this basis, interpreted aks as: 'Everything to which the defined applies, the definition applies' – i.e., within tard, the ruling of the defined is universal over the definition, and within aks, the ruling of the definition is universal over the defined. And some have taken it – i.e., some scholars have taken aks in its famous meaning, i.e., the inversion of affirmation to negation. According to this, the meaning of aks is: 'Whenever the definition is negated, the defined is negated', i.e., where the definition does not apply, the defined does not apply, because if the defined applies but the definition does not apply there, then comprehensiveness is lost – i.e., the definition is not comprehensive for all individuals. In any case, with tard and aks, the definition becomes mani' and jam'.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the conditions for a valid definition. The commentator begins by distinguishing between real and nominal definitions. A nominal definition identifies the object for which a term is coined; it answers the question 'ma huwa' (what is it) in a linguistic sense. This definition may coincide with the real essence or may be different. The same definition is nominal before verification of existence and real after verification. The commentator then turns to the core: the conditions of tard and aks. Tard means the definition must apply to every instance of the defined term; it ensures universality. Aks means the definition must apply only to the defined term; it ensures exclusivity. These conditions together make the definition both comprehensive (jami') and excluding (mani'). The passage clarifies that tard is about the definition's extension over the defined, while aks is about the defined's extension over the definition in a customary inversion. Some scholars interpret aks as the reverse implication: if the definition is absent, the defined is absent. The commentary follows the Hanafi usul tradition in emphasizing the importance of these logical conditions for sound definitions.

Key Terms
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A definition that identifies the meaning of a term for which it was coined, regardless of the existence of the thing.
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that describes the real essence of the thing after its existence is known.
طرد (tard): The condition that the definition applies to every individual of the defined term.
عکس (aks): The condition that the definition applies exclusively to the defined term; also interpreted as the reverse implication.
مانع (mani'): That which prevents the entry of what is not the defined.
جامع (jami'): That which includes all individuals of the defined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the condition of 'aks' require in a definition?
A) The definition must apply to every instance of the defined.
B) The definition must apply only to the defined.
C) The definition must be based on a textual proof.
D) The definition must be nominal.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must satisfy both tard (comprehensiveness) and aks (exclusivity) to be both jami' and mani'.

Tard as a Condition in Nominal Definitions
Argument that tard is not a necessary condition for nominal definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal and nominal definitions and evaluate the necessity of tard in each.

Core Idea
Tard is not required for verbal definitions; it is only required for complete nominal definitions.

This passage engages a classical debate in usul al-fiqh: must every definition be comprehensive (tard) and exclusive (mani')? The author argues that tard is not an absolute condition, distinguishing nominal definitions of technical terms from simple verbal explanations in lexicons. The context is the definition of 'asl' as 'ma yahtaju ilayhi' (that which is needed), which is an incomplete definition but sufficient to distinguish 'asl' from its opposite 'far''.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of definitions
The passage distinguishes between verbal (lafzi) and nominal (ismi) definitions. Verbal definitions explain a word using a more famous synonym; nominal definitions list essential characteristics.
Verbal definitions are common in lexicons; nominal definitions are used in technical disciplines like usul al-fiqh.
2
Understand the commentator's objection
The commentator (Sharh) argues that lack of tard (comprehensiveness) corrupts any definition, whether nominal or non-nominal.
His position is based on the logical principle that a definition must be convertible with the defined term.
3
Follow the author's rebuttal using the distinction
The author counters that the definitions found in lexicons are verbal, not nominal, and no one objects to them for lacking tard. Therefore, tard is not necessary for all definitions.
The author also notes that the definition of 'asl' is an incomplete definition by al-amm (the more general), which is allowed to distinguish from a specific opposite.
4
Apply to the definition of 'asl'
The definition 'ma yahtaju ilayhi' is a definition by al-amm (it applies to more than just 'asl'). The author defends it as valid for the purpose of distinguishing 'asl' from 'far''.
This shows that not all definitions need to be fully comprehensive; context matters.

وههنا بحث من وجوه - الاول اس مبحث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تعریف مطلق میں طرد کوئی ضروری شرط نہیں ہے لہذا طرد کا نہ ہونا جیسے کہ محصول کی تعریف ہے تو یہ امر مفسد للتعریف نہیں ہے بلکہ بدون الطرد بھی تعریف صحیح ہے علی الخصوص تعریف اسمی میں تو طرد شرط نہیں ہے دیکھئے کہ کتب لغت میں تفسیر الفاظ ایسے الفاظ و معانی کے ساتھ بالکثرة موجود ہے جو عام من المفسر ہوتے ہیں جو مفسر کے علاوہ اغیار پر صادق آجاتے ہیں تو ان تفسیرات کے اوپر کوئی شخص بھی نقض بعدم الاطراد نہیں کرتا تو معلوم ہوا کہ طرد صحت تعریف کے لئے کوئی شرط ضروری نہیں ہے۔ آپ کو یاد ہوگا کہ شارح نے اس قول کی شروع میں فرمایا ہے کہ هذا لا دخل له في بيان فساد التعریف از عدم الاطراد مقد له اسمیا کان اوغیرہ تو اس قول کے اندر شارح علام اطراد کو ہر تعریف کے لئے خواہ اسمی ہو یا غیر اسمی مفسد قرار دے رہا ہے لیکن مصنف کے اوپر بلاوجہ اعتران کہ نا شارح کی عادت ثانویہ ہو چکی ہے اس لئے ناجائز اعتراضات ہمیشہ کرتا رہے گا اور یہ اسی کا ایک نمونہ ہے حالانکہ طرد تعریف کے لئے شرط ہے شارح کا انکار کر نا صرف تحکم ہے پھر استدلال شارح کو دیکھئے جو فان کتب اللغة الخ کے ساتھ پیش کیا ہے یہ بھی قابل تعجب ہے کیونکہ یہ تمام تعریفات جو کتب لغت میں موجود ہیں یہ تمام تعریفات لفظیہ ہیں تعریفات اسمیہ نہیں ہیں ان دونوں میں بڑا فرق ہے امور بدیہیہ کی تعریف لفظی ہوا کرتی ہے لیکن تعریف اسمی نہیں ہوتی یہاں تو لفظ اصل ایک اصطلاحی امر ہے اور کتب اصول جو اس کی تعریف کرتی ہیں وہ تعریف اسمی ہے جس کے لئے طرد شرط ہے اور یہ تعریف لفظی جو بلفظ اشہر مرادف ہوتی ہے یہ وہ نہیں ہے لہذا شارح کا استدلال مثبت دعویٰ نہیں ہے۔ قال فی الزاھدیۃ علی الامور العامة وذهب المحقق التفتازاني ومن وافقه الى انه الى التعريف اللفظى من المطالب التصورية زاحمین عدم الفرق بينه وبين التعريف الاسمى ومن البين ان البديي يحتمل التعريف اللفظي ولا يحتمل التعريف الاسمى - التعريفات المذكورة في كتب اللغة لفظية من المطالب التصديقية - فقد صرح المحققون المحاصل اس بحث کا یہ ہے کہ محققین نے تعریفات ناقصہ کے اندر تعریف بالاعم کو جائز قرار دیا ہے جو صرف بعض ما حد المحدود سے امتیاز کا فائدہ دے گی جو مانع از دخول غیر نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ بسا اوقات غرض من التفسیر ایک معین شی سے تمییز مقصود ہوتی ہے جیسے یہاں ہم اصل کو ممتاز عن الفرع کرنا چاہتے ہیں تو اصل کی تعریف المحتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کریں گے اور فرع کی المحتاج کے ساتھ کریں گے۔ شارح کی اس بحث کا کوئی اثر مصنف پر نہیں پڑتا کیونکہ اس بحث کے اندر تسلیم کیا جارہا ہے کہ اصل کی تعریف جو محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے یہ تعریف بالاعم ہے جو ناقص ہے جو مانع از دخول
And here is a discussion from several aspects: First, the result of this investigation is that in an absolute definition, tard is not a necessary condition. Therefore, the lack of tard, as in the definition of al-Mahsul, is not a corruption of the definition; rather, without tard the definition is also valid. Specifically, in a nominal definition, tard is not a condition. See that in lexicons, explanations of words are frequently found with words and meanings that are general (common) that apply to other things besides the explained term. Yet no one objects to these explanations for lacking tard. Hence it is known that tard is not a necessary condition for the validity of a definition. You will recall that the commentator said at the beginning of this statement: 'This has no relevance in explaining the corruption of the definition from the lack of tard, whether it is nominal or non-nominal.' So in that statement, the commentator considers the lack of tard as corrupting for every definition, whether nominal or non-nominal. But he objects to the author without reason. The commentator's habit has become secondary, so he always makes unjust objections, and this is one example of it. However, tard is a condition for definition; the commentator's denial is mere obstinacy. Then look at the commentator's argument presented with 'for the books of language, etc.' This is also surprising, because all these definitions found in books of language are verbal definitions, not nominal definitions. There is a big difference between the two. Self-evident matters are defined verbally, but not by nominal definition. Here, the word 'asl' is a terminological matter, and the books of usul that define it give a nominal definition, for which tard is a condition. This verbal definition which is synonymous with a more famous word is not that. Therefore, the commentator's argument does not prove his claim. It is said in al-Zahidiyyah 'ala al-Umur al-'Ammah: 'And al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani and those who agree with him held that it refers to the verbal definition from among the conceptual demands, claiming that there is no difference between it and the nominal definition, while it is clear that the self-evident admits verbal definition but does not admit nominal definition. The definitions mentioned in books of language are verbal from among the assertoric demands.' The investigators have clearly stated: The result of this discussion is that the investigators have allowed definition by the more general (al-amm) in incomplete definitions, which gives only the benefit of distinguishing from some limit of the defined, but it will not prevent entry of other things, because sometimes the purpose of explanation is to distinguish from a specific thing. For example, here we want to distinguish 'asl' from 'far'' (branch), so we define 'asl' with 'ma yahtaju ilayhi' (that which is needed) and 'far'' with 'ma yahtaju' (that which needs). The commentator's discussion has no effect on the author, because in this discussion it is acknowledged that the definition of 'asl' given with 'ma yahtaju ilayhi' is a definition by the more general (al-amm), which is incomplete and does not prevent entry [of others].
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul dispute) about whether tard (comprehensiveness) is a necessary condition for all definitions, particularly nominal definitions. The author of the supercommentary (likely the text we are reading) defends the view that tard is not required for nominal definitions, citing examples from lexicons where definitions are given that are not comprehensive. The commentator (sharh) had argued that lack of tard corrupts any definition, but the author refutes this by distinguishing between verbal and nominal definitions. Verbal definitions (as in lexicons) merely explain the meaning of a word and do not need to be comprehensive; they only need to be clear. Nominal definitions (as in technical terminology) require tard. The passage also references discussions in al-Zahidiyyah and al-Mahsul, and names al-Taftazani. The conclusion is that the definition of 'asl' as 'ma yahtaju ilayhi' is a definition by the more general (al-amm), which is acceptable as an incomplete definition that distinguishes 'asl' from 'far''.

Key Terms
طرد (tard): Comprehensiveness: the definition should apply to all instances of the defined term
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A definition that explains the meaning of a term by listing its essential characteristics
تعریف لفظی (ta'rif lafzi): A definition that simply explains the meaning of a word using a more well-known synonym

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The commentator does not have authority
C) The definition is complete and has tard

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, tard is not an absolute condition; verbal definitions and incomplete nominal definitions that serve a specific purpose are accepted.

The Requirement of Tard in Definitions and the Definition of Al-Asl
Defending Sadr al-Shariah's objection to the definition of al-asl as muhtaj ilayhi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between nominal and lexical definitions in Hanafi usul and evaluate the necessity of tard (comprehensiveness) in defining technical terms like al-asl.

Core Idea
Not all definitions require tard; lexical definitions need only synonymy, while nominal definitions demand comprehensiveness.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Sadr al-Shariah and Taftazani over the definition of al-asl (the original/root). The key issue is whether the condition of tard (comprehensiveness/coextensiveness) is necessary for all definitions. By understanding the distinction between nominal (ismi) and lexical (lafzi) definitions, you will see why Sadr al-Shariah rejects the definition of al-asl as 'muhtaj ilayhi' (that which is needed) and proposes 'ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr' (that upon which something else is founded).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The author (Sadr al-Shariah) argues that tard is not a necessary condition for all definitions; it is required only for nominal definitions. The commentator (Taftazani) insists that tard is necessary for every definition, including lexical ones.
Keep track of who holds which view: the passage defends the author against Taftazani.
2
Understand the distinction between nominal and lexical definitions
A nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) aims to capture the essence of a term and must be both comprehensive (tard) and exclusive ('aks). A lexical definition (ta'rif lafzi) simply explains a word by a more common synonym and does not require tard. The passage argues that definitions in dictionaries (kutub al-lughah) are lexical, not nominal.
This distinction is crucial for evaluating the validity of definitions in usul.
3
Analyze Taftazani's objection
Taftazani claims that the definition of al-asl as 'muhtaj ilayhi' is valid and comprehensive. He argues that it applies to the agent (fa'il), and that the author himself elsewhere admits that every 'muhtaj ilayhi' is an 'asl'.
The passage systematically refutes each of Taftazani's points.
4
Trace the Hanafi response
The author's defenders make three points: (a) The definition 'muhtaj ilayhi' applies to conditions and ends, which are not 'asl', so it lacks tard. (b) The term 'asl' does not lexically apply to the agent; 'ibtina' means foundational dependence, not causal dependence. (c) The author's discussion in the chapter on majaz only provides a criterion for distinguishing haqiqah from majaz, not a universal definition.
Focus on how each rebuttal undermines Taftazani's position.
5
Apply the concept to a new usul term
Consider how you would define another technical term like 'amm (general) or 'illah (cause). Would you provide a nominal or lexical definition? What conditions would it need to satisfy?
This step reinforces the practical relevance of the tard condition.

تاثیری یعنی ابتناء الشتی علی الغیر سے مراد یہ ہے کہ یہ غیر اسی شئی کے لئے بمنزلہ اساس کے ہو نہ یہ کہ وہ غیر اس شئی کے وجود میں مؤثر ہو فاصل مؤثر في وجود الفعل ہوتا ہے نہ یہ کہ فاعل ایک اساس ہے جس پر فعل کی بنا ہو لہذا ما يبتنی علیه الغیر والی تعریف صادق علی الفاعل نہیں ہو سکتی ثالثاً یہ کہ فاعل پر الا صل کے صادق آجانے کے ساتھ محتاج الیہ والی تعریف پھر بھی مطرد نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ غایت اور شرط پر محتاج الیہ ہونا صادق آتا ہے لیکن وہ الاصل نہیں ہیں پھر بھی تو طرد برقرار نہ ہوا۔ الثالث اس بحث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے باب المجازہ میں جریان الاصالة والتبعية من الجانبیین میں جو کلام کی ہے وہ دلالت کرتی ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل ہے تو جب مصنف اس بحث میں محتاج الیہ کا اصل ہونا تسلیم کر رہا ہے تو پھر صاحب المحصول نے جو الا صل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کی ہے تو یہ محل اعتراض کیوں ہے۔ جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ مصنف کی عبارت اس پر قطعا دال نہیں ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل ہے تا کہ محتاج الیہ والی تعریف مطرد عند المصنف ہو بلکہ اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جب حقیقت جو بدرجہ اصل ہے اور مجاز جو بدرجہ فرع ہے تو جہاں ان دونوں کے درمیان اشتباہ واقع ہو جائے اور ان کے درمیان امتیاز کرنا مقصود ہو تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ جو محتاج الیہ کے درجہ میں ہے تو اس کو اصل قرار دیا جائے گا اور جو محتاج ہوگا
And here is a discussion from several aspects: First, the summary of this topic is that in absolute definition, tard is not a necessary condition. Therefore, the lack of tard, as in the definition of al-Muhassal, does not corrupt the definition. Rather, even without tard, the definition is correct. Especially in a nominal definition, tard is not a condition. Observe that in lexicological books, interpretations of words are often found that are more general than the interpreted [word] and apply to other than the specific, yet no one criticizes them for lack of tard. So it is known that tard is not a necessary condition for the correctness of a definition. You will recall that the commentator (sharih) said at the beginning of this statement: 'This has no bearing on explaining the corruption of definition due to lack of tard, absolutely, whether it is a nominal definition or otherwise.' In this statement, the commentator declares lack of tard to be corrupting for every definition, whether nominal or not. But he criticizes the author (musannif) without reason—the commentator has a secondary habit, so he always makes invalid objections, and this is an example of it. However, tard is a condition for definition; the commentator's denial is merely arbitrary. Then consider the commentator's proof, which he presented with 'fa inna kutub al-lughah' etc. This is also astonishing, because all these definitions found in lexicological books are lexical definitions, not nominal definitions. There is a great difference between the two. Self-evident matters are defined lexically, but not nominally. Here the term 'asl' is a technical matter, and the books of usul that define it give a nominal definition for which tard is a condition. This lexical definition, which is synonymous with a more common word, is not that. Therefore, the commentator's argument does not support his claim. It is stated in al-Zahidiyyah on general matters: 'Al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani and those who agreed with him held that it is a lexical definition from the category of tasawwuri demands, claiming no difference between it and nominal definition. But it is clear that the self-evident can bear lexical definition but not nominal definition. The definitions mentioned in lexicological books are lexical from the category of tasdiqi demands.' The investigators (muhaqqiqun) have stated that the summary of this discussion is that investigators have permitted definition by inclusive (al-a'amm) in incomplete definitions, which only give distinction from some of the limits of the defined, not preventing entry of others. Because sometimes the purpose of interpretation is distinction from a specific thing. For example, here we want to distinguish the original from the derivative; we define the original as 'that which is needed by something else' (al-muhtaj ilayhi) and the derivative as 'that which needs' (al-muhtaj). The commentator's discussion has no effect on the author, because in this discussion it is admitted that the definition of the original as 'muhtaj ilayhi' is a definition by inclusive (ta'rif bi'l-a'amm), which is incomplete and does not prevent entry of others, nor does it give distinction from everything else. These are the reasons why the author considered this definition objectionable and abandoned it. So what benefit did the commentator gain by objecting to the author without reason? Second, the summary of this discussion: The predicate (fa'il) is such that the definition 'muhtaj ilayhi' applies to it, and similarly the defined (al-asl) also applies to it, because the existence of the act is dependent on the agent and attributed to the agent. And the author's definition of al-asl as 'ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr' also applies to the agent, because 'ibtina' 'ala al-ghayr' means being dependent on and attributed to that other. So according to the author's definition, al-asl also applies to the agent. Thus, the author's objection that the definition 'muhtaj ilayhi' applies to the agent but the defined (al-asl) does not, making the definition non-comprehensive, falls away. The answer given is that the author means that the term 'asl' is not applied to the agent lexically or in usage. The commentator only mentioned the denial of the applicability of 'asl' to the agent; with that, the application of 'asl' to the agent is not established unless a report of such application is presented. Secondly, 'ibtina'' means foundational dependence, not effective dependence. That is, 'ibtina' of a thing upon another means that this other is like a foundation for that thing, not that the other is effective in the existence of that thing. The agent is effective in the existence of the act, not that the agent is a foundation upon which the act is built. Therefore, the definition 'ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr' cannot apply to the agent. Thirdly, even if 'al-asl' applies to the agent, the definition 'muhtaj ilayhi' still cannot be comprehensive because 'muhtaj ilayhi' applies to the end and the condition, but they are not 'asl'. So still comprehensiveness is not maintained. Third, the summary of this discussion: The author's discussion in the chapter of majaz about the flow of originality and subordination from both sides indicates that every 'muhtaj ilayhi' is an 'asl'. So when the author admits in this discussion that 'muhtaj ilayhi' is 'asl', then why is the definition of al-asl by sahib al-Muhassal as 'muhtaj ilayhi' objectionable? The answer given is that the author's statement does not indicate that every 'muhtaj ilayhi' is 'asl' so that the definition by 'muhtaj ilayhi' would be comprehensive according to the author. Rather, his meaning is that when the reality which is at the level of 'asl' and the metaphor which is at the level of far' are confused, and distinction between them is intended, then it will be seen which is at the level of 'muhtaj ilayhi'—that will be considered 'asl', and which is 'muhtaj' (needing).
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a detailed critical commentary defending the position of the author (Sadr al-Shariah) against the attacks of the commentator (Taftazani) regarding the definition of 'al-asl' (the original/root). The central issue is whether the condition of 'tard' (comprehensiveness/coextensiveness) is necessary for a correct definition. The passage argues three main points: (1) Tard is not a necessary condition for all definitions; it is required for nominal (ismi) definitions but not for lexical (lafzi) definitions. The commentator incorrectly treats lexical definitions as if they were nominal. (2) Even if the definition 'muhtaj ilayhi' applies to the agent (fa'il), the author's objection that it is not comprehensive still stands because the term 'asl' does not lexically apply to the agent, and the concept of 'ibtina' is foundational, not causal. (3) The author's discussion elsewhere does not imply that every 'muhtaj ilayhi' is 'asl'; it only provides a criterion for distinguishing between haqiqah and majaz, not a universal definition. The passage uses rigorous usul reasoning with examples from Arabic lexicography and usul texts.

Key Terms
طرد (tard): Comprehensiveness or coextensiveness of a definition, meaning the definition applies to all instances of the defined term and nothing else.
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A nominal definition that provides the essence or quiddity (mahiyyah) of a thing, requiring both tard and 'aks (comprehensiveness and exclusiveness).
تعریف لفظی (ta'rif lafzi): A lexical definition that explains a word by a more common synonym; it does not require tard as it merely gives a rough equivalence.
اصل (asl): The original or root; that upon which something else is built and without which it cannot exist. In usul, it is contrasted with far' (derivative).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the definition of al-asl as 'muhtaj ilayhi' is rejected?
A) It is too narrow and excludes the agent (fa'il).
B) It is not comprehensive because it also applies to conditions and ends, which are not considered asl.
C) It is a lexical definition, not a nominal definition.
D) The term 'muhtaj ilayhi' is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
The definition of al-asl as 'muhtaj ilayhi' is rejected because it lacks tard; a proper nominal definition requires foundational dependence (ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr).

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
Definition of 'Asl' in Hanafi Usul: Foundational vs. Effective Dependence
Analyzing objections to the definition of 'asl' and providing responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi definition of 'asl' as 'ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr' and the alternative definition 'muhtaj ilayh', and apply the criteria of tard (coextensiveness) and jami' (comprehensiveness) to evaluate them.

Core Idea
An 'asl' is a foundation, not merely a cause; effective dependence does not make one an origin.

This passage from Sadr al-Shariah's 'al-Tawdih' and its commentary engages with definitions of 'asl' (origin) in usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi school insists on a precise definition that captures the foundational relationship, rejecting broader alternatives. The commentator addresses four objections to the author's definition, clarifying the distinction between foundational reliance (ibtina' asasi) and effective reliance (ibtina' ta'thiri).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of 'asl'
Locate in the passage the definition proposed by the author (ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr) and the alternative (muhtaj ilayh) that is criticized.
The author is Sadr al-Shariah; the opponent may be the commentator or the author of al-Mahsul.
2
Apply the criterion of tard (coextensiveness)
Check whether the alternative definition 'muhtaj ilayh' applies to all instances that should be 'asl' and excludes non-instances. The objection is that it applies to the agent (fa'il) but 'asl' does not apply to the agent.
Also check that it excludes ends and conditions (ghayat wa shart) which are not 'asl'.
3
Distinguish foundational vs. effective reliance
Understand the Hanafi response: 'ibtina' in the definition means foundational reliance (istinad asasi), not effective reliance (istinad ta'thiri). The agent is effective, not foundational, so the definition does not apply.
This refines the definition to exclude mere causality.
4
Analyze the third objection and response
The opponent cites the author's own words from the metaphor chapter to argue that he himself equates 'muhtaj ilayh' with 'asl'. Examine how the author's response limits that statement to local distinction, not a universal definition.
This shows the importance of context in usul definitions.
5
Evaluate the fourth objection regarding thought
The objection claims the author's definition is not comprehensive because thought depends on known matters but not in the sense of 'subordination of a ruling to its evidence'. The response clarifies that intellectual dependence (ibtina' 'aqli) is defined as 'subordination of one thing to another in the mind', which does apply.
This highlights that examples do not restrict definitions.

حاصل ہوا۔ والثانی اس بحث کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ فاعل پہ جیسے محتاج الیہ والی حدو تعریف صادق آ رہی ہے اسی طرح محدود یعنی الاصل بھی اس پر صادق آتا ہے کیونکہ وجود فعل مترتب على الفاعل اورستند الی الفاعل ہوتا صادق علی الفاعل ہے لہذا مصنف " کا اعتراض کرنا کہ فاعل پر محتاج الیہ والی تعریف صادق آتی ہے اور محدود یعنی الاصل صادق نہیں آتا لہذا یہ تعریف مطرد نہیں ہے یہ اعتراض ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ لفظ اصل کا اطلاق علی الفاعل اور اس کی استعمال في الفاصل واقع نہیں ہے اور شارح نے صرف عدم صدق الاصل علی الفاعل کے متعلق صرف منع ذکر کی ہے اس کے ساتھ اطلاق اصل علی الفاعل صحیح نہیں ہو جاتا جب تک اس اطلاق کی نقل پیش نہ کی جائے۔ ثانیاً یہ کہ ابتناء سے مراد استناد اساسی ہے نہ کہ استناد تاثیری یعنی ابتناء الشتی علی الغیر سے مراد یہ ہے کہ یہ غیر اسی شئی کے لئے بمنزلہ اساس کے ہو نہ یہ کہ وہ غیر اس شئی کے وجود میں مؤثر ہو فاصل مؤثر في وجود الفعل ہوتا ہے نہ یہ کہ فاعل ایک اساس ہے جس پر فعل کی بنا ہو لہذا ما يبتنی علیه الغیر والی تعریف صادق علی الفاعل نہیں ہو سکتی ثالثاً یہ کہ فاعل پر الا صل کے صادق آجانے کے ساتھ محتاج الیہ والی تعریف پھر بھی مطرد نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ غایت اور شرط پر محتاج الیہ ہونا صادق آتا ہے لیکن وہ الاصل نہیں ہیں پھر بھی تو طرد برقرار نہ ہوا۔ الثالث اس بحث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مصنف " نے باب المجازہ میں جریان الاصالة والتبعية من الجانبیین میں جو کلام کی ہے وہ دلالت کرتی ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل ہے تو جب مصنف اس بحث میں محتاج الیہ کا اصل ہونا تسلیم کر رہا ہے تو پھر صاحب المحصول نے جو الا صل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کی ہے تو یہ محل اعتراض کیوں ہے۔ جواب اس کا یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ مصنف کی عبارت اس پر قطعا دال نہیں ہے کہ ہر محتاج الیہ اصل ہے تا کہ محتاج الیہ والی تعریف مطرد عند المصنف ہو بلکہ اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جب حقیقت جو بدرجہ اصل ہے اور مجاز جو بدرجہ فرع ہے تو جہاں ان دونوں کے درمیان اشتباہ واقع ہو جائے اور ان کے درمیان امتیاز کرنا مقصود ہو تو دیکھا جائے گا کہ جو محتاج الیہ کے درجہ میں ہے تو اس کو اصل قرار دیا جائے گا اور جو محتاج ہوگا اس کو فروع کہا جائے گا یہ تو صرف مقامی لحاظ سے تفرقہ کرنا مطلوب ہے اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ الاصل کی تعریف علی الاطلاق محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ صحیح ہو جائے۔ الرابع اس بحث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مصنف کی تعریف الاصل ما يبتنی علیہ الغیر جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ فکر کی تعریف جو ترتیب امور معلومہ کے ساتھ کی جاتی ہے تو امور معلومہ فکر کے لئے مادہ اور اصل ہیں حالانکہ فکر کی ابتنا ان امور معلومہ پر حسی تو ہے نہیں جیسے کہ یہ ظاہر ہے اور ان امور پر ابتنا ، عقلی بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ مصنف کے نزدیک ابتنا، عقلی کی تعریف ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ ہے اور فکر کا ابتناء ان امور پر ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ تو ہے نہیں لہذا مصنف کی تعریف جامع نہیں ہے یہ اعتراض بالکل لغو اور ضعیف ہے کیونکہ یہ پہلے واضح ہو چکا ہے کہ ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ یہ صرف ابتنا، عقلی کی تمثیل ہے کی نہ کہ تعریف اور شارح نے خود بھی اسے تسلیم کیا تھا اب معلوم نہیں کہ شارح کیوں یہ اعتراض کر رہا ہے صرف اپنی عادت کو پورا کرنے کی خاطر ور نہ تو ابتنا، عقلی کی تعریف جو مصنف کی عبارت سے مفہوم ہوتی ہے وہ یہ ہے ترتب امر علی آخر فی العقل وہو صادق علی ابتناء الفكر على الامور المذكورة
It is not that it cannot provide distinction from all other [things]. So these are the reasons on the basis of which the author considered this definition objectionable and abandoned it. Then what benefit did the commentator gain by objecting to the author without reason? Second: The summary of this discussion is that just as the definition of 'dependent on' applies to the agent, similarly the limited [term], i.e., 'asl', also applies to it, because the existence of the act is dependent on the agent and is attributed to the agent. And the author's definition of 'asl' as 'that upon which the other is based' applies to the agent, because 'being based on another' means being dependent on and attributed to that other. Therefore, according to the author's definition, 'asl' also applies to the agent. Hence, the author's objection that the definition of 'dependent on' applies to the agent but 'asl' (the limited) does not, so this definition is not coextensive, falls away. The answer given is that the author means that the word 'asl' is not used for the agent, and the commentator only mentioned denial regarding the non-application of 'asl' to the agent. This does not make the application of 'asl' to the agent correct unless a transmitted usage is cited. Secondly, 'being based on' means foundational reliance, not effective reliance. That is, 'being based on another' means that this other is like a foundation for that thing, not that the other is effective in its existence. The agent is effective in the existence of the act, not that the agent is a foundation upon which the act is built. Thus, the definition 'that upon which the other is based' cannot apply to the agent. Thirdly, even if 'asl' applies to the agent, the definition of 'dependent on' still cannot be coextensive because 'dependent on' applies to the end and condition, but they are not 'asl'. Yet the coextensiveness is not maintained. Third: The summary of this discussion is that the author's statement in the chapter on metaphor about the flow of originality and subsidiary from both sides indicates that every 'dependent on' is 'asl'. So when the author in this discussion accepts that 'dependent on' is 'asl', then why is the definition of 'asl' by the author of al-Mahsul as 'dependent on' objectionable? The answer given is that the author's statement does not definitively indicate that every 'dependent on' is 'asl', such that the definition of 'dependent on' would be coextensive according to the author. Rather, he means that when reality, which is at the level of 'asl', and metaphor, which is at the level of branch, are confused and distinction between them is intended, then whichever is at the level of 'dependent on' will be considered 'asl', and whichever is dependent will be called branch. This is only a local distinction; it does not necessitate that the definition of 'asl' absolutely is correct with 'dependent on'. Fourth: The summary of this discussion is that the author's definition of 'asl' as 'that upon which the other is based' is not comprehensive, because the definition of thought as 'arrangement of known matters' makes the known matters the matter and origin for thought, although the dependence of thought on these known matters is neither sensory, as is apparent, nor intellectual, because according to the author, the definition of intellectual dependence is 'the subordination of a ruling to its evidence', and the dependence of thought on these matters is not the subordination of a ruling to its evidence. Hence the author's definition is not comprehensive. This objection is completely frivolous and weak, because it has already been clarified that 'the subordination of a ruling to its evidence' is only an example of intellectual dependence, not its definition, and the commentator himself acknowledged that. It is not known why the commentator raises this objection, perhaps only out of habit. Otherwise, the definition of intellectual dependence understood from the author's statement is 'the subordination of one thing to another in the mind', and that applies to the dependence of thought on the mentioned matters.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute where the commentator (Sharh) critiques and defends the definition of 'asl' (origin) as given by the matn author (Sadr al-Shariah). The discussion is structured around four objections and their responses. The first objection (al-thani) concerns whether 'asl' applies to the agent (fa'il). The commentator argues that the definition 'ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr' (that upon which the other is based) does not apply to the agent because 'being based' here means foundational reliance (istinad asasi) not effective reliance (istinad ta'thiri). The agent is effective in the existence of the act, not the foundation. The second objection (al-thalith) raises that the author's own statements in the metaphor chapter imply that every 'dependent on' (muhtaj ilayh) is 'asl', but the response clarifies that this is only a local criterion for distinguishing reality from metaphor, not a universal definition. The third objection (al-rabi') claims the definition is not comprehensive because thought (fikr) depends on known matters but not in the sense of subordination of a ruling to evidence. The response rejects this by stating that 'subordination of a ruling to evidence' is only an example of intellectual dependence, not its definition; the real definition is 'subordination of one thing to another in the mind', which applies to thought. This critical refinement follows the Hanafi usul tradition of rigorous definition and counter-definition.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): That upon which another thing is based (ma yabtani 'alayhi al-ghayr), in contrast to branch (far').
محتاج الیہ (muhtaj ilayh): That which is needed or depended upon by another; proposed as a definition of 'asl' but rejected here.
ابتناء عقلی (ibtina' 'aqli): Intellectual dependence: the subordination of one thing to another in the mind (tartubu amrin 'ala akhar fi al-'aql).
مطرد (mutarid): Coextensive; a definition that applies to all members of the defined term and excludes non-members.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi author reject the definition of 'asl' as 'muhtaj ilayh' (that which is depended upon)?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah.
B) Because it fails the criterion of tard (coextensiveness) as it applies to ends and conditions which are not 'asl'.
C) Because it is the definition used by the Shafi'i school.
D) Because it is too narrow and excludes the agent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'asl' as foundational reliance (ibtina' asasi) is more precise than alternative definitions and is essential for correct analogical reasoning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Three Objections to the Definition of Hukm and Ash'ari Responses
Criticizing the definition of hukm shari' with three objections and Ash'ari replies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of iqtida' dimni to include wad'i rulings in the definition of hukm and evaluate the three Ash'ari responses.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm can include wad'i rulings through implicit demand, as taught by the Hanafi school.

This lesson delves into three objections raised against the standard definition of hukm shari'i, particularly regarding its failure to encompass wad'i (declaratory) rulings. The Ash'ari school offers diverse responses, from adding a new term to denying that wad'i address constitutes a ruling. The Hanafi school, however, elegantly includes wad'i rulings via the concept of implicit demand (iqtida' dimni), preserving the definition's comprehensiveness without modification. Understanding these debates strengthens your ability to define and classify legal rulings within usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under critique
Recall the definition of hukm shari'i: 'Allah's address relating to acts of legally responsible persons by demand (iqtida'), choice (takhyir), or wad''. Focus on the three categories mentioned.
The third category (wad') is not universally accepted.
2
List the three objections
The first objection: rulings are temporal (hadith) while the definition implies eternal character. The second: the particle 'aw' may indicate doubt, invalid for definitions. The third: wad'i rulings (cause, condition, preventer) are excluded because they lack demand or choice.
Each objection targets a specific aspect: temporality, linguistic form, and comprehensiveness.
3
Analyze the Ash'ari responses to each objection
For objection 1: distinguish between ruling (eternal) and its attachment (originated); 'illah can be a sign, not an efficient cause. For objection 2: 'aw here is tanwi'iyyah (division of types), not tashkikiyyah (doubt). For objection 3: three Ash'ari groups respond—adding 'aw al-wad', denying wad'i as ruling, or interpreting wad'i as implicit demand.
The third response aligns with the Hanafi position.
4
Compare the Hanafi position with the Ash'ari responses
The Hanafi school adopts the third Ash'ari response: all wad'i rulings are included under 'implicit demand' (iqtida' dimni). For example, the cause of sunset implies the obligation of prayer. This avoids changing the definition.
The Hanafi position is thus more parsimonious and maintains the original definition.
5
Recognize the internal diversity among Ash'aris
The passage identifies three distinct Ash'ari groups with varying responses. This highlights that consensus within a school is not always absolute.
Understanding these nuances is key for advanced usul analysis.

دوسرا گروہ ہے۔ ولو سلم فلا نسلمان شارح نے اس تسلیمی جواب کو اس دوسرے فریق کی طرف منسوب کر دیا یعنی پہلا جواب ان کی طرف سے عدم تسلیمی تھا اور ان ہی کی طرف سے یہ تسلیمی جواب ہے حالانکہ یہ صحیح نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ اشاعرہ کا تیسرا فریق ہے جو خطاب وضعی کا حکم ہونا تو تسلیم کرتا ہے لیکن او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کرنے کی ضرورت تسلیم نہیں کرتا بلکہ اقتضاء کی تعمیم کرکے ان خطابات کو اقتضا ، ضمنی میں ترج کرتا ہے تو یہ درحقیقت وہی حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ فلانسلو خروجها عن الحد يعني ان خطابات وضعیه کا خروج از تعریف حکم ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کیونکہ ہماری مراد بالاقتضاء، والتغییر سے عام ہے خواہ صریح ہو یا ضمنی تو خطاب وضع اقتضاء ضمنی کے قبیلہ سے ہے اور اسی میں درج ہے کیونکہ سبینہ دلوک سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس وقت نماز واجب ہے اور شرطیہ طہارت کا معنی یہ ہے کہ صلوٰۃ میں طہارت واجب ہے اور بدون الطہارت نماز کا ادا کر نا حرام ہے اور مانعیت نجاست سے مقصود یہ ہے کہ نجاست کے ہوتے ہوئے ادائیگی نماز حرام ہے یا یہ کہ حالتِ صلوٰۃ میں اس کا ازالہ واجب ہے كذا في جميع الاسباب والشور والمواقع تو تمام اسباب اور شروط و موانع میں یہی تاویل کر کے اقتضاء ضمنی میں درج کیا جائے گا تو ا و الوضع کی قید کے اضافہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ۔ اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس بارہ میں اشاعرہ کے تین گروہ
Third objection: the definition is not comprehensive. The third objection is that this definition is not comprehensive of all individuals, because wad'i [declaratory] rulings like the causality of the sun's decline for the obligation of prayer, the conditionality of purity for prayer, and the preventiveness of impurity for prayer are not included, because they contain neither demand (iqtida) nor choice (takhyir), while they are rulings. So this definition is not comprehensive. And the author [musannif] omitted mentioning man'iyyah in the interpretation of 'aw'. The author omitted mentioning preventiveness in the interpretation of wad'i address, while mentioning it was necessary; by habit they objected to the author. Yet in the text, after 'sababiyyah' and 'shartiyyah' the author mentioned the word 'maw' (?) indicating preventiveness etc. So the author did not omit its mention; rather the commentator did not pay attention to it. The Ash'aris answered the first objection by denial: they said we do not accept that the ruling is qualified by existence after non-existence; rather the attachment (ta'liq) of the ruling exists after non-existence, and the attachment is originated, while the ruling itself is eternal. 'She became permissible after not being permissible' means: the attachment of permissibility to the woman existed after it was not attached. She was not attached before, after marriage the attachment of permissibility to her occurs. So the attachment is originated, not the ruling. And they deny the reasoning of hukm. This is the answer to the first objection's second point: the word 'illah is used in two senses: one is effective cause (mu'aththirah) which influences the existence of the effect, bringing it from non-existence to existence. The second is 'illah as sign/mark (amarah wa 'alamah). Its function is not influence/effect but it is a sign to know the existence of the effect. A originated effective cause cannot be for the eternal, but a sign can be, just as the existence of the world is a sign for knowledge of the eternal Creator. So the existence of the universe gives knowledge that there must be an eternal Creator. Similarly, marriage is a sign for knowledge of permissibility, and divorce is a sign for knowledge of prohibition, because shari' acts are signs and indicators, not bringers into existence and effecters. And about the second [objection]: by 'aw' [meaning doubt or disjunction]… The answer to the second objection is: the word 'aw' has two types: one is for tanwi' (division into types), i.e., a thing has multiple different types, and 'aw' is used to express them. Its use in definitions is correct when the defined's types are different, because it is difficult to collect different types into one definition. So here 'aw' is for division and detailing of the defined, because one type of ruling is that which relates to the act of the mukallaf by demand and request, and another type relates to [wad']? So using 'aw' to present these type details was necessary. The second type of 'aw' is for tashkik (doubt/hesitation). This type of 'aw' is not correct in definition. Summary of answer: this 'aw' is for tanwi', which is correct in definitions, and it is not for tashkik, which is not correct. As for the third [objection], its answer is detailed. Summary: Some Ash'aris conceded that this definition does not include wad'i rulings, so it is not comprehensive. They added the qualification 'aw al-wad' to make it comprehensive. So the definition of hukm according to them becomes: 'the address of Allah the Exalted relating to the acts of the legally responsible ones by demand, choice, or wad'. This is one faction of Ash'aris. And some of them answered: we do not accept that wad'i address is a ruling at all; we do not call it a ruling, although others do; that is their terminology. Hence there is no dispute in terminology; only they need to change the definition, not us. This is the second group. And if it is conceded [that wad'i is a ruling], we do not concede that it falls outside the definition. The commentator attributed this concessionary answer to the second group, but this is not correct; rather there is a third group of Ash'aris who concede wad'i address is a ruling but do not concede the need to add 'aw al-wad'. Rather they generalize iqtida', interpreting these addresses as implicit demand (iqtida' dimni). They say: we do not accept their exit from the definition, because we mean by iqtida' and takhyir generally, whether explicit or implicit. So wad'i address is of the type of implicit demand and included in it. For example, the causation of the sun's decline means that at that time prayer is obligatory; the conditionality of purity means that in prayer purity is obligatory, and without purity performing prayer is prohibited; the preventiveness of impurity means that while impurity exists, performing prayer is prohibited or that its removal is obligatory during prayer. Similarly for all causes, conditions, and preventers, this interpretation is made and they are included under implicit demand. So adding the qualification 'aw al-wad' is not necessary. From this detail it is known that regarding this matter there are three groups of Ash'aris.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage examines three objections leveled against the definition of 'hukm shari' (legal ruling), typical of Ash'ari critiques, and the responses offered by various Ash'ari factions. The first objection is that rulings are qualified by temporal existence ('huduth'), but the Ash'aris respond by distinguishing between the ruling itself (eternal) and its attachment (originated). They also clarify that the term 'illah (cause) can mean either an effective cause or a sign; acts like marriage are signs, not efficient causes. The second objection concerns the word 'aw' in the definition, which could imply doubt. The Ash'aris explain that here 'aw' is used for tanwi' (division of types), not tashkik (doubt), and is thus valid. The third objection is that the definition fails to include wad'i rulings (like cause, condition, preventer). Three Ash'ari groups respond: one adds 'aw al-wad' to the definition; another denies that wad'i address is a ruling at all; a third includes wad'i rulings under 'implicit demand' (iqtida' dimni) without adding a new term. The commentator notes that the author of the matn actually indicated preventiveness via 'maw' and the commentator neglected it. This demonstrates the nuance in defining fundamental usul terms and the internal diversity within the Ash'ari school.

Key Terms
حكم شرعي (hukm shari'i): Legal ruling defined as Allah's address relating to acts of legally responsible persons by demand, choice, or wad'
خطاب وضعي (khitab wad'i): Declaratory address: Allah's statements about causes, conditions, and preventers
او تنويعة (aw tanyaw'iyyah): The particle 'aw' used to indicate different types of a single category

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Ash'ari group responded to the third objection by interpreting wad'i rulings as implicit demand (iqtida' dimni)?
A) The first group, which added 'aw al-wad' to the definition.
B) The second group, which denied that wad'i address is a ruling.
C) The third group, which generalized iqtida' to include implicit demand.
D) The Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school includes wad'i rulings in the definition of hukm through the concept of implicit demand (iqtida' dimni), making the definition comprehensive without needing modification.

Mutual Exclusivity of Hukm Taklifi and Hukm Wad'i
Refuting the inclusion of hukm wad'i within hukm taklifi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i based on their necessary concomitants (lawazim) and explain why they are mutually exclusive realities in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are mutually exclusive (mutabayinan); one cannot include the other.

This passage tackles a critical classification issue in Hanafi usul: whether declaratory rulings (ahkam wad'iyya) can be considered a subset of prescriptive rulings (ahkam taklifiyya). The author argues forcefully that they are separate and exclusive categories. Understanding this distinction is essential for properly deriving and categorizing rulings from the primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Define hukm taklifi (prescriptive ruling) and hukm wad'i (declaratory ruling). Hukm taklifi demands action or abstention, while hukm wad'i establishes relationships (sabab, shart, mani).
2
Understand the Refuted Claim
Some scholars held that hukm wad'i is implicitly included within hukm taklifi (as a part or consequence). This is the view the author refutes.
3
Analyze the Author's Argument
The author uses the concept of 'lazim' (necessary concomitant). The lazim of hukm wad'i is 'talluq shay' bi shay' (connection of one thing to another); the lazim of hukm taklifi is wujub or hurma (obligation or prohibition). These are mutually exclusive, so the rulings themselves must be mutually exclusive.
Mutual exclusivity of lawazim implies mutual exclusivity of malzumat (subjects).
4
Recognize the Commentator's Objection and Rebuttal
The commentator accused the author of tasamuh (leniency) in definition. The author responds that he was presenting the lazim, not the essential meaning. Hence the objection is invalid.
5
Apply the Principle
Practice identifying whether a given shari' ruling is taklifi or wad'i, and determine its lazim. Confirm they belong to distinct categories.
For example, 'wudu is a condition for prayer' is wad'i (shart). 'Prayer is obligatory' is taklifi.

Source Text

تھے بلکہ اقتضا ضمنی میں درج کر کے خطاب تکلیفی میں داخل کرتے تھے ان پہ مصنف نے رد کیا ہے بقوله لان المفهوم من الحكم الوضعي تعلق شي بشئ آخر اس عبارت کے ساتھ مصنف صرف تفایر مفہوم نہیں بتلا رہا بلکہ یہ ثابت کر رہا ہے کہ حکم تکلیفی اور حکم وضعی نوعان مقباسنان و حقیقتان مختلفان فكيف يندرج أحدهما في الآخر لان المتباين لا يندرج في حقيقة متباتنہ اور مصنف اس تباین حقیقت کی طرف اشارہ کرتے ہوئے کہ رہا ہے ان المفہوم من الحکم الوضعی تعلق شی یہ حکم وضعی کا مفہوم و معنی پیش نہیں کر رہا ہے بلکہ اس کا لازم پیش کر رہا ہے تب تو وہ کہہ رہا ہے المفہوم من الحكم الوضعی یعنی حکم وضعی سے بطور لازم کے جو سمجھ آتا ہے وہ ہے تعلق شی بشی یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ خطاب وصنع کا مفہوم و معنیٰ یہی ہے لہذا شارح کی اگلی بحث جس کے اندر مصنف پر الزام مسامحہ دیا ہے وہ ساقط ہو جائے گی اور حکم تکلیفی سے بطور لازم کے یہ مفہوم تعلق شی بشی حاصل نہیں بلکہ اس سے بطور لازم کے جو کچھ سمجھ آتا ہے وہ ہے وجوب فعل یا تحریم فعل اور یہ دونوں لازم آپس میں متباین ہیں اور تباین لوازم دلیل ہوتا ہے تبدین ملزومات کی تو جب خطاب وضعی اور خطاب تکلیفی آپس میں متباستین ہیں تو ایک متباین کے اندر تعمیم کر کے دوسرے متبائن کو اس میں داخل کرنا کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے اب شارح کی یہ توجیہ کی وکیل الخطاب التكليفي اہم منہ شاملاً لہ یہ بے فائدہ ہے کیونکہ مقبائن کے اندر تعمیم کر کے اس کے دوسرے مقیائن کو شامل کرنا کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے۔ فاتي صور له في تغاير مفهو ميهما یہاں صرف تغایر مفہو مین نہیں ہے بلکہ تباین مفہومین ہے لہذا ایک متباین دوسرے متبائن کو شامل نہیں ہو سکتا فيلزم ضرر عدم الجامعية كيف يتحد مفهوم العام والخاص ليس بينها عموم و خصوص بل بينهما تباين على ان المفهوم من الخطاب الوضعي یہ اعتراض بھی فضول ہے کیونکہ مصنف ” خطاب وضعی کا مفہوم و معنی پیش نہیں کر رہا بلکہ اس کا لازم پیش کر رہا ہے جو ملزوم سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے اور حکمین کے لازمین مقباستین پیش کر کے ملزومین کے تباین کو ثابت کر رہا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ المفہوم من الحكم الوضعي و المفہوم من التكليفی کہا ہے مفہوم الحكم الوضعی و مفہوم التکلیفی نہیں کہا۔ اب شارح کا اعتراض بالتسامح مندفع ہے۔
[They] used to include [hukm wad'i] within hukm taklifi by way of implicit inclusion (iqtida). The author refuted them by saying: 'Because the understood meaning from declaratory ruling (hukm wad'i) is the connection of one thing to another.' With this phrase, the author is not merely stating the difference in meaning but is proving that hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are two mutually exclusive types (naw'an mutabayinan) and two different realities. So how can one be included in the other? Because what is mutually exclusive cannot be included in the reality of another mutually exclusive thing. And the author, pointing to this mutual exclusivity of reality, says: 'The understood meaning from declaratory ruling (al-mufhum min al-hukm al-wad'i) is connection of a thing to a thing' – he is not presenting the meaning of declaratory ruling, but rather presenting its necessary concomitant (lazim). So then he says 'al-mufhum min al-hukm al-wad'i' meaning what is understood from declaratory ruling by way of necessity is the connection of a thing to a thing. It is not meant that this is the actual meaning of the address. Hence, the commentator's subsequent discussion in which he accuses the author of leniency (tasamuh) becomes invalid. And from hukm taklifi, this meaning of connection of a thing to a thing is not obtained by way of necessity; rather, what is understood from it by way of necessity is obligation of an act or prohibition of an act. And these two necessary concomitants are mutually exclusive with each other. And the mutual exclusivity of concomitants is evidence for the mutual exclusivity of the subjects. So when declaratory address (khitab wad'i) and taklifi address are mutually exclusive, how can it be correct to generalize one and include the other within it? Now the commentator's justification that 'the encompassing taklifi address includes it (shamila lahu)' is useless, because including one mutually exclusive into another is not correct. So he gave examples of the difference in their meanings. Here it is not merely a difference in meanings but a mutual exclusivity of meanings. Hence one mutually exclusive cannot include another, resulting in lack of comprehensiveness. How can the concept of general and specific be unified? There is not a general-specific relationship between them but mutual exclusivity. Moreover, the accusation that the understood meaning from declaratory address is this objection is also superfluous, because the author is not presenting the meaning of declaratory address, but its necessary concomitant, which is understood from the object. And by presenting the mutually exclusive concomitants of the two rulings, he is proving the mutual exclusivity of the subjects. That is why he said 'al-mufhum min al-hukm al-wad'i' and 'al-mufhum min al-taklifi' and not 'mafhum al-hukm al-wad'i' and 'mafhum al-taklifi'. Now the commentator's objection of leniency is repelled.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a dispute over the classification of declaratory rulings (ahkam wad'iyya) and prescriptive rulings (ahkam taklifiyya). The author refutes those who attempt to include declaratory rulings within prescriptive rulings by way of implicit inclusion. He argues that the two are mutually exclusive (mutabayinan) because their essential meanings are different: prescriptive rulings involve obligation or prohibition directed at the mukallaf, while declaratory rulings involve the connection of one thing to another (e.g., causality, condition, or impediment). The author clarifies that when he says 'the understood meaning from declaratory ruling is connection of a thing to a thing', he is not giving the essence of declaratory ruling but its necessary concomitant (lazim). Similarly, the necessary concomitant of prescriptive rulings is obligation or prohibition, not connection. Since the concomitants are mutually exclusive, the subjects (the rulings themselves) are also mutually exclusive. Therefore, one cannot be subsumed under the other. The commentator's accusation of tasamuh is thus invalid. This argument reinforces the Hanafi distinction between the two categories.

Key Terms
حكم تكليفي (hukm taklifi): A prescriptive ruling that demands action or abstention from the mukallaf, such as obligation or prohibition.
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): A declaratory ruling that establishes a relationship (sabab, shart, mani') between things, without directly demanding action.
متباین (mutabayin): Two things that are mutually exclusive in reality, having no common ground.
لازم (lazim): A necessary concomitant that necessarily follows from a thing without being its essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that hukm taklifi cannot include hukm wad'i?
A) Because hukm wad'i is a subset of hukm taklifi.
B) Because their necessary concomitants are different and mutually exclusive.
C) Because the commentator objected to the definition.
D) Because hukm taklifi only applies to adults.

Key Takeaway
Hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are separate, mutually exclusive categories; the mutual exclusivity of their necessary concomitants proves their fundamental distinction.

The Definition of Hukm: Hanafi and Ash'ari Perspectives
Analyzing objections to the definition of hukm and Hanafi responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between the Hanafi and Ash'ari schools on the definition of hukm and evaluate the arguments for each position, including the handling of rulings concerning minors.

Core Idea
Hukm is either the divine address itself (Ash'ari) or the attribute it establishes in the action (Hanafi) — a foundational usul difference.

This passage tackles a core usul question: what exactly is a shari' ruling? Hanafi jurists define hukm as the attribute of obligation or prohibition that becomes attached to an action (e.g., wujub, hurmah), while Ash'ari scholars insist it is the divine speech itself (khitab Allah). The text presents two objections to the Hanafi definition and multiple responses, revealing the theological and methodological stakes of this definitional debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of hukm
The passage begins by stating the Hanafi definition: hukm is 'that which is established by address' (thabit bil-khitab), i.e., attributes like wujub. The first objection is that this fails to capture the intended meaning; the responses then clarify the Hanafi view and contrast it with the Ash'ari position that hukm is the khitab itself.
Focus on the difference between 'attribute of action' vs. 'divine speech'.
2
Analyze the three Hanafi responses to the first objection
Three responses are given: (1) 'khitab' in the definition means 'that which is addressed with' by rational context; (2) hukm in reality is ijab/tahrim (divine acts), and wujub/hurmah are metaphorical; (3) hukm is identical to the address itself, but differs by consideration (ijab vs. wujub). Understand the nuance of each.
The third response is closest to the Ash'ari view, showing internal Hanafi variations.
3
Examine the second objection and the Ash'ari answer
The definition includes 'acts of the mukallaf', so rulings on minors (e.g., validity of their acts) seem excluded. Ash'aris answer that such rulings actually relate to the guardian. Evaluate this answer's strength.
Consider the author's refutation using examples of minor's sale, prayer, etc.
4
Evaluate the author's refutation and the commentator's defense
The author (musannif) argues that many rulings directly pertain to the minor, not the guardian. The commentator (sharih) defends the Ash'ari definition by claiming validity/invalidity are rational, not shari', rulings, so the objection misfires. Assess which argument is more persuasive.
Note that the commentator's defense relies on a different classification of 'hukm'.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: for Hanafis, a ruling is a property of the action; for Ash'aris, it is the divine speech itself. This affects how we understand taklif and the nature of obligation. Reflect on why this distinction matters for usul al-fiqh.
The choice influences whether rulings can be analogized or abrogated differently.

الاول ان المقصود الم یعنی مقصود اصلی اُس حکم کی تعریف تھی جو مصطلح بین الفقہاء ہے اور وہ ما ثبت بالخطاب کو حکم کہتے ہیں جیسے وجوب و حرمت جو فعل مکلف کی صفات ہیں فقہاء حضرات نفس خطاب جو اللہ تعالیٰ کی صفات میں سے ہے اس کو حکم نہیں کہتے خلاصہ یہ کہ جو مقصود تھا اس کی تعریف نہیں کی گئی جس کی تعریف کی گئی ہے وہ مقصود نہیں ہے۔
اجيب عنه بوجوه الاول انه كما اريد الا یعنی جیسے ماثبت بالخطاب پر حکم کا اطلاق مصدری مفہوم میں نہیں ہے بلکہ اس سے مراد ما حکیم یہ ہے اسی طرح حکم کی تعریف میں لفظ خطاب سے مراد ما خوطب یہ ہے للقرينة العقلية یعنی عقل شاہد ہے کہ تعریف فقہ میں جو لفظ حکم مذکور ہے اس سے مراد وجوب وحرمت ہے اور وجوب و حرمت نفس خطاب کا نام نہیں ہے بلکہ ما خوطب به کا نام ہے لہذا خطاب سے مراد ما خوطب یہ ہوگا - الثاني ان الحكوا خلاصہ اس جواب کا یہ ہے کہ حقیقتاً حکم وجوب حرمت کا نام نہیں بلکہ ایجاب و تحریم کا نام ہے جو صفات الہیہ میں سے ہیں لہذا اس کی تعریف میں لفظ خطاب اللہ استعمال کرنا صحیح ہے اور ما خوطب بہ کے معنی میں کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور وجوب و حرمت پسا طلاق حکم بنابر مسامحت ہے چونکہ حکم بمعنی ایجاب اور تحریم کا یہ اثر مرتب ہیں لہذا مجازا انہیں حکم کہ دیا گیا ہے۔ الثالث ان الحکم خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ حکم خود خطاب اللہ کا نام ہے کیونکہ ایجاب مین ہے قول افعل کا لیکن فعل مکلف کے لئے اس قول سے کوئی صفت حقیقیہ قائمہ بالفعل نہیں اور چونکہ یہ قول متعلق بالمعدوم ہے اس لئے اس کے متعلق یعنی فعل مکلف کے لئے کوئی صفت قائمہ ماخوذه من القول نہیں ہے بس یہی قول خطاب بعینہ حکم ہے جب اس کی نسبت الی الحاکم ہو تو اسے ایجاب کہتے ہیں جب اس کی نسبت اس فعل کی طرف ہو جس کے بارہ میں یہ قول واقع ہوا ہے تو اسے وجوب کہتے ہیں تو وجوب و ایجاب ذاتاً ایک ہی شئی نہیں کیونکہ یہ دونوں بعینہ قول افعل کا نام ہیں اور مختلف بالاعتبار ہیں یعنی اس اعتبار سے کہ اس قول کی نسبت الی الحاکم ہو تو ایجاب اگر اس کی نسبت الی فعل المکلف ہو تو اس کا نام وجوب ہے بہر حال حقیقتاً یہ نفس خطاب کا نام ہے لہذا ما خوطب یہ کی تاویل کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ۔ فلذلك یعنی چونکہ ایجاب و جوب میں ذاتاً اتحاد ہے اس لئے یہ حضرات اقسام حکم کبھی وجوب و حرمت اور کبھی ایجاب و تحریم اور کبھی وجوب تحریم قرار دیتے ہیں جیسے اصول ابن حاجب میں ہے۔
الثاني انه غير منعکس تعریف حکم پر یہ دوسرا اعتراض ہے یعنی یہ تعریف جامع بجميع الافراد نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس تعریف میں افعال مکلفین کا لفظ موجود ہے وہ احکام جو غیر مکلفین کے افعال کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں مثلاً جو احکام افعال صبیان کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں وہ اس تعریف سے خارج ہو یہ ہے ہیں حالانکہ وہ بھی افراد حکم میں ہیں۔ فالا ولی ان یقال تو بہتر یہ تھا کہ افعال مکلفین کی بجائے افعال العباد کہنا چاہئے تھا ۔ وقد اجيب عن ذلك في كتبهم الى كتب الاشاعره بان الاحكام یعنی وہ احکام جن کے متعلق یہ خیال گذرتا ہے کہ یہ فعل صبح کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں وہ حقیقتاً فعل صبح کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں بلکہ فعل ولی کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتے ہیں جیسے ولی پر ہی واجب ہے کہ وہ مال صبی سے حقوق ادا کرے اور ولی تو مکلف ہے لہذا متعلق با فعال المکلفین ہو گئے۔
وردة المصنف أو لا مصنف نے اولاً اس جواب کو بایں طور رد کیا کہ صبی کی بیع کا جائز ہوتا جب کہ اس کو ولی سے اذن حاصل ہو ۔ صحة اسلامہ یعنی اسلامی اعمال کا مع الاقرار ادا کرنا كما هو مذكور معنى الاسلام فی الحدیث اسی طرح صحت صلوٰۃ اور اس کا مندوب ہونا یہ تمام امور ایسے ہیں جو براہ راست صبح کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں اور ان امور میں ولی کو کوئی دخل بھی نہیں ہے تو تعلق بفعل الولی کا جواب کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے و ثانیا یعنی ثانیا اس جواب کو رد کرتے ہوئے کہا تعلق الحق بمال الصبی اور تعلق حق بذمہ صبی یہ ایک ایسی شئی ہے جس کا تعلق صبح کے ساتھ ہے اور پھر اس کے بعد ولی کا ادا کرنا ایک ایسا حکم ہے جو اس پر مرتب ہے اس کا عین نہیں ہے تو اعتراض ان امور کے متعلق تھا جن کا تعلق صیبی سے ہے لہذا ان کے متعلق تعلق بفعل الولی کا حجاب درست نہیں ہے۔
ولا يتأتى هذا السوال شارح یہاں سے رد على المصنف کر رہا ہے کہ فعل صبی کا سوال کرے سے ان اشاعرہ پر واقع ہی نہیں ہوتا جنہوں نے حکم کی تعریف مذکور کی ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک کوئی حکم متعلق بالصبی ہے ہی نہیں بجز اداء الحق من مالہ کے اور یہ ادائے حق ولی کے ذمہ ہے نہ کہ بذمہ صبی لہذا تعریف حکم پر اعتراض بفعل الصبی بے فائدہ ہے ۔
تو لا یخفی پھر یہ بھی مخفی نہیں ہے کہ تعلق الحق بمالہ وذمتہ کسی صورت میں حکم ہو ہی نہیں سکتا کیونکہ اس کا تعلق بالا فعال نہیں ہے اگرچہ المکلفین کے بجائے العباد لے آئیں تو داخل فی الحکم نہیں ہو سکتا جب یہ افراد محدود سے نہیں ہے تو اس کو داخل تحت المحد کر نیکی سعی فضول و عبث ہے وبان الصحة والفساد مصنف نے جواز بیع و صحتہ اسلام صبح کے متعلق کہا تھا کہ اس کا تعلق بفعل ولی نہیں ہے تو اس کے متعلق شارح رد کر رہا ہے کہ صحت و فساد سرے سے احکام شرعیہ میں سے نہیں ہیں بلکہ یہ احکام عقلیہ ہیں کیونکہ صحت کا مفہوم کون الماتی به موافقا لما ورد به الشرع ہے یعنی جو چیز لائی گئی ہے اور ادا کی گئی اگر یہ موافق شریعت ہے تو اس کا نام صحتہ ہے اگر مخالف ہے تو
First: The intended meaning (maqsud) was the definition of hukm as it is used by jurists, which is that which is established by address (thabit bil-khitab). They call wujub and hurmah, which are attributes of the action of the mukallaf, hukm. The jurists do not call the address itself, which is an attribute of Allah, hukm. In summary, what was intended was not defined; what was defined was not intended.
It was answered with several aspects. First: Just as the application of hukm to thabit bil-khitab is not in the مصدری sense, but the intended meaning is ma hukim (the thing judged), similarly in the definition of hukm, the word khitab means ma khutib bihi (that which is addressed with) by rational indication. Second: In reality, hukm is not the name for wujub and hurmah, but for ijab and tahrim, which are among the attributes of Allah. So using the word khitab in its definition is correct, and there is no need to interpret it as ma khutib bihi. Wujub and hurmah are called hukm metaphorically because they are effects of ijab and tahrim. Third: Hukm is itself the name of the address of Allah. Because ijab is the saying 'Do', but from this saying no real attribute subsists in the action of the mukallaf. Since this saying relates to a non-existent thing, no attribute derived from the saying subsists for its subject. So this saying, the address itself, is hukm. When attributed to the ruler (hakim), it is called ijab; when attributed to the action about which the saying occurred, it is called wujub. So wujub and ijab are not essentially one thing, but both are identical with the saying 'Do', differing only by consideration. Therefore, there is no need for interpretation. Hence, in defining hukm, sometimes wujub/hurmah, sometimes ijab/tahrim, and sometimes wujub/tahrim are used.
Second objection: The definition is not comprehensive (ghayr mun'akis). It is not inclusive of all individuals because it includes the word 'acts of mukallafun'. Those rulings that relate to the acts of non-mukallafs, such as rulings related to the acts of minors, are excluded from this definition, even though they are also instances of hukm. So it would be better to say 'acts of servants' instead of 'acts of mukallaf'. It has been answered in the books of the Ash'aris that those rulings thought to relate to the action of a minor actually relate to the action of the guardian. For example, it is obligatory on the guardian to discharge rights from the minor's property. Since the guardian is mukallaf, the ruling relates to the acts of the mukallaf.
The author (musannif) refuted this answer: First, the permissibility of a minor's sale when he has permission from the guardian; the validity of his Islam (performance of Islamic acts with acknowledgment) as mentioned in the hadith; similarly, the validity of his prayer and its being recommended – all these directly relate to the minor, and the guardian has no role in them. So how can the answer that it relates to the guardian's act be correct? Second, the attachment of a right to the minor's property and the attachment of a right to the minor's liability are things that relate to the minor. Afterwards, the guardian's performance is a ruling that is consequent to it, not the same as it. The objection concerned those matters that relate to the minor, so the answer of relation to the guardian's act is not correct for them.
The commentator (sharih) says: This objection about the act of the minor does not even arise against those Ash'aris who defined hukm as mentioned, because in their view there is no ruling relating to the minor except the discharge of a right from his property, and this discharge is the responsibility of the guardian, not the minor. Therefore, objecting to the definition with the act of the minor is pointless.
Then it is not hidden that the attachment of a right to one's property and liability can never be hukm because it does not relate to acts. Even if we substitute 'servants' for 'mukallafun', it cannot be included in hukm. Since this is not a limited class, attempting to include it under a limited class is futile. And regarding validity and invalidity: The author said that the permissibility of a sale and validity of Islam relate to the minor and not to the guardian. The commentator responds that validity and invalidity are not among the shari' rulings at all; rather, they are rational rulings. Because the meaning of validity is correspondence to what has been brought by the law. So if a thing brought and performed is in accordance with the law, it is called valid; if contrary, invalid.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the definition of hukm (حكم). The author presents a definition commonly used among jurists: 'hukm is that which is established by address (khitab), such as obligation and prohibition which are attributes of the action of the mukallaf'. The first objection is that this definition misses the intended meaning: jurists actually use hukm for the attributes of the action (e.g., wujub), not for the address itself. Three Hanafi responses are given: (1) The word 'khitab' in the definition is interpreted as 'that which is addressed with' (ma khutib bihi) by rational context. (2) Hukm in reality is ijab and tahrim (divine acts of imposing obligation/prohibition), and wujub/hurmah are their effects, called hukm metaphorically. (3) Hukm is identical to the address itself, but different attributions (to Allah as ijab, to the action as wujub). The second objection is that the definition excludes rulings concerning minors (e.g., validity of their acts). Ash'aris answer that such rulings actually relate to the guardian. The author refutes this with examples: a minor's sale with permission, validity of his Islam, prayer—these directly concern the minor. The commentator (sharih) then defends the Ash'ari definition, stating that validity/invalidity are not shari' rulings but rational, and that the objection does not apply to Ash'aris who consider only the guardian's acts. The passage ends by noting that even substituting 'servants' does not help because rights attached to property/liability are not rulings about acts.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The term is debated: the passage defines it either as thabit bil-khitab (what is established by address) or as the address itself (khitab Allah). The author leans toward the former (Hanafi usage), but the commentator defends the latter (Ash'ari).
خطاب (khitab): The divine address (speech of Allah) that contains a command, prohibition, or permissibility.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation – the attribute of an action that makes it required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in the passage, what is the primary meaning of 'hukm'?
A) The divine address itself (khitab Allah)
B) The attributes of actions like wujub and hurmah
C) The act of imposing obligation (ijab)
D) The rational validity of an act

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm is not merely semantic; it reflects deeper usul principles about the relationship between divine speech and human obligations.
