The Redundancy Objection to 'Amaliyyah in the Definition of Fiqh
Refuting redundancy claim of 'amaliyyah qualifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the objection that the qualifier 'amaliyyah is redundant in the definition of fiqh and explain why it arises when 'hukm' is taken terminologically.

Core Idea
If 'hukm' means divine address, 'amaliyyah is redundant: 'shar'iyyah' already excludes beliefs.

In defining fiqh as 'knowledge of practical shar'i rulings', each term is scrutinized. A key objection is that 'amaliyyah (practical) is unnecessary. This passage examines that objection and the commentator's refutation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms in the definition
The definition of fiqh includes 'shar'iyyah' (dependent on revelation) and 'amaliyyah' (relating to acts of limbs). Understand each qualifier's role: shar'iyyah excludes purely rational obligations; amaliyyah excludes theoretical rulings and beliefs.
Belief in the Prophet is not dependent on revelation—it is rationally known.
2
Understand the terminological meaning of 'hukm'
The objection arises when 'hukm' is taken as 'khiṭāb Allāh al-muta‘alliq bi af‘āl al-mukallafīn' (divine address related to actions of the legally responsible person). In this sense, hukm covers only rulings communicated via revelation.
This is the standard usul definition of hukm.
3
Trace the redundancy claim
If 'hukm' is divine address, then 'shar'iyyah' already excludes matters known by reason (like the obligation of belief in the Prophet). So 'amaliyyah seems to repeat that exclusion. Additionally, theoretical rulings like 'ijmā‘ is a proof' are not even part of technical hukm because they lack requirement (iqtiḍā’) or option (takhyīr). Hence 'amaliyyah has no work—it is redundant.
The objector argues that 'amaliyyah is either redundant (for beliefs) or unnecessary (for theoretical rulings).
4
Analyze the commentator's rejection
The commentator (al-Shāriḥ) strengthens the objection by showing that theoretical rulings are not inside technical hukm at all. Thus 'amaliyyah cannot even serve to exclude them; it remains redundant.
This deepens the critique of the definition.

متعلق بفعل الجوارح نہیں ہیں انہیں خارج کر دے گی ۔ ولقائل ان يقول اذا حمل الحکو مصنف نے عملیہ کی قید کو تکرار سے بچانے کے لئے جو جواب دیا ہے قاتل کا یہ اعتراض اسی پر ہے خلاصہ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ فقہ کی اس وقت شرعیہ کا معنی ما توقف علی الشرع تھا لکما مر سابقا اور ایمان اور تصدیق بالنبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام چونکہ موقوف على الشرع نہیں ہیں لہذا یہ قید شرعیہ سے خارج ہو جائیں گے عملیہ کی قید کو ان کے لئے مخرج بنانا تحصیل حاصل اور اخراج مخرج ہے اس صورت میں مصنف نے حکم شرعی کو دو قسم بنایا تھا ایک نظری جیسے اجماع کا حجت ہونا اور دوسرا عملی تو عملیہ کی قید کے ساتھ اس وقت احکام نظریہ کا اخراج کیا تھا تو شارح نے اس کو رد کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ مثل كون الاجماع حجة 4 یہ خود حکم مصطلح میں داخل نہیں ہے کیونکہ حکم مصطلح میں جو قید بالاقتضاء والتخییر ہے وہ اس کے لئے مخرج ہے اس لئے عملیہ کی قید کا بجز تکرار کے اور کوئی فائدہ معتد بہا نہیں لایقال یہ شارح کے رد کا جواب دینے کی کوشش ہے جس کو شارح رد کرنا چاہتا ہے حاصل یہ ہے کہ سنت اور اجماع وقیاس کے حج ہونے کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ ان کے مقتضیٰ پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے لہذا یہ اقتضا ضمنی میں داخل ہو جائیں گے تو اس پر لانا نقول سے رد کر دیا کہ پھر قید عملیہ سے خارج نہیں ہوں گے کیونکہ جب ان کے مقتضا پر عمل کرنا واجب ہوا تو یہ احکام عملیہ میں داخل ہو جائیں گے پھر اخراج کیسے صحیح ہوگا ۔ و يمكن ان يقال سے شارح نے عملیہ کو مکرر ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے یہ توجیہ کر دی کہ ہو سکتا ہے جواز الا جائے اور وجوب قیاس حکم شرعی ہیں لیکن عملی نہیں ہیں لہذا عملیہ کے ساتھ ان کا اخراج ہو سکتا ہے اور بعض حضرات نے پہلے جواب کو یعنی یہ کہ سنت اور اجماع کے مقتضا پر عمل کرنا واجب ہے اس کا معنی یہ لیا ہے کہ وجوب العمل بمقتضاها سے مراد وجوب الاستدلال بہا والافتاء بموجبها یعنی مسائل پر ان سے استدلال کرنا واجب ہے اور اس کے موجب وہ مقتضا کے موافق فتویٰ دینا لازم ہے تو یہ امر عملیات سے نہیں لہذا عملیہ کی قید اس صورت میں ان کے لئے مخرج ہو جائے گی۔
It is either an act of the heart or of the limbs, so the obligation of belief and the obligation of consideration will fall under 'ruling', and 'amaliyyah refers to acts specific to the limbs, so the qualifier 'amaliyyah will not be redundant; rather, it will exclude from the definition of fiqh the obligation of belief etc., which are not related to acts of the limbs. And one may object: when 'ruling' is interpreted terminologically as the address of Allah related to actions, then the 'amaliyyah qualifier is indeed repeated because the obligation of belief would be excluded by the qualifier 'shar'iyyah', since when 'ruling' is meant terminologically, 'shar'iyyah' means that which depends on the Law, as previously mentioned, and belief and affirmation of the Prophet (peace be upon him) are not dependent on the Law, so they are excluded by the 'shar'iyyah' qualifier. Making the 'amaliyyah qualifier a means of excluding them is redundant. In this case the author had divided the shar'i ruling into two types: one theoretical, like ijmā' being a proof, and the other practical. So with the 'amaliyyah qualifier he excluded theoretical rulings. Then the commentator rejected this, saying that such as ijmā' being a proof is not itself included in the technical ruling, because the technical ruling has the qualifier of requirement and option which excludes it, so the 'amaliyyah qualifier has no benefit besides repetition. This is an attempt to answer the commentator's rejection, which the commentator wants to refute. The summary is that the purpose of the Sunnah, ijmā', and qiyās being proofs is that acting upon their implications is obligatory, so they fall under implicit requirement. Then it is refuted by saying that they would not be excluded by the 'amaliyyah qualifier, because when acting upon their implications is obligatory, they become practical rulings, so how can exclusion be valid? And it can be said that the commentator offered this justification to save 'amaliyyah from being redundant: that perhaps the permissibility and obligation of qiyās are shar'i rulings but not practical, so their exclusion by 'amaliyyah is possible. And some have taken the earlier response—that acting upon the implications of Sunnah and ijmā' is obligatory—to mean that 'obligation of acting upon their implications' refers to the obligation of using them as evidence and giving fatwas accordingly, i.e., it is obligatory to deduce from them issues and to give fatwa in accordance with their implications, and this is not among practical matters, so the 'amaliyyah qualifier would be a mukhrij for them in this case.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of fiqh, addressing an objection that the qualifier 'amaliyyah (practical) is redundant. The objection arises if 'hukm' in the definition is taken in its terminological sense as 'the address of Allah related to actions of the mukallaf' (khiṭāb Allāh al-muta‘alliq). In that case, the qualifier 'shar'iyyah' already excludes matters known by reason (like wujūb al-īmān, the obligation of belief), because belief in the Prophet is not dependent on divine address (it is known by reason). Thus, the 'amaliyyah qualifier appears to be a repetition for those matters, and it also attempts to exclude theoretical rulings like 'ijmā‘ is a proof'. But the commentator (al-Shāriḥ) argues that such theoretical rulings are not even part of the technical term 'hukm' in the first place, because 'hukm' in its technical sense is restricted to requiring or giving an option (iqtiḍā’ or takhyīr), and theoretical rulings do not fit that; so excluding them via 'amaliyyah is unnecessary, making 'amaliyyah redundant. The text then presents two responses: (1) one could say that even theoretical rulings imply an obligation to act upon their implications, so they are implicitly part of 'hukm', but then the objection that they become practical rulings and thus not excluded by 'amaliyyah arises. (2) Alternatively, some scholars reinterpret 'obligation of acting upon their implications' as the obligation to use them as evidence and issue fatwas, which is not a practical ruling of an act itself, so 'amaliyyah can exclude them after all. The passage follows the Hanafi usage of terms: 'amaliyyah refers to acts of the limbs, and 'shar'iyyah' means dependent on revelation. The commentary aims to preserve the definition of fiqh as knowledge of practical shar'i rulings without redundancy.

Key Terms
حکم شرعی (ḥukm shar‘ī): Two types: theoretical (naẓarī) like ijmā‘ being a proof, and practical (‘amalī) like wajib acts.
عملیہ (‘amaliyyah): Pertaining to acts of the limbs (jawaarih), not beliefs.
نظری (naẓarī): Theoretical ruling such as the proof-value of ijmā‘ or qiyās.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main objection against the 'amaliyyah qualifier in the definition of fiqh?
A) It is too broad and includes irrational rulings.
B) It becomes redundant if 'hukm' is defined terminologically as divine address.
C) It excludes too many practical rulings.
D) It contradicts the principle of ijmā‘.

Key Takeaway
The redundancy objection to 'amaliyyah is based on a narrow interpretation of 'hukm'; responses must either broaden the concept of hukm or reinterpret the work of 'amaliyyah.

Deriving the Four Sources: Two Logical Divisions
Classification of legal proofs into four using two logical divisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply two methods (revelation/non-revelation and Prophetic/non-Prophetic) to classify any shar'i evidence as Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', or Qiyas.

Core Idea
All shar'i evidence is either revelation or non-revelation; both branches subdivide into the four sources.

This passage presents two systematic ways to delimit the four sources of Islamic law. Understanding these divisions is foundational to Hanafi usul al-fiqh, as it clarifies why only four are primary and how all other proofs are ultimately subordinate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the First Division
The passage first divides evidence into revelation (wahy) and non-revelation (ghayr wahy). Write down what each includes.
2
Subdivide Revelation
Revelation is either recited (Quran) or unrecited (Sunnah). Identify the key condition: miraculous wording for Quran.
3
Subdivide Non-Revelation
Non-revelation is either unanimous consensus of the entire Ummah (Ijma') or individual reasoning (Qiyas). Infallibility distinguishes them.
4
Apply the Second Division
Alternatively, evidence either originates from the Prophet or not. If from the Prophet, with miraculous wording (Quran) or not (Sunnah); if from others, with infallibility (Ijma') or not (Qiyas).
5
Practice Classification
Given a specific proof (e.g., a hadith or a ruling based on analogy), trace it through both divisions to confirm its category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یعنی بیان مصادیق جو کہ بحکم استقرار منحصر فی الا ربعہ ہیں۔ وجہ ضبطہ یہ دلیل حصر ہے حاصل یہ ہے کہ دلیل شرعی وحی ہوگی یا غیر وحی شق اول پر وحی اگر متلو ہو تو وہ کتاب اللہ ہے ورنہ تو وہ سنت ہے۔ والثانی یعنی غیر وحی اگر کسی عصر و زمان میں کل امت کا قول ہو تو اجماع ہے ورنہ تو قیاس او ان الدليل الخر یہ دوسری وجہ حضر ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دلیل ہماری طرف یا تو از جانب رسول علیہ الصلوٰۃ والسلام پہنچے گی پانہ پہلی شق پر اگر اس کی نظم و عبارت کے ساتھ تعلق اعجاز ہو یعنی اس کی نظم معجز ہو جس کی مثل پیش کرنے سے جمیع انسان عاجز ہوں تو وہ کتاب اللہ ہے اگر اس کی نظم معجز نہ ہو تو وہ سنت ہے والثانی یعنی جو دلیل از جانب رسول علیہ الصلوة و السلام نہیں پہنچی بلکہ دوسرے اشخاص کی جانب سے صادر ہوتی ہے تو پھر دیکھا جائے گا کہ جن اشخاص سے صادر ہوئی ہے ان کی عصمت عن الخطا شرط ہے تو وہ اجماع ہے لن تتجمع امنی علی ملالہ اور اگر عصمہ عن الخطا مشروط نہیں ہے تو وہ قیاس ہے المجتہد مخطی ویصيب واما شرائع من قبلنا الم اولا كو جواربعہ میں منحصر کیا گیا ہے اس پر اشکال وارد ہوتا تھا کہ ان ادلہ اربعہ کے علاوہ شرائع من قبلنا یعنی شريعة التوراة والانجيل جو محرف نہیں ہے وہ بھی دلیل احکام ہے اسی طرح تعامل بین العوام اور قول صحابی اور اس جیسی اور ایشیا، مثلاً ستحری۔ اخذ بالظاہر - اخذ بالاحتیاط یہ بھی تو حج و دلائل احکام ہیں تو حصر فی الاربعہ صحیح نہ ہوا تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ فراجعة الى الاربعة یعنی یہ اشیاء ان ادله اربعہ کی طرف راجع ہیں یہ ان کے علاوہ نہیں ہیں کیونکہ شرائع من قبلنا اس وقت حجت ہیں جب ان کو قرآن مجید یا حدیث رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام میں ان کا ذکر بلا انکار ہوا اگر قرآن مجید میں اس کا تذکرہ ہے تو پھر یہ استدلال بالکتاب ہوا اگر اس کا تذکرہ فی الحدیث والسنتہ ہے تو استدلال بالسنت ہو اور تعامل راجع الى الاجماع ہے بشرطیکہ تعامل بین القرون الفاضلہ ہو بلانکیر ولا عبرة بما يتعامل به بعد ذلک اور قول صحابی جو غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہے وہ راجع الی السنتہ ہے ورنہ تو وہ داخل فی القیاس ہے اور تحری و غیر با بھی ان کی طرف راجع ہے کیونکہ تحری کے اندر شہادت قلب ہوتی ہے تو یہ عمل بالحدیث و استفت قلبک ہے اور اخذ بالاحتیاط میں عمل با قومی الدلیلین ہوتا ہے اسی طرح اخذ بالظاہر میں بھی اخذ بظاہر الدلیل ہوتا ہے - وکی المعقول نوع استدلال یہ المعقول جس کو بعض حضرات نے نوع خامس من الادلہ قرار دیا ہے اور اس کا نام الاستدلال رکھا ہے یہ بھی درحقیقت راجع ہوتا ہے تمسک معقول النص یا بمعقول الاجماع کی طرف کیونکہ صرف خالص عقلی رائے کو کوئی دخل فی اثبات الاحکام نہیں ہے اور اس کی تفسیر یوں کی گئی ہے کہ یہ ایک ایسی دلیل ہے جو نص اور اجماع و قیاس شرعی کے علاوہ ہے اس کے انواع میں اختلاف ضرور ہے مالکیہ کے نزدیک مصالح مرسلہ کہا جاتا ہے حنفیہ استحسان کے نام سے موسوم کرتے ہیں ابن حاجب نے اس کو التلازم والاستصحاب کہا بہر حال ان اشیاء کا رجوع انہیں ادلہ اربعہ میں سے کسی کی طرف ضرور ہوتا ہے۔
That is, explanation of the particulars which, by virtue of established consensus, are confined to the four [sources]. The reason for this classification is that the legal evidence is either revelation or non-revelation. In the first branch, if revelation is recited, it is the Book of Allah; otherwise it is the Sunnah. In the second, i.e. non-revelation, if it is the saying of the entire Ummah in any era, it is Ijma'; otherwise it is Qiyas. And the other proof: that is the second way of limitation, whose gist is that the evidence reaches us either from the Messenger (peace be upon him) or not. In the first branch, if its wording is accompanied by miraculous inimitability, i.e. its composition is miraculous such that all humans are incapable of producing its like, then it is the Book of Allah; if its composition is not miraculous, then it is Sunnah. In the second, i.e. evidence that does not come from the Messenger but originates from other persons, then it will be seen whether those persons require infallibility from error: if yes, it is Ijma' — 'my Ummah will not agree on error' — and if infallibility is not required, then it is Qiyas — 'the mujtahid may err and may be correct'. As for the laws of those before us (sharā'i' man qablanā) and the like, the objection was raised that they are not included among the four, because besides these four there are the laws of those before us, i.e. the Torah and Gospel that are not distorted, which are also proof of rulings; similarly, the practice (ta'āmul) among the common people, the saying of a Companion, and other things like taharrī (seeking the correct ruling), akhdh bil-zāhir (taking by the apparent), akhdh bil-ihtiyāt (taking by precaution) — these are also proofs of rulings. So the limitation to four is not correct. The answer was given: they all revert to the four. That is, these matters refer to one of these four, they are not outside them. Because the laws of those before us are proof only when they are mentioned in the Qur'an or Hadith of the Messenger without rejection: if mentioned in the Qur'an, it is istidlāl bil-kitāb; if mentioned in the Hadith/Sunnah, it is istidlāl bis-sunnah. Practice (ta'āmul) reverts to Ijma', provided that the practice is among the virtuous generations without disapproval, and no consideration is given to practices that come after that. And the saying of a Companion that is not attainable by analogy reverts to Sunnah; otherwise it falls under Qiyas. And taharrī and others also revert to these because taharrī involves the testimony of the heart — it is acting on hadith and 'consult your heart' — and akhdh bil-ihtiyāt involves acting on the stronger of two evidences; similarly akhdh bil-zāhir involves acting on the apparent of the evidence. And the ma'qūl (rational deduction), which is a type of istidlāl that some have considered a fifth type of evidence and named it istidlāl — this also in reality reverts to the rationale of the text or the rationale of Ijma', because pure rational opinion has no role in establishing rulings. Its interpretation is that it is a proof other than text, Ijma', and shar'i Qiyas. There is indeed difference in its types: the Malikis call it al-masālih al-mursalah, the Hanafis call it istihsān, and Ibn al-Hājib called it al-talāzum wal-istishāb. In any case, these matters necessarily revert to one of the four proofs.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the limitation of the sources of Islamic law (adillah) to four: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. The author first presents two ways to delimit these four: the first divides evidence into revelation (wahy) vs. non-revelation; revelation is either recited (Quran) or not (Sunnah), and non-revelation is either consensus of the entire ummah (Ijma') or individual reasoning (Qiyas). The second division is based on whether the evidence comes from the Prophet or not; if from the Prophet, it is either miraculous in wording (Quran) or not (Sunnah); if from others, it requires infallibility for Ijma' or not for Qiyas. Then the author addresses the objection that other proofs exist, such as the laws of previous prophets (sharā'i' man qablanā), the practices of people (ta'āmul), sayings of companions, taharrī (seeking the soundest opinion), akhdh bil-zāhir (apparent meaning), akhdh bil-ihtiyāt (precaution), and ma'qūl (rational deduction). The answer is that all these revert to one of the four main sources. For example, previous laws are valid only if mentioned in Quran or Sunnah. Ta'āmul reverts to Ijma' if it is the practice of the virtuous predecessors with no disapproval. A companion's saying not deducible by analogy reverts to Sunnah; otherwise it falls under Qiyas. Taharrī and the like involve acting on hadith or weighing evidences, thus reverting to Sunnah or Qiyas. Even the so-called fifth source (istidlāl) is actually based on the rationale of text or Ijma', as pure reason has no authority. Thus the limitation to four sources remains intact.

Key Terms
الاستدلال (al-istidlāl): A proof that relies on the rationale (ma'qūl) of a text or consensus, distinct from pure reason.
شرائع من قبلنا (sharā'i' man qablanā): Laws revealed to prophets before Muhammad (PBUH), which are binding only if confirmed without rejection in Quran or Sunnah.
تعامل (ta'āmul): Common practice among people; it serves as evidence only if it is the practice of the virtuous generations without disapproval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first division in the passage, if a legal evidence is classified as 'non-revelation' (ghayr wahy), what are the two possible categories it can fall into?
A) Quran and Sunnah
B) Ijma' and Qiyas
C) Sunnah and Ijma'
D) Quran and Qiyas

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification logically deduces the four sources of law from two fundamental divisions: revelation/non-revelation and Prophetic/non-Prophetic.

All Other Proofs Revert to the Four Sources
Rebuttal of additional sources and their reversion to the four

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how shar' man qablana, ta'amul, qawl sahabi, taharri, akhdh bil-zahir, akhdh bil-ihtiyat, and istidlal revert to the four primary sources according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Every apparent proof beyond the four returns to one of them: previous laws via Quran/Sunnah, practice via Ijma', companion sayings via Sunnah or Qiyas, and rational deduction via text or Ijma'.

While the four sources are primary, some proofs appear additional. This lesson addresses that objection and demonstrates that every such proof ultimately reverts to one of the four. Understanding this reversion is crucial for maintaining the systematic unity of Hanafi usul and avoiding methodological errors.

Guided Path
1
List the Additional Proofs
From the passage, identify: shar' man qablana, ta'amul, qawl sahabi, taharri, akhdh bil-zahir, akhdh bil-ihtiyat, and istidlal.
2
Trace Each Proof to a Primary Source
For each, determine which of the four (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) it reverts to, based on the passage's reasoning.
Shar' man qablana: reverts to Quran or Sunnah if mentioned without rejection. Ta'amul: reverts to Ijma' if from virtuous generations. Qawl sahabi: if not analogical, reverts to Sunnah; otherwise Qiyas. Taharri: acts on hadith, thus Sunnah. Akhdh bil-zahir: acts on apparent evidence, thus Sunnah or Qiyas. Akhdh bil-ihtiyat: acts on stronger evidence, thus relevant source. Istidlal: ma'qul of text or Ijma'.
3
Understand the Reversion Mechanism
The passage shows that these proofs are not independent; they depend on textual or consensus-based criteria.
4
Apply to a New Example
Given a ruling based on the practice of the people of Madinah, explain its reversion according to Hanafi view.
Hanafis do not accept it as independent; it would revert to Ijma' if it was the practice of the virtuous generations without disapproval.

یعنی بیان مصادیق جو کہ بحکم استقرار منحصر فی الا ربعہ ہیں۔ وجہ ضبطہ یہ دلیل حصر ہے حاصل یہ ہے کہ دلیل شرعی وحی ہوگی یا غیر وحی شق اول پر وحی اگر متلو ہو تو وہ کتاب اللہ ہے ورنہ تو وہ سنت ہے۔ والثانی یعنی غیر وحی اگر کسی عصر و زمان میں کل امت کا قول ہو تو اجماع ہے ورنہ تو قیاس او ان الدليل الخر یہ دوسری وجہ حضر ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دلیل ہماری طرف یا تو از جانب رسول علیہ الصلوٰۃ والسلام پہنچے گی پانہ پہلی شق پر اگر اس کی نظم و عبارت کے ساتھ تعلق اعجاز ہو یعنی اس کی نظم معجز ہو جس کی مثل پیش کرنے سے جمیع انسان عاجز ہوں تو وہ کتاب اللہ ہے اگر اس کی نظم معجز نہ ہو تو وہ سنت ہے والثانی یعنی جو دلیل از جانب رسول علیہ الصلوة و السلام نہیں پہنچی بلکہ دوسرے اشخاص کی جانب سے صادر ہوتی ہے تو پھر دیکھا جائے گا کہ جن اشخاص سے صادر ہوئی ہے ان کی عصمت عن الخطا شرط ہے تو وہ اجماع ہے لن تتجمع امنی علی ملالہ اور اگر عصمہ عن الخطا مشروط نہیں ہے تو وہ قیاس ہے المجتہد مخطی ویصيب واما شرائع من قبلنا الم اولا كو جواربعہ میں منحصر کیا گیا ہے اس پر اشکال وارد ہوتا تھا کہ ان ادلہ اربعہ کے علاوہ شرائع من قبلنا یعنی شريعة التوراة والانجيل جو محرف نہیں ہے وہ بھی دلیل احکام ہے اسی طرح تعامل بین العوام اور قول صحابی اور اس جیسی اور ایشیا، مثلاً ستحری۔ اخذ بالظاہر - اخذ بالاحتیاط یہ بھی تو حج و دلائل احکام ہیں تو حصر فی الاربعہ صحیح نہ ہوا تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ فراجعة الى الاربعة یعنی یہ اشیاء ان ادله اربعہ کی طرف راجع ہیں یہ ان کے علاوہ نہیں ہیں کیونکہ شرائع من قبلنا اس وقت حجت ہیں جب ان کو قرآن مجید یا حدیث رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام میں ان کا ذکر بلا انکار ہوا اگر قرآن مجید میں اس کا تذکرہ ہے تو پھر یہ استدلال بالکتاب ہوا اگر اس کا تذکرہ فی الحدیث والسنتہ ہے تو استدلال بالسنت ہو اور تعامل راجع الى الاجماع ہے بشرطیکہ تعامل بین القرون الفاضلہ ہو بلانکیر ولا عبرة بما يتعامل به بعد ذلک اور قول صحابی جو غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہے وہ راجع الی السنتہ ہے ورنہ تو وہ داخل فی القیاس ہے اور تحری و غیر با بھی ان کی طرف راجع ہے کیونکہ تحری کے اندر شہادت قلب ہوتی ہے تو یہ عمل بالحدیث و استفت قلبک ہے اور اخذ بالاحتیاط میں عمل با قومی الدلیلین ہوتا ہے اسی طرح اخذ بالظاہر میں بھی اخذ بظاہر الدلیل ہوتا ہے - وکی المعقول نوع استدلال یہ المعقول جس کو بعض حضرات نے نوع خامس من الادلہ قرار دیا ہے اور اس کا نام الاستدلال رکھا ہے یہ بھی درحقیقت راجع ہوتا ہے تمسک معقول النص یا بمعقول الاجماع کی طرف کیونکہ صرف خالص عقلی رائے کو کوئی دخل فی اثبات الاحکام نہیں ہے اور اس کی تفسیر یوں کی گئی ہے کہ یہ ایک ایسی دلیل ہے جو نص اور اجماع و قیاس شرعی کے علاوہ ہے اس کے انواع میں اختلاف ضرور ہے مالکیہ کے نزدیک مصالح مرسلہ کہا جاتا ہے حنفیہ استحسان کے نام سے موسوم کرتے ہیں ابن حاجب نے اس کو التلازم والاستصحاب کہا بہر حال ان اشیاء کا رجوع انہیں ادلہ اربعہ میں سے کسی کی طرف ضرور ہوتا ہے۔
That is, explanation of the particulars which, by virtue of established consensus, are confined to the four [sources]. The reason for this classification is that the legal evidence is either revelation or non-revelation. In the first branch, if revelation is recited, it is the Book of Allah; otherwise it is the Sunnah. In the second, i.e. non-revelation, if it is the saying of the entire Ummah in any era, it is Ijma'; otherwise it is Qiyas. And the other proof: that is the second way of limitation, whose gist is that the evidence reaches us either from the Messenger (peace be upon him) or not. In the first branch, if its wording is accompanied by miraculous inimitability, i.e. its composition is miraculous such that all humans are incapable of producing its like, then it is the Book of Allah; if its composition is not miraculous, then it is Sunnah. In the second, i.e. evidence that does not come from the Messenger but originates from other persons, then it will be seen whether those persons require infallibility from error: if yes, it is Ijma' — 'my Ummah will not agree on error' — and if infallibility is not required, then it is Qiyas — 'the mujtahid may err and may be correct'. As for the laws of those before us (sharā'i' man qablanā) and the like, the objection was raised that they are not included among the four, because besides these four there are the laws of those before us, i.e. the Torah and Gospel that are not distorted, which are also proof of rulings; similarly, the practice (ta'āmul) among the common people, the saying of a Companion, and other things like taharrī (seeking the correct ruling), akhdh bil-zāhir (taking by the apparent), akhdh bil-ihtiyāt (taking by precaution) — these are also proofs of rulings. So the limitation to four is not correct. The answer was given: they all revert to the four. That is, these matters refer to one of these four, they are not outside them. Because the laws of those before us are proof only when they are mentioned in the Qur'an or Hadith of the Messenger without rejection: if mentioned in the Qur'an, it is istidlāl bil-kitāb; if mentioned in the Hadith/Sunnah, it is istidlāl bis-sunnah. Practice (ta'āmul) reverts to Ijma', provided that the practice is among the virtuous generations without disapproval, and no consideration is given to practices that come after that. And the saying of a Companion that is not attainable by analogy reverts to Sunnah; otherwise it falls under Qiyas. And taharrī and others also revert to these because taharrī involves the testimony of the heart — it is acting on hadith and 'consult your heart' — and akhdh bil-ihtiyāt involves acting on the stronger of two evidences; similarly akhdh bil-zāhir involves acting on the apparent of the evidence. And the ma'qūl (rational deduction), which is a type of istidlāl that some have considered a fifth type of evidence and named it istidlāl — this also in reality reverts to the rationale of the text or the rationale of Ijma', because pure rational opinion has no role in establishing rulings. Its interpretation is that it is a proof other than text, Ijma', and shar'i Qiyas. There is indeed difference in its types: the Malikis call it al-masālih al-mursalah, the Hanafis call it istihsān, and Ibn al-Hājib called it al-talāzum wal-istishāb. In any case, these matters necessarily revert to one of the four proofs.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the limitation of the sources of Islamic law (adillah) to four: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. The author first presents two ways to delimit these four: the first divides evidence into revelation (wahy) vs. non-revelation; revelation is either recited (Quran) or not (Sunnah), and non-revelation is either consensus of the entire ummah (Ijma') or individual reasoning (Qiyas). The second division is based on whether the evidence comes from the Prophet or not; if from the Prophet, it is either miraculous in wording (Quran) or not (Sunnah); if from others, it requires infallibility for Ijma' or not for Qiyas. Then the author addresses the objection that other proofs exist, such as the laws of previous prophets (sharā'i' man qablanā), the practices of people (ta'āmul), sayings of companions, taharrī (seeking the soundest opinion), akhdh bil-zāhir (apparent meaning), akhdh bil-ihtiyāt (precaution), and ma'qūl (rational deduction). The answer is that all these revert to one of the four main sources. For example, previous laws are valid only if mentioned in Quran or Sunnah. Ta'āmul reverts to Ijma' if it is the practice of the virtuous predecessors with no disapproval. A companion's saying not deducible by analogy reverts to Sunnah; otherwise it falls under Qiyas. Taharrī and the like involve acting on hadith or weighing evidences, thus reverting to Sunnah or Qiyas. Even the so-called fifth source (istidlāl) is actually based on the rationale of text or Ijma', as pure reason has no authority. Thus the limitation to four sources remains intact.

Key Terms
الاستدلال (al-istidlāl): A proof that relies on the rationale (ma'qūl) of a text or consensus, distinct from pure reason.
شرائع من قبلنا (sharā'i' man qablanā): Laws revealed to prophets before Muhammad (PBUH), which are binding only if confirmed without rejection in Quran or Sunnah.
تعامل (ta'āmul): Common practice among people; it serves as evidence only if it is the practice of the virtuous generations without disapproval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the practice (ta'amul) of people is only valid as legal evidence if it is the practice of which group?
A) The common people at any time
B) The virtuous generations (qurun fadilah) without disapproval
C) The scholars of a particular region
D) The Companions only

Key Takeaway
All additional legal proofs are not independent; they revert to the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', or Qiyas, preserving the four-source structure.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Definition of Usul al-Fiqh and the Meaning of Qā'ida
Commentary on the definition of usul al-fiqh and qāʿida

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define usul al-fiqh as the science of universal rules that provide proximate access to fiqh with verification, and explain why Arabic grammar and theology are excluded from this definition.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules that give proximate access to fiqh with verification.

This passage from al-Tawḍīḥ and its commentary al-Talwīḥ clarifies the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh. After defining it as a relational compound, the author now defines it as a title for a specific science: knowledge of universal rules (qawāʿid) through which one reaches fiqh with verification. The commentary then explains key qualifiers: 'proximate access' excludes preliminary disciplines like grammar and theology, and 'with verification' excludes mere debate. This lesson will help you internalize the precise scope of uṣūl al-fiqh and understand the foundational concept of a qāʿida.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of usul al-fiqh
Read the opening sentences. The author states that usul al-fiqh is 'knowledge of rules through which access to fiqh is achieved with verification.' Note that the definition now treats usul al-fiqh as a science, not a relational compound.
The word 'rules' (qawāʿid) is key; it refers to universal propositions.
2
Analyze the qualifier 'proximate access'
The text says 'proximate access' (tawassul qarīb) excludes disciplines like Arabic grammar and theology. These are only preliminaries (mabādī) that lead to fiqh through an intermediary, so they are remote, not proximate.
The reason: grammar helps understand word indications, theology establishes authenticity of sources; both are steps before actual derivation.
3
Analyze the qualifier 'with verification'
The text says 'with verification' (ʿalā wajh al-taḥqīq) excludes the science of debate (jadal) which aims to compel an opponent (ilzām) rather than arrive at truth. Debate may use similar rules but its purpose differs.
This ensures usul al-fiqh is about genuine derivation, not polemical argumentation.
4
Understand the definition of qāʿida
The passage defines qāʿida as a universal ruling (ḥukm kullī) that applies to all its particulars, from which rulings of those particulars can be derived when needed. Example: 'Every ruling indicated by analogy is established' is a qāʿida that covers all analogically derived rulings.
This definition is crucial because usul al-fiqh is built upon such universal rules.

Source Text

قال المصنف في التوضيح ولما عرف أصول الفقه الا یعنی اصول فقہ کی باعتبار مرکب اضافی کے تعریف ہو چکی اب مصنف اس کی تعریف بایں اعتبار کر رہا ہے کہ وہ علم مخصوص کا لقب ہے فیقول علم اصول الفقه النج یعنی اصول فقہ ایسے قواعد کا علم ہے جن قواعد کے ساتھ فقہ تک توصل اور وصول على وجه التحقیق ہو جائے اى العلم بالقضايا الكلية یعنی قواعد سے مراد قضایا کلیہ ہیں جن کے ساتھ فقہ کی طرف توصل قریب حاصل ہو جائے توصل کے ساتھ قریب کی قید لگا کر مباری سے احترانہ کیا ۔ كالعربية يعنى علم بالقواعد العربية كالصرف والنحوي الكلام یعنی علم الکلام ان سے توصل قریب الی الفقہ حاصل نہیں لہذا یہ اصول فقہ سے خارج ہیں۔ وقولنا على وجه التحقيق احتر از اتم یعنی علی وجہ التحقیق سے ہمارا مقصود علم الخلاف والجدل سے احتراز کرنا ہے کیونکہ یہ علم اگر چہ ایسے قواعد پشتمل ہے جو موصل الى مسائل الفقہ ہیں لیکن علی وجہ التحقیق نہیں بلکہ علی وجہ الالزام ہے اور اس سے غرض صرف الزام خصم ہوتی ہے جیسے کہ وہ قواعد جو مذکورہ فی الارشاد و المقدمہ ہیں یہ دونوں اسماء کتب ہیں صرف نکت خلافیہ کو ان پر مبتنی کیا ہے ۔ قال الشارح في التلويح قوله وعلم اصول الفقه بعد ما تقر ریعنی جب یہ متقرر اور ثابت ہو چکا ہے کہ اصول فقہ علم مخصوص کا لقب ہے تو اس وقت لفظ علم کو اصول الفقہ کی طرف مضاف کر کے علم اصول الفقہ کہنے کی ضرورت نہیں تھی بلکہ صرف اصول الفقہ کہہ دینا کافی تھا الا ان ہاں مگر یہ کہ مقصود زیادہ بیان اور زیادہ توضیح ہو تو اس وضاحت کی خاطر کہ اصول الفقہ ایک علم ہے اس لئے اصافت کر دی جیسے شجر الار اک لفظ اراک پیلو کے درخت کو کہتے ہیں لہذا شجر کے مضاف کرنے کی ضرورت نہ تھی مگر بقصد زيادة توضیح اضافت کر دی گئی ہے۔ القاعدة حکم کلی چونکہ لفظ القواعد جمع تھی للقاعدہ اس لئے قاعدہ کی تعریف کی اور کہا ایک حکم کلی جو اپنے جمیع جزئیات پر منطبق ہو اور بوقت ضرورت ان جزئیات کے احکام اس حکم کلی سے معلوم کئے جا سکیں جیسے کل حکم دل علیہ القیاس فھو ثابت اس کے ساتھ جمیع احکام قیاسی کا ثبوت حاصل ہو سکتا ہے مثلاً کہا جائے گا ہذا الحکم دل علیہ القیاس کلما دل علیہ القیاس فھو ثابت تو نتیجہ ہو گا ہذا الحکم ثابت و التوصل القريب مستفاد یعنی توصل کے ساتھ جو قریب کی قید لگائی ہے وہ بجھا کی بار سببیت سے مستفاد ہے جو سببیہ قریبہ میں ظاہر و متبادر ہے دوسرا توصل الی الفقہ سے کیونکہ سبب قریب ہی موصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے اور سبب بعید موصل الى الواسطہ ہوتا ہے اور یہی واسطہ سبب قریب ہو کہ موصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے ۔ فيخرج العلم بقواعد العربية سببیہ قریبہ کے ساتھ علم بقواعد العربیہ و قواعد الکلام خارج ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ یہ دونوں مبادی ہیں برائے اصول فقہ اور ان کے ساتھ توصل الی الفقہ توصل قریب نہیں ہے کیونکہ قواعد عربیہ کے ساتھ توصل ہوتا ہے الى معرفة كيفية دلالة الالفاظ یعنی ان قواعد سے یہ حاصل ہوتا ہے کہ الفاظ کی دلالت علی مدلولاتها الوضعیہ کس قسم کی دلالت ہے مطابقی ہے یا تضمنی والتزامی اور پھر یہ دلالت علی سبیل الفا علیہ ہے یا علی سبیل المفعولية وغيرها - وبواسطة ذلك اور اسی کے واسطہ سے اقتدار علی استنباط الاحكام من الكتاب والسنة حاصل ہوتا - وكذا لك يتوصل بقواعد الکلام یعنی علم الکلام کے قواعد سے توصل الى ثبوت الكتاب والسنة حاصل ہوتا ہے یعنی ان قواعد کلامیہ سے کتاب اللہ کا کتاب اللہ ہونا اور سنہ کا سنتہ رسول ہونا اور ان کے صدق کا وجوب حاصل ہوتا جو علم الکلام کے مطابق عقائد نہیں رکھتا تو وہ کتاب اللہ کو اور سنہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو تسلیم نہیں کرے گا اور نہ ان کے صدق کا قائل ہو گا تو علم الکلام سے ان کا ثبوت حاصل ہوا پھر اس کے بعد ان کے ذریعہ توصل الی الفقہ ہوگا تو یہ توصل قریب نہ ہوا بلکہ بعید ہوا
The author said in al-Tawdih: When the definition of usul al-fiqh as a compound relational term has been given, now the author defines it as a title for a particular science, saying: 'The science of usul al-fiqh' means the knowledge of such rules through which access to and attainment of fiqh is achieved with verification. That is, knowledge of universal propositions. By 'rules' are meant universal propositions, through which proximate access to fiqh is attained. By specifying 'proximate', he excludes such things as Arabic grammar and theology, for they do not provide proximate access to fiqh, hence they are outside usul al-fiqh. And our saying 'with verification' is a complete exclusion, meaning we intend to exclude the science of argumentation and debate, for although it comprises rules that lead to fiqh issues, it does so not with verification but with binding (ilzām), its purpose being only to compel the opponent—like the rules mentioned in al-Irshād and al-Muqaddima, both book names, based solely on points of disagreement. The commentator said in al-Talwīh: 'His saying: And the science of usul al-fiqh, after it has been established that usul al-fiqh is a title for a particular science, there was no need to add the word 'science' and say 'science of usul al-fiqh'; rather, it was sufficient to say 'usul al-fiqh'. However, if the aim is greater clarity and elaboration, then for the sake of that clarification the idāfah was made, just as one says 'shajar al-ārāk'—the word 'ārāk' means the willow tree, so there was no need to add 'shajar', but it was added for greater clarity.' Al-qā'ida: a universal ruling. Since the word al-qawā'id is the plural of al-qā'ida, he defined it: A universal ruling that applies to all its particulars, and when needed the rulings of those particulars can be known from this universal ruling—like 'Every ruling that analogy indicates is established'; by this, the establishment of all analogical rulings can be attained. For example, one says: 'This ruling is indicated by analogy; whenever analogy indicates, it is established', so the result is 'This ruling is established.' And 'proximate access' is derived—meaning the qualification 'proximate' attached to 'access' is derived from causation, which in proximate causation is apparent and discernible. Secondly, from 'access to fiqh', because the proximate cause is the one that leads to fiqh, while the remote cause leads to an intermediary, which itself becomes the proximate cause leading to fiqh. Thus, the knowledge of Arabic rules and the rules of theology are excluded by the specification of proximate causation, because these are both preliminaries for usul al-fiqh, and through them access to fiqh is not proximate, for through Arabic rules one attains knowledge of how words indicate their meanings—whether the indication is conjunctive, implicative, or necessary, and whether this indication is on the basis of fa'iliyya or maf'ūliyya, etc.—and through that one gains the ability to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. Similarly, through the rules of theology one attains establishment of the Book and Sunnah—meaning that through these theological rules it is established that the Book of Allah is the Book of Allah and the Sunnah is the Sunnah of the Messenger, and the obligation of their truthfulness; one who does not hold beliefs in accordance with theology will not accept the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, nor will he affirm their truthfulness. So through theology their establishment is obtained, then after that through them access to fiqh is achieved, so this access is not proximate but remote.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of usul al-fiqh. It begins by noting that the previous definition was from the perspective of a relational compound, and now the author defines it as a title for a specific science: 'the science of usul al-fiqh' meaning knowledge of universal rules that enable one to reach fiqh with verification. The word 'rules' (qawā'id) is defined as universal rulings (qadāyā kulliyya) that apply to all their particulars. The qualification 'proximate access' (tawassul qarīb) excludes disciplines like Arabic grammar and theology, which are only preliminaries (mabādī) and do not lead directly to fiqh. 'With verification' (ala wajh al-tahqīq) excludes the science of debate (jadal) which aims to compel the opponent rather than to arrive at truth. The commentator then explains why the word 'science' was added despite the term 'usul al-fiqh' already implying a science—it was for further clarification, analogous to saying 'shajar al-ārāk' (the tree of the ārāk tree) for emphasis. Then a specific example of a qā'ida is given: 'Every ruling that analogy indicates is established', which serves as a universal proposition to derive rulings for particular cases. Finally, the distinction between proximate and remote access is elaborated: Arabic grammar provides knowledge of how words indicate meanings (a middle step), and theology establishes the authenticity of the primary sources; both are remote because they lead to fiqh through an intermediary.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (uṣūl al-fiqh): The science of universal rules through which fiqh rulings are derived with verification.
القاعدة (al-qāʿida): A universal ruling that applies to all its particulars and from which their rulings can be derived.
توصل قريب (tawassul qarīb): Proximate access to fiqh, i.e., direct derivation without intermediary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why are Arabic grammar and theology excluded from usul al-fiqh?
A) Because they do not lead to fiqh at all.
B) Because they provide only proximate access to fiqh.
C) Because they provide only remote access to fiqh, not proximate.
D) Because they are not universal rules.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is defined as knowledge of universal rules (qawāʿid) that provide proximate access to fiqh with verification, excluding remote disciplines and mere debate.

Haythiyya and Tashāruk al-ʿIlmayn: The Sadr al-Shariah vs. Taftazani Dispute
Debate on haythiyya as qualification vs. expression in defining science subjects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the dispute between Sadr al-Shariah and Taftazani on the role of haythiyya in defining the subject matter of a science and evaluate the author's resolution.

Core Idea
A single entity can be subject of multiple sciences if considered under different aspects that are not qualifications but expressions of accidents.

This lesson explores a foundational debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: how do we define the subject of a science? Sadr al-Shariah distinguishes between two types of 'aspects' (haythiyya): one that qualifies the subject and one that merely expresses which accidents are discussed. The commentator Taftazani objects, arguing that any aspect must be a qualification, otherwise a logical contradiction arises. By working through this dispute, you will sharpen your ability to handle subtle distinctions between essential and accidental properties in defining scientific domains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divisions of haythiyya
Sadr al-Shariah classifies haythiyya into two types: one that is part of the subject (qualification) and one that is an expression of essential accidents. The first restricts the discussion to accidents qualified by that aspect; the second merely clarifies which accidents are relevant.
The second division is the point of contention.
2
Understand Taftazani's objection
Taftazani argues that if haythiyya is not a qualification but an expression, then in the case of two sciences sharing the same subject (e.g., bodies studied in astronomy and physics), the aspect would have to be both prior (as medium) and posterior (as accident), which is impossible.
This is essentially a charge of logical circularity.
3
Trace Sadr al-Shariah's response
The author clarifies that the second type of haythiyya does not cause the accidents to occur; it only indicates which accidents are discussed. Thus, the logical priority problem disappears. The accidents are attributed directly to the subject under that aspect, not through the aspect.
The well-known answer (using 'possibility') is rejected as artificial.
4
Apply the distinction to the example of astronomy and physics
Bodies considered in astronomy under the aspect of shape, and in physics under the aspect of nature, are the same entity. Since these aspects are expressions of the relevant accidents, not qualifications, there is no real overlap or contradiction.
This shows that tashāruk al-ʿilmayn is possible without logical flaw.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and thamarah al-khilaf
The passage favors Sadr al-Shariah, noting that Taftazani is eventually forced to adopt the author's explanation. The practical consequence is that a single object (e.g., the human body) can be studied by both medicine and physics without needing to artificially split its subject.
This principle affects how we define boundaries between sciences in the Islamic traditio.

If, not in accordance with the idea, it is not made an expression for the essential accidents, still it is possible to discuss from this aspect, and this discussion will not be about the parts of the subject. And in this form of expression, the objection of the two sciences sharing one subject in essence and in consideration, which is leveled against the author, will not apply to us. Since the author, in the second division, considers the aspect to be an expression of accidents and does not acknowledge its relationship with the subject as a qualification or part, so when a single object is beloved with two such aspects that it becomes the subject of two sciences, then in that case the subject of the two sciences becomes a single entity that is one in essence and also one in consideration, like the bodies of the universe which for astronomy become the subject from the aspect of shape, and for natural science become the subject from the aspect of nature. So this aspect according to the author is for the expression of accidents because in these two sciences the mentioned aspect is brought into discussion. So it will be for expression of accidents, not a qualification. Then the subject of those two sciences becomes a single entity that is one in every respect, whether in essence or in consideration. And since the commentator considers this kind of aspect as a qualification of the subject, due to these two qualifications the distinction in consideration remains. The objection that the commentator leveled against the author has no reality. What the author meant by calling the aspect a part of the subject in the first division is that this aspect will be considered in the descriptive attribute of the subject such that the accidents that occur to the subject will be considered qualified with that description, and those same accidents will be brought under discussion, like the subject of theology is 'existent insofar as it is existent', and this aspect of being existent is included in the descriptive attribute of the subject, and those accidents will be brought under discussion whose occurrence is by virtue of existence itself. And this meaning of being a part is not contrary to being a qualification for subjectivity, just as 'rational' is a part of 'human' and is not contrary to the qualification of humanity. As for the sharing of two sciences in one subject, the author's investigation which will come in the third section is correct, and the distinction of the two sciences will be by virtue of the distinction of specific accidents which are the predicates in the issues, and due to the difference of these predicates, there will be difference in the issues, thereby those two sciences will be considered different. As will come in the third section. Yes, the well-known objection occurs against considering the aspect as a qualification for subjectivity in the second division, as the commentator claims. The summary of the objection is that when it is a qualification for subjectivity, then this aspect cannot be from the accidents discussed in the science because the meaning of being a qualification is that those accidents will be discussed which occur to the subject from this same aspect, and this aspect cannot itself be an accident to the subjects from its own perspective; otherwise, being a medium for occurrence, it would be prior, and in terms of being an accident, it would be posterior, necessitating the priority of a thing over itself, because that by which something becomes an accident necessitates the priority of that cause over the accident. This is the proof. For example, in medicine, discussion of health and disease is with respect to the human body from the aspect of being healthy and diseased, not from the aspect of being something that can be healthy or diseased. Similarly, motion and rest cannot occur to the body from the aspect that it moves or rests, otherwise the priority of a thing over itself would be necessitated, which is false. And the well-known answer is that by 'from the aspect of being healthy and diseased' what is meant is not health and disease themselves, but the possibility of health and disease; and similarly, from 'the aspect that it moves and rests' the possibility of motion and rest is meant, and this possibility is not from the accidents discussed. And the verification indicates that the well-known answer is merely well-known, contrary to verification, based on clear artifice. The summary of the verification is that since the subject is that thing whose accidents are discussed in the science, it is qualified with an aspect, and the meaning is that accidents will be discussed with consideration of that aspect and with regard to it, meaning that in the discussed accidents this aspect will be kept in view and the general meaning of the aspect will be considered and valid in all discussions; but it is not meant that all discussed accidents occur through that aspect. And the summary of the verification reverts to this: that this aspect will clarify and explain the discussed accidents, that is, what kind of accidents can be brought under discussion. This is the same meaning that the author presented: that the aspect is an expression of the essential accidents discussed. Finally, the commentator has been forced to adopt this same explanation that the author chose; the commentator merely fulfilled his habit of objecting, otherwise the author's view was entirely correct and balanced. The author said in al-Tawdih: 'Among them is that it is well-known that a single thing is not the subject of two sciences.'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh regarding the definition and role of 'haythiyya' (aspect) in determining the subject matter of a science. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) distinguishes two types of aspects: one that qualifies the subject and one that merely expresses the accidents. The commentator (al-Taftazani) criticizes this, leading to an objection about tashāruk al-ʿilmayn (two sciences sharing the same subject). The passage explains that the author's view is that a single object can be the subject of two sciences if considered under different aspects, and these aspects are not qualifications but expressions of the accidents discussed. The commentator's view would lead to a logical contradiction (priority of a thing over itself) if the aspect were a qualification. The well-known answer (involving possibility) is rejected as artificial. The true verification is that the aspect serves to clarify which accidents are relevant, not to be the cause of their occurrence. The passage concludes that the author's position is correct and the commentator's objection is unfounded.

Key Terms
حیثیت (haythiyya): A consideration or aspect under which the subject is taken, functioning either as a qualification (qayd) or as an expression of essential accidents (bayān li-aʿrāḍ).
تشارك العلمین (tashāruk al-ʿilmayn): The situation where two sciences share a single subject entity, either in essence (bi-dh-dhāt) or in consideration (bi-l-iʿtibār).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the 'well-known answer' (al-mashhūr fī al-jawāb) to Taftazani's objection?
A) That the aspect is a part of the subject.
B) That 'min haythu yasihhu wa yamradu' refers to the possibility of health and disease.
C) That the aspect is an expression of essential accidents.
D) That two sciences cannot share a subject.

Key Takeaway
Haythiyya can function as an expression of relevant accidents rather than a qualification, allowing a single entity to be subject of multiple sciences without logical contradiction.

The Unity of Fiqh Despite Diverse Accidental Attributes
Response to objection that fiqh could be multiple sciences due to diverse attributes of its subject

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a common genus (jins) preserves the unity of a science despite diverse essential accidents, and evaluate the commentator's objection by constructing the analogy with nahw.

Core Idea
Fiqh remains one science because all its rulings share the common genus of hukm.

In this passage, the author defends the unity of fiqh against an objection that its subject—the act of the mukallaf—has diverse essential attributes (obligation, prohibition, etc.) which could fragment it into multiple sciences. The Hanafi response hinges on the concept of a common genus (jins) that is the very focus of investigation. Just as the science of nahw is one despite its diverse accidents (raf', nasb, jar) because they all belong to the genus i'rab, so fiqh is unified by the genus hukm. We will walk through the objection, the response, and the deeper philosophical argument about essential accidents using the example of the 'truly one' (Wajib Ta'ala).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The commentator argues that because the act of the mukallaf has diverse essential accidents (e.g., obligation, prohibition), one could divide fiqh into separate sciences each corresponding to one type of accident. Recognize this as a challenge to the unity of fiqh.
See the passage: 'بعض اعراض من حیث الوجوب سے لاحق ہوتے ہیں اور بعض من حیث الحرمۃ'.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The response states that diversity of accidents necessitates multiple sciences only when those accidents do not share a common genus that is the actual focus of investigation. In fiqh, the shared genus is 'hukm' (legal rule). Therefore, fiqh is one science.
The response uses the analogy with nahw: diverse accidents of the word (raf', nasb, jar) share genus i'rab, so nahw is one science.
3
Examine the 'Truly One' Argument
The author extends the discussion to the 'wahid haqiqi' (the Necessarily Existent) to show that even a simple essence without parts can have many essential attributes. This refutes the need for fragmentation.
The passage argues that attributes of Allah (power, creating, etc.) are essential accidents despite His simplicity.
4
Evaluate the Commentator's Second Point
The commentator had objected that the aspect (haythiyya) is a restriction on the subject, not the accident itself. The Hanafi response turns this around: if aspects create multiple subjects, then even the commentator's own view would lead to multiple sciences, thus the objection is self-defeating.
The passage says: 'فما هو جوابكم هو جوابنا'.
5
Synthesize the Tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that fiqh is a single science with the subject 'act of the mukallaf from the aspect of hukm'. The common genus ensures unity despite diverse accidents.
This conclusion is supported by consensus among Hanafi usul scholars.

Source Text

د اما ثالثا یہ مصنف پر تیسرا اعتراض ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ ایسا کوئی علم نہیں ہیں جس کا موضوع اعراض ذاتیہ متنوعہ یعنی مختلف بالنوع پر مشتمل نہ ہو فلکل واحد پس ہر ایک کیلئے جائزہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ اعراض ذاتیہ النوع ہونے پر استدلال پیش کیا ہے بان الواحد الحقيقي الذي لاكثره في ذاته الخ یعنی واحد حقیقی جس کے درجہ ذات میں کثرۃ بالکل نہیں یعنی واجب تعالى يتصف بصفات كثيرة الخ يعنى وہ صفات کثیرہ کے ساتھ متصف ہے ذاتیہ متنوعہ کے ساتھ متصف ہوتا ہے ان صفات کا مختلفة النوع ہونا تو ظاہر ہے کیونکہ صفات حقیقیہ اور صفات اضافیہ کی حقیقت الگ الگ ہے اور صفات سلبیہ کی حقیقت ان سے مختلف ہے اب ضرورت اس کی ہے یہ اعراض ہیں نہیں سکتا کیونکہ واحد حقیقی کی کوئی جز ہے ہی نہیں وہ تو ذہنا اور خارجاً بسیط ہے کسی قسم کی اس میں ترکیب نہیں ہے یہ ویسے بیان واقع ہے ورنہ تو جو عارض بواسطة جزء کے لاحق ہوتا ہے وہ عرض ذاتی کہلا تا ہو اسطہ جز مساوتی کے تو بالاتفاق اور بیواسطہ جزہ عام کے عند الشارح عرض ذاتی ہے۔ ولا للمبائن اور ان صفات کا لحوق بواسطته المبائن بھی نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ واحد حقیقی کا اپنے صفات میں محتاج الی الامر المبائن نوع آخر کے ثابت کرنے کے لئے جو کہا ہے وان کان غیر متکلم في ذلك الغير الم یہی تو تعرض بالمبائن ہے اور اس کا تعلق بکلا انو جنین ہے نہ کہ صرف آخری وجہ سے لہذا شارح کا اعتراض صیح نہیں جیسے کہ شارح نئے اسی کا بواسطه صفته آخری تو تسلسل في المبادی لازم آجائیں گے یعنی ایسی صفات میں جو ہر ایک صفہ دوسری صفتہ کے لئے مبدا الحوق بنتی چلی جائیگی اور تسلسل محال ہے
Thirdly, this is the third objection against the author. Its summary is that there is no science whose subject is not comprised of diverse essential accidents, i.e., different in kind. So for each one, it is possible to declare that single science as multiple sciences due to the diverse essential accidents. For example, making the investigation about the act means the subject of fiqh is the act of the responsible person, and it comprises diverse essential accidents: some accidents attach from the aspect of obligation, some from the aspect of prohibition. Now a science in which the act of the responsible person is discussed from the aspect of obligation, and another science in which the act of the responsible person is discussed from the aspect of prohibition – these sciences would have a single subject, and the distinction between them would be by virtue of the investigated accidents: in one, accidents of obligation are discussed; in the other, accidents of prohibition. In this respect, the science of fiqh could be multiple sciences. Thus it cannot be regulated. Then the unity of science and the difference of science cannot be regulated. The response given to the commentator's question is that diversity of accidents necessitates difference of sciences only when those accidents are not shared in a genus that is the intended focus of investigation. For example, in syntax, the diverse accidents of the word include raf', nasb, and jar, but these are not multiple sciences because these accidents share the genus of i'rab; due to that generic commonality, the science is one. Similarly, despite the act of the responsible person's accidents being diverse due to obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and disapproval, al-hukm is the genus for them; all share in it. Therefore the subject of fiqh is the act of the responsible person from the aspect of hukm, so fiqh will be considered a single science. Moreover, we concede to the commentator that the aspect does not express the accident but is a subjective restriction and a restriction of discussion. Then we say: the act of the responsible person from the aspect of obligation is one subject, from the aspect of prohibition is a second subject, and from the aspect of disapproval is a third subject. In this respect, the subject becomes multiple; due to multiplicity of subject, according to the commentator, sciences could be multiple. So according to the commentator's own research, fiqh could become multiple sciences. So what is your answer? That is our answer. His saying: 'And we only said: he adduced proof...' i.e., the author adduced proof for the diversity and different-type of accidents of the single thing: 'that the truly one which has no multiplicity in its essence...' i.e., the Necessarily Existent, exalted, is described with many attributes. Some are real, like power; some are relational, like creating; some are negative, like being free from matter, i.e., He has no matter. And the one described with many attributes is described with diverse essential accidents. That these attributes are different in kind is obvious, because the reality of real attributes and relational attributes are separate, and the reality of negative attributes is different from them. Now the need is to prove that these are essential accidents. For that, he said: 'Necessarily, none of those attributes attaches through a part...' i.e., he is presenting the reason for the diverse accidents being essential. The gist is that the attachment of these diverse attributes cannot be through a part because the truly one has no part; it is simple mentally and externally, having no composition of any kind. This statement occurs; otherwise, an accident that attaches through a part is called an essential accident – through a co-equal part unanimously, and through a general part according to the commentator. 'Nor through the separate thing': and the attachment of these attributes cannot be through a separate thing either, because the truly one being in need of a separate, disconnected thing for its attributes is impossible and invalid. An objection was raised against the author: that mentioning this separate thing was appropriate, but the author omitted it, which is inappropriate. Our answer is that there is no need to mention the separate thing, because essential accident means that which can be a predicate; since the separate thing itself cannot be a predicate, it cannot be an effective intermediary for predication of another. Moreover, what the author said to prove another type of essential accident, 'even if he does not speak about that other...' this is indeed a discussion about the separate thing, and it relates to both types, not just the last reason. Hence the commentator's objection is not correct, as the commentator himself acknowledges at the end of this statement, as will come. And then: either the attachment of each of them... meaning when the attachment of an attribute is not through a part or a separate thing, then either the attachment will be through a subsequent attribute, and then that subsequent attribute through another subsequent attribute, leading to infinite regress in the foundations, i.e., attributes where each attribute becomes the source of attachment for the next, and infinite regress is impossible.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the unity of the science of fiqh. The commentator (presumably Taftazani in Al-Talwih) raises an objection: since the subject of fiqh (the act of the mukallaf) has diverse essential accidents (wujub, hurma, etc.), one could fragment fiqh into multiple sciences each focusing on one type of accident. The response (from the matn author, Sadr al-Shariah) is that such fragmentation does not occur if the diverse accidents share a common genus that is the actual focus of investigation. In fiqh, that common genus is 'hukm' (legal rule). Thus, despite the acts having different attributes like obligation and prohibition, all are investigated qua their legal rule, so fiqh remains one science. The discussion then extends to the nature of essential accidents, using the example of the 'truly one' (Wajib Ta'ala) to argue that attributes can be essential even without composition. The author defends his position against the commentator's criticism regarding the omission of the 'separate thing' intermediary, showing that infinite regress is avoided. This is a classic Hanafi usul discussion distinguishing between subject and aspect.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتی (arad dhati): An accident that attaches to a thing not through an intermediary (part or separate thing), or through a co-equal part, etc. Essential to the subject.
واحد حقیقی (wahid haqiqi): That which has no multiplicity in its essence, e.g., Allah (Wajib Ta'ala).
حکم (hukm): The legal rule (obligation, prohibition, etc.) that is the common genus for the diverse attributes of the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is fiqh considered a single science despite the act of the mukallaf having diverse attributes like obligation and prohibition?
A) Because the attributes are all essential and cannot be separated.
B) Because the attributes share the common genus of 'hukm' which is the focus of investigation.
C) Because the subject 'act of mukallaf' is one and indivisible.
D) Because the commentator proved that diversity of accidents always requires multiple sciences.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh remains a single science because all its diverse rulings share the common genus of hukm, which is the intended object of investigation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Basmalah: One Verse Repeated or 113?
Dispute on Basmalah's Quranicity and implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on the Basmalah, explain the later preferred view, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf concerning its count and use in prayer.

Core Idea
The Basmalah is one verse repeated for separation, not 113 separate verses.

This lesson explores the juristic dispute over whether the Basmalah at the start of each surah is part of the Quran. The Hanafi school has two views: the early position denies it (except in Surah Naml), while the later preferred view affirms it as one independent verse revealed for separation between surahs. We will examine the evidence, the objections raised, and the practical differences with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Define the Quran
Understand that the Quran is only what is transmitted by tawatur and written in the mushaf, excluding hadith qudsi, abrogated verses, and irregular recitations.
This sets the threshold: any claimed Quranic status must meet tawatur and inclusion in the mushaf.
2
Identify the two Hanafi positions
State the early position (Basmalah not Quran except in Surah Naml) and the later preferred view (one verse repeated for separation).
The early view is from the majority of early texts; the later view is adopted by mutakhkhirin.
3
Analyze the proof for the later view
The dalil: it is written in the mushaf in the script of the Quran, and no Salafi rejection is reported despite the emphatic rule of purifying the mushaf from non-Quran.
This is an implied ijma' or practice-based proof.
4
Address the three objections
Explain why prayer is invalid if limited to Basmalah (doubt of completeness), why junub/ha'id can recite it (intention of blessing, not recitation), and why no takfir for denial (doubt and ikhtilaf).
These objections help refine the application of the later view.
5
Compare with Shafi'i and extract thamarah al-khilaf
Shafi'is count 113 Basmalah verses; Hanafis count one. This affects the number of Quranic verses and the obligation of Basmalah in prayer.
The practical difference: Shafi'is require Basmalah before Fatihah; Hanafis do not oblige it.

العلمین علی قصد الشکر جنب و حائض کے لئے جائز ہے اور علی قصد التلاوہ ناجائز ہے ۔ وعدم تکفیر یہ تیسرا مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر تسمیہ جزء من القرآن ہے تو جو اس کے قران ہونے کا انکار کرے اس کی تکفیر کیوں نہیں کی جس نے اس شیعہ کو قومی کر دیا ہے جس کی وجہ سے اس کی قرانیہ مقام وضوح سے نکل کر حیر ز اشکال داشتباہ میں پہونچ چکی ہے اور اس جیسا شبہ مانع عن التکفیر ہوتا ہے ۔ خان قیل خلاصہ سوال یہ ہے کہ متأخرین حنفیہ کے حسب مختار کہ تسمیہ جزء قرآن ہے کیا اس کے باوجود فریقین میں یعنی احناف اور شوافع کے مابین اختلاف باقی رہیگا یا کہ نہیں ۔ قلنا نعم ہاں اختلاف باقی ہے کیونکہ تسمیہ شوافع کے نزدیک ہر سورۃ کی جز اور ایک آیت چونکہ قرآن مجید کی کل سورۃ ایک سو چودہ ہیں اور سورۃ براۃ کی شروع میں تسمیہ نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک قرآن مجید کی یہ ایک سو تیرہ آیات ہیں جیسے فیاستی آلاء ربکما تکذبان سورة الرحمن کی متعدد آیات ہیں اور عند الحنفیہ قرآن مجید کی یہ صرف ایک آیت ہے اس کا تکرار اوائل سور میں صرف فصل بین السور اور تبرک کی خاطر ہے اور یہ کسی سورۃ کی آیت نہیں ہے اور اس کا تکرار اوائل سور میں اس لئے جائز ہے کہ اس کا نزول اسی خاطر ہے اور سلف سے ایسے منقول ہے۔ بخلاف من اخذ الخ یعنی تسمیہ کے علاوہ بقصد تبرک وغیرہ کسی اور آیت کا تکرار اوائل سور میں جائز نہیں مثلاً کوئی ہر سورۃ کے اول میں بقصد تیرک الحمد الله رب العلمین لکھنا شروع کر دے یہ قطعا جائز نہیں ایسے شخص کو زندیق یا مجنون شمار کیا جائیگا۔ نعلى ما هو المناسب یہ مصنف کی تعریف پر ایک قسم کا اعتراض ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اصولی آدمی چونکہ کتاب اللہ تعالیٰ سے استدلال علی الاحکام کرتا ہے اور اس کیلئے قرآن مجید کا ہر بعض استعمال ہوتا ہے یعنی آیت یا اس کے مقدار سے عموما استدلال کرتا ہے مجموعے من حیث المجموع کو استدلال میں پیش نہیں کرتا اس لئے اصول کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسب یہ ہے کہ ما نقل بین
And divine hadiths, qudsi hadiths, abrogated recitation verses, and prophetic hadiths are not transmitted between the covers of the mus-haf, because the name [Quran] is for this customary collection known among people, even children know it. And all mentioned [things] are not transmitted in this customary mus-haf. And irregular recitations are excluded by the condition of tawatur, because their transmission, even if in some specific mus-hafs, is by way of ahad or mashhur, not tawatur. So there is no need to mention revelation and inimitability, etc. The phrase 'without doubt' is for emphasis of tawatur. Without these, the definition excluding everything other than Quran is achieved. As for the Basmalah: the famous madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifah in most early books is that the Basmalah is not a part of the Quran except the one in Surah Naml which is part of a verse. That Basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is not Quran. However, according to the later scholars, the correct view is that according to the Imam, the Basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is only one verse of the Quran, and its revelation is for separation between surahs. The proof is that it is written in the Quran with the script of the Quran, and no rejection from the salaf is reported, even though the rule of purifying the Quran from non-Quran is emphasized. So it becomes clear that the Basmalah is a part of the Quran. [Then the text addresses doubts about its Quranicity through three issues:] (1) The impermissibility of prayer [if limited to Basmalah]: because there is doubt about it being a complete verse, so the obligatory amount is not fulfilled. (2) The permissibility for a junub or ha'id to recite it is on the intention of seeking blessing, not on the intention of recitation, like saying 'alhamdulillah' as thanks. (3) No takfir for denying its Quranicity because of the doubt and disagreement among imams, which makes its Quranicity unclear. Then a question: According to the later Hanafis that Basmalah is part of Quran, does the difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is remain? Yes, because according to Shafi'is, it is a separate verse for each surah, so there are 113 verses (since Surah Bara'ah has no Basmalah). According to Hanafis, it is only one verse repeated. Repeating it at the beginning of surahs is allowed for separation and blessing, reported from Salaf. But repeating any other verse at the beginnings of surahs is not allowed; whoever does that would be considered a zindiq or madman. Then an objection: The usuli deduces rulings from parts of the Quran, not the whole collection, so the definition should be what is between the covers, etc.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the legal status of the Basmalah (bismillah al-rahman al-rahim) and its implications in Hanafi fiqh. The author first delimits the definition of Quran: it is only what is transmitted by tawatur and written in the mushaf, excluding hadith qudsi, abrogated verses, and irregular recitations. Then he addresses the Basmalah. In the Hanafi school, there are two positions: the early well-known position of Imam Abu Hanifah (transmitted in the majority of early texts) holds that the Basmalah is not part of the Quran except the one in Surah al-Naml (verse 30). The Basmalah at the beginnings of surahs is not Quran. However, the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) give preponderance to the view that the Imam considered the Basmalah at the beginnings of surahs to be one independent verse of the Quran, revealed for separation between surahs. This is proven by its being written in the mushaf and the absence of any rejection from the Salaf. The passage then clarifies three objections that might arise from this view: (1) If Basmalah is Quran, why is prayer invalid if one only recites it? Answer: because there is doubt about whether it is a complete verse for the purpose of prayer; thus the obligatory amount is not fulfilled. (2) Why is it permissible for a junub or a ha'id to recite it? Answer: they recite it with the intention of seeking blessing, not as Quranic recitation; analogous to saying 'alhamdulillah' as thanks. (3) Why is the one who denies its Quranicity not declared an unbeliever? Answer: because there is doubt and disagreement among scholars, which prevents takfir. Finally, the passage explains that even though later Hanafis adopt this view, the difference with the Shafi'is remains: Shafi'is consider the Basmalah a separate verse of each surah (except Surah Bara'ah), so they count 113 Basmalah verses in the Quran. Hanafis consider it a single verse repeated for separation between surahs, and it is not a verse of any particular surah. Repeating any other verse at the beginnings of surahs is prohibited and would be considered blasphemy or insanity. The passage concludes with an objection regarding the definition of Quran for usul purposes: since a usuli deduces rulings from parts of the Quran (e.g., a verse), the definition should focus on the transmitted words, not the entire collection.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmia): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) considered as a potential part of the Quran.
قرآن (Quran): The speech of Allah revealed to Prophet Muhammad, transmitted by tawatur, written in the mushaf.
شاذة (shadhdha): Irregular recitations that are not transmitted by tawatur; excluded from the definition of Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi view (mutakhkhirin), how many Quranic verses does the Basmalah constitute?
A) 113 verses
B) 114 verses
C) One verse repeated at the beginning of most surahs
D) It is not part of the Quran at all

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi view holds the Basmalah as one Quranic verse repeated for separation, differing from the Shafi'i count of 113 verses, with practical implications for prayer.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
