Tard and 'Aks Objections to the Definition of the Qur'an
Analysis of definition objections and response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the objections of tard and 'aks against the definition of 'ma naqala' and explain how the Hanafi school resolves them by distinguishing the composite whole from the universal concept and by clarifying the usuli's purpose.

Core Idea
A definition must apply to all and only its instances; a single verse is both part of the Qur'an and a valid proof.

This passage examines the logical coherence of defining the Qur'an as 'the transmitted text' (ma naqala). Two objections arise: if the definition is too general, it includes letters not called Qur'an; if too specific, it excludes incomplete verses that are nevertheless considered Qur'an. The response reconciles these by interpreting 'ma naqala' as the composite whole (majmu' min hayth al-majmu') and by showing that the usuli's use of individual verses as proofs does not contradict the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
The first objection (tard) claims that if 'ma naqala' is general, it applies to every letter, but the Shariah does not call each letter Qur'an. The second objection ('aks) claims that if it is specific to complete speech, incomplete parts (like a single verse) are excluded, yet they are considered Qur'an for purposes like touching and recitation. Note the definitions: tard requires coverage of all instances; 'aks requires coverage of only instances.
2
Examine the author's solution
The author (Sadr al-Shariah) intends 'ma naqala' as the particular composite (majmu' shakhsi), i.e., the whole collection considered as one entity. This avoids both objections because the whole is not the part, and the part is included in the whole only in a derivative sense. However, a new objection arises: the usuli needs to use parts (verses) as evidence, but the definition treats them as not being the book itself.
3
Follow the response to the new objection
The response argues that the usuli uses each verse as a proof precisely because it is part of the Book, not because it is the Book itself. The usuli's purpose is to derive rulings from the conditions of words (generality, specificity, etc.), and each word or verse is a valid proof (dalil) for that purpose.
4
Connect to the nature of proof (dalil)
The passage expands on what constitutes a dalil: it is something by which one can reach a desired conclusion through sound consideration of its established conditions. This includes nouns, verbs, and particles, each having attributes like 'amm, khass, haqiqah, majaz, amr, nahy. Thus, even a single word is suitable for inference, making the definition suitable for the usuli's purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رفتی المصاحف سے مراد عام ہو جو کل اور بعض دونوں کو شامل ہو تو پھر اس عموم کے لحاظ سے به تعریف قرآن مجید کے ہر ہر حرف اور سر کلمہ پر صادق آجائیگی حالانکہ عرف شرع میں اسے قران نہیں کہتے تو گویا حد غیر محدود پر صادق آگئی جو اس کے طرد کے منافی ہے اگر مانقل سے على المخصوص کلام نام مراد ہو تو پھر وہ جو کلام تام نہیں ہے خارج از حد ہو جائیگی لیکن اسے قرآن کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ محدث کے لئے اس حصہ کو مس کرنا اور جنب کا تلاوۃ کرنا حرام ہے تو محدود اس کو شامل ہے اور حد شامل نہ ہوئی تو یہ عکس تعریف کے منافی ہے۔ وعلى مادل عليه سياق الجو لیکن مصنف " کے نزدیک جیسے کہ اس کی کلام دال ہے ما نقل سے مراد مجموع من حیث المجموع ہے لانه جعله تعریفا کیونکہ مصنف نے اس کو مجموع شخصی کی تعریف قرار دیا ہے اور مجموع کلی جو کہ صادق علی الکل والبعض آسکتا ہے اس کی تعریف نہیں بناتا تو اس لحاظ سے اس اشکالین سابقین میں سے کوئی اشکال وارد تو نہیں ہو سکتا لیکن یہ اصول کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسب نہیں ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ ما نقل سے مراد اگر مفہوم کلی ہو جو کل اور بعض دونوں پر صادق آتے تو پھر طر یا عکس منتقض ہو جاتا ہے اگر مانقل سے مجموع من حیث المجموع مراد ہو جو کہ شخصی درجہ ہے تو پھر یہ اصولی کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسب نہیں ہے ۔ اس اعتراض کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مصنف کی مراد ما نقل سے مجموع من حیث المجموع شخصی ہے آپ کا اعتراض کہ یہ اصولی کی غرض کے ساتھ مناسبت نہیں رکھتا ہم اسے تسلیم نہیں کرتے کیونکہ اصولی جو آیت آیت سے استدلال کرتا ہے وہ بایں حیثیت کرتا ہے کہ انہا من الكتاب لا من حيث انها نفس الكتاب و عینہ یعنی یہ آیت مستدل بها کتاب کا حصہ اور جز ہے نہ یہ کہ یہ کتاب اللہ کا عین ہے اگر مفہوم کلی مراد لیا جائے جو صادق علی الکل والبعض ہے تو بھی اعتراض وارد نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اصولی کی غرض استدلال علی الاحکام ہے لہذا اصولی کتاب اللہ یا سنہ کے احوال سے من حیث کو نہا دلیل شرعیا سے بحث کرتا ہے اور دلیل ما یمکن التوصل بصيح النظر فيه الى مطلوب خبری کو کہتے ہیں اس لحاظ سے ضروری ہے کہ وہ کلمہ والہ ہو لہذا یہ اسم فعل حرف کو شامل ہو جائیںگی یہی وجہ ہے کہ اصولی احوال خاص عام اور مشترک و حقیقت و مجاز اور امر و نہی سے بحث کرتا ہے جو اسے استدلال کا کام دیتے ہیں لہذا ما نقل کا بعض کو شامل ہونا تعریف میں خلل نہیں ڈالتا کیونکہ دلیل کا جو مفہوم پیش کیا گیا ہے ما یمکن التوصل بصیح النظر فیہ اس صحیح النظر تمراد یہ ہے کہ اس کے احوال ثابتہ صحیحہ کا جائزہ لیکر مطلوب خبری تک پہونچنے کی کوشش کی جائے جیسے عالم کو دلیل علی وجود اللہ بنایا جاتا ہے تو عالم کے حالات صحیحہ کا جائزہ لیکر کہا جاتا ہے العالم متغیر اور کبری کل متغیر حادث ملاکر مطلوب خبری العالم حادث تک پہونچتے ہیں پھر کہا جاتا الحادث لہ محدث اسی صانع تو ثابت ہو جاتا ہے العلم یہ صانع اسی طرح اصولی ہر کلمہ اسم و فعل و حرف کے حااات از قسم عموم و خصوص داشتراک اور حقیقت و مجاز اور امر و نہی جیسے حالات کا جائزہ لیکر استدلال علی الاحکام کرتا ہے تو اس کے لئے ایک ایک کلمہ مناسب مقصود ہے اس لئے اس کو قران کہنا اس کی مرض کے لحاظ سے صحیح ہے۔
If what is meant by 'what is transmitted to the musahif' is general, including both the whole and the part, then according to this generality the definition would apply to every letter and word of the Noble Qur'an, even though in the Shariah term it is not called Qur'an. Thus the definition would apply to something unlimited, which contradicts its coextension (tard). If by 'what is transmitted' is meant specifically complete speech, then that which is not complete speech would be outside the definition, but it is called Qur'an because for a person in minor impurity (muhdith) touching that part and for a junub reciting it is forbidden. So that part is included in what is limited, but the definition does not include it, which contradicts the converse ('aks) of the definition. And according to what is indicated by the context of the response, but according to the author (musannif), as his words indicate, by 'what is transmitted' he means the composite as a whole (majmu' min hayth al-majmu'), because he made it a definition. He made it a definition of the particular composite (majmu' shakhsi), not a definition of the universal composite (majmu' kulli) which can apply to the whole and the part. So from this perspective, none of the previous two objections can arise. However, this is not suitable for the purpose of usul. In summary, if by 'what is transmitted' is meant the universal concept that applies to both the whole and the part, then tard or 'aks would be violated. If by 'what is transmitted' is meant the composite as a whole, which is of the degree of particular, then this is not suitable for the purpose of the usuli. The response to this objection is that the author's intention by 'what is transmitted' is the particular composite as a whole. Your objection that this is not suitable for the purpose of the usuli is not accepted because when the usuli draws evidence from one verse after another, he does so in the capacity that they are part of the Book, not in the capacity that they are the Book itself. That is, this verse being used as evidence is a part and portion of the Book, not that it is the very Book of Allah. Even if the universal concept that applies to both the whole and the part is taken, the objection cannot arise because the purpose of the usuli is to use evidence for rulings. Therefore, the usuli discusses the conditions of the Book of Allah or the Sunnah insofar as they are a legal proof. And a proof (dalil) is that by which one can reach a desired news (matlub khabari) through sound consideration. From this perspective, it is necessary that it be a word; hence it includes nouns, verbs, and particles. This is why the usuli discusses conditions of specific, general, homonymous, real, metaphorical, command, and prohibition, which give him the function of inference. Therefore, the inclusion of part in 'what is transmitted' does not cause defect in the definition because the concept of proof presented is 'that by which one can reach through sound consideration'. By 'sound consideration' is meant that by examining its established sound conditions, one tries to reach the desired news. For example, when the world is made a proof for the existence of Allah, one examines the sound conditions of the world and says: 'The world is changing, and everything changing is created', combining to reach the desired news: 'The world is created.' Then it is said: 'Every created thing has a creator, thus the Maker is established.' So the world is, in its own right, a proof for the Maker. Similarly, the usuli examines each word, noun, verb, and particle, from the categories of generality, specificity, homonymy, real, metaphorical, command, and prohibition, and draws evidence for rulings. Thus for him each single word is suitable for the intended purpose. Therefore, calling it Qur'an is correct according to his intention.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the definition of 'ma naqala' (the transmitted text) as used in defining the Qur'an. It addresses two key objections: (1) If 'ma naqala' is general, it would include every letter and word, but in Shariah such parts are not called Qur'an, violating the condition of 'tard' (the definition must apply to all instances). (2) If it is specific to complete speech, then incomplete parts (like a single verse) would be excluded, even though they are considered Qur'an for purposes of touching and recitation, violating the condition of 'aks' (the definition must apply only to instances). The author (Sadr al-Shariah) intends 'ma naqala' as the composite whole (majmu' min hayth al-majmu'), a particular composite. But a further objection arises: this does not suit the usuli's purpose because the usuli uses individual verses as evidence. The response explains that the usuli uses each part as a proof precisely because it is part of the Book, not the Book itself. Even if the universal concept is taken, it works because the usuli studies the conditions of words (generality, specificity, etc.) to derive rulings. Thus the definition need not exclude parts. The passage concludes by relating this to the nature of a proof (dalil), which requires sound consideration of conditions.

Key Terms
ما نقل (ma naqala): The transmitted text (i.e., the Qur'an) as defined by the author; either as a universal concept or a particular composite.
طرد (tard): Coextension: the definition must apply to all instances of the definiendum.
عكس ('aks): Conversion: the definition must apply only to instances of the definiendum.
مجموع من حیث المجموع (majmu' min hayth al-majmu'): The composite as a whole, i.e., the entire collection considered as one entity, not distributively.
دلیل (dalil): That by which one can reach a desired conclusion through sound consideration of its established conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key objection raised if 'ma naqala' is interpreted as a universal concept applying to whole and part?
A) It violates 'aks because it excludes parts.
B) It violates tard because it includes things not called Qur'an.
C) It is circular because it uses the defined term.
D) It is too narrow for the usuli's purpose.

Key Takeaway
The definition of the Qur'an as a composite whole is logically sound and compatible with the usuli's use of individual verses as proofs, as long as the distinction between the whole and its parts is maintained.

Defending 'Qur'an' as Applicable to Both Whole and Part Against 'Umum al-Mushtarak'
Defending the definition of Quran against the charge of homonymy leading to 'umum al-mushtarak'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that 'Qur'an' can apply to both the whole and a part without violating the rule of 'la 'umum fi al-mushtarak', and apply this distinction in analyzing definitions.

Core Idea
'Qur'an' has a general wad' covering whole and part — avoiding homonymy by a single general meaning.

In defining 'al-Kitab' as 'al-Qur'an', an objection arises: if 'Qur'an' is real for both the whole book and a single verse, does it become a homonym (mushtarak) violating the rule that homonyms cannot be generalized? The Hanafi response distinguishes between a specific wad' for the whole and a general wad' encompassing both. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
The objector claims that if 'Qur'an' is used both for the whole and a part, it has two distinct meanings, making it a homonym. Since the definition intends only one meaning, using it for both would require generalizing the homonym, which is prohibited.
The principle 'la 'umum fi al-mushtarak' is well-established in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis argue that 'Qur'an' is not a homonym; it has a single general wad' that covers both the whole and the part. The reality of its usage is not separate assignments but one assignment that includes both.
The term is used mutawatiran for the transmitted speech.
3
Distinguish Between Specific and General Wad'
There is a specific wad' for the whole alone, and another general wad' that covers both. When applied to the transmitted mutawatir speech, it operates under the general wad', so it is real for both without being a homonym.
This resolves the objection by showing no true homonymy exists.
4
Apply to the Definition
Thus, 'al-Kitab' in the second sense can be interpreted as 'al-Qur'an' legitimately, avoiding 'umum al-mushtarak' entirely.

فان قيل فالكتاب بالمعنى الثاني الى بالمعنى الصادق على الكل والبعض بل يصح تفسيره بالقران جب کہ قرآن توكل من حیث الکل کو کہا جاتا ہے کیا یہ کتاب بالمعنی الکلی کی تفسیر ہوسکتا ہے۔ قلنا نعہ کیونکہ قرآن کا اطلاق علی البعض حقیقی ہے جیسے کل میں حقیقہ ہے اس لئے یہ الکتاب کی تفسیر ہو سکتا ہے فان قيل فلزم عموم المشترك کیونکہ جب بعض کے لئے بھی حقیقت اور کل پر بھی اس کا اطلاق علی سبیل الحقیقۃ ہے تو ان دونوں معنی کے لئے موضوع ہوا تو یہ شرک بين المعنیین ہوگیا اور ایک ہی اطلاق میں مشترک کے جمیع معانی مراد لینا یہ عموم فی المشترك ہے جو کہ ممنوع ہے کیونکہ لا عموم فی المشترک کے مشہور ضابطہ کے خلاف ہے۔ قلنا ليس معنی کونه حقیقة اتخذ یہ اس سوال کا جواب ہے یعنی اس کا بعض میں حقیقت ہونا جیسے کل میں حقیقت ہے اس سے یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ اس کی علی الخصوص صرف بعض کے لئے وضع ہے جیسے کل کے لئے علی الخصوص وضع ہے جس سے حمل علی الکل والبعض سے عموم مشترک لازم آتے بلکہ ہماری مراد یہ ہے کہ اس کی ایک وضع علی الخصوص صرف کل کے لئے ہے اور دوسری وضع اس سے عام ہے جو کل وبعض دونوں کو شامل ہے اعتی الکلام المنقول فى المصحف تواترا تو اس صورت میں بوضع واحد کل وبعض میں حقیقت قرار پائیگا۔ اور ہماری مراد یہی عمومی معنی ہے اسی لحاظ سے الکتاب بالمعنی الکلی کی تفسیر ہو سکتا ہے۔ ولا يكون من عموم المشترک فی شتی
If it is said: 'al-Kitab' in the second sense is the sense true of both the whole and the part, rather it is correct to interpret it as 'al-Qur'an'? But al-Qur'an is said only of the whole in its entirety. Can this be an interpretation of 'al-Kitab' in the universal sense? We say: Yes, because the application of 'Qur'an' to a part is real (haqiqi), just as it is real for the whole. Therefore, it can be an interpretation of 'al-Kitab'. If it is said: Then it necessitates 'umum al-mushtarak' (generalizing a homonym), because when it is real for the part and also real for the whole, and it is used for both meanings, then it becomes a homonym (mushtarak) between the two meanings, and intending all meanings of a homonym in a single application is 'umum fi al-mushtarak', which is prohibited because it contradicts the well-known principle 'la 'umum fi al-mushtarak' (there is no generality in homonyms). We say: The meaning of its being real is not that it is established specifically for the part alone, just as it is specifically established for the whole, which would necessitate 'umum al-mushtarak' when applied to both whole and part. Rather, our meaning is that it has one specific wad' (linguistic convention) solely for the whole, and another wad' that is more general, covering both the whole and the part. That is, the transmitted speech in the musahif continuously (mutawatir). In that case, with one wad', it becomes real for both whole and part. And our meaning is this general meaning. From this perspective, it can be an interpretation of 'al-Kitab' in the universal sense. And it is not from 'umum al-mushtarak' at all.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about whether the term 'Qur'an' can be used for both the whole and a part without falling into 'umum al-mushtarak' (using a homonym in all its meanings). The objection: If 'Qur'an' is real for both part and whole, then it becomes a homonym (mushtarak) with two distinct meanings. Using it for both in one utterance would require intending both meanings, which violates the rule 'la 'umum fi al-mushtarak' — homonyms cannot be taken generally. The response distinguishes between two kinds of wad' (linguistic assignment): one specific for the whole alone, and another general that covers both whole and part. When applied to the transmitted text (mutawatir), the term is real for both under the general wad'. Thus, it is not a homonym but a single term with a scope that includes both. Hence, interpreting 'al-Kitab' (the second sense) as 'al-Qur'an' is valid without falling into the forbidden generalization of homonyms.

Key Terms
اشتراک (ishtirak): Homonymy: a single word having two or more distinct meanings.
عموم المشترك (umum al-mushtarak): Generalizing a homonym: intending all meanings of a homonym in a single use, which is prohibited.
وضع (wad'): Linguistic convention by which a word is assigned to a meaning.
حقیقة (haqiqah): Real (literal) meaning: the meaning for which the word was originally coined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core reason that the Hanafi position avoids the problem of 'umum al-mushtarak' in using 'Qur'an' for both whole and part?
A) 'Qur'an' is a homonym with two separate meanings, but using both is allowed in this context.
B) 'Qur'an' has a single general wad' that covers both whole and part, so it is not homonymous.
C) 'Qur'an' is never used for a part, so the problem does not arise.
D) The rule 'la 'umum fi al-mushtarak' is not accepted in Hanafi usul.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends 'Qur'an' as a general wad' term covering whole and part, thereby avoiding the prohibition of 'umum al-mushtarak' and allowing its use in definitions.

Why Definitions Cannot Rely on Changing Accidental Properties
Critiquing definitions that rely on accidental properties for particulars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the flaw in definitions that include accidental properties for particulars and explain why the Hanafi usul accepts accidentals only if they are stable.

Core Idea
A definition of a particular must apply perpetually; accidentals change, so they cannot ground a valid definition.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, definitions (حدود) must be comprehensive (جامع) and exclusive (مانع), applying to the defined at all times. This passage critiques definitions that rely on accidental properties (عرضیات) for identifying a particular individual. We will explore why such definitions fail and how the usuliyyun definition differs from the logicians'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of a definition in usul
A definition must be comprehensive and exclusive and must apply to the defined whenever it exists.
This is the standard of حد اصولیین.
2
Recognize the problem with accidentals
Accidental properties can change over time (e.g., youth to old age). If the definition includes such properties, it may cease to apply to the same individual later.
The passage gives the example of Zayd defined by his youth.
3
Distinguish usul definition from logical definition
Logicians (حد منطقیین) include only essential properties (ذاتیات); usuliyyun allow accidentals for identification. But if the accidental changes, the definition fails because it no longer applies.
The objection that accidentals cannot be in a definition is specific to logic, not usul.
4
Understand the rejection of the 'cessation' argument
Some argue that when accidentals change, the defined person ceases to exist, so the definition still applies to the former individual. The author rejects this: the person's identity persists.
The argument that the youth ceases and an old person appears is invalid.
5
Conclude that only pointing can fully individuate
For particulars, intellectual distinction through universals can only achieve existence-based distinction, not full conceptual uniqueness. Pointing (اشارہ) is the only way.
This leads to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The specific also applies to other human beings; then it does not count as distinction. So this type of definition cannot even give the benefit of distinguishing the defined particular from others, which is the least and lowest level of definition; therefore this definition cannot be correct. And if the specifying accidents are mentioned with it, meaning that in the definition of a particular, if along with the constitutive elements of its quiddity, specifying accidents are also mentioned, which are specific to it and beneficial for distinction, then their applying to the defined particular is not necessary perpetually due to the possibility of their cessation. For example, we define Zayd in his time of youth; then the accidents of youth that are presented at that time will cease in the state of old age, so that previous definition will not apply to him in this state of old age. Thus it will not be a definition because the application of the definition to the defined is necessary, whereas it does not apply in this state. It should be clear that what is meant here by definition is the definition of the usuliyyun, i.e., a comprehensive and exclusive description, not the definition of the logicians, which only comprises essential properties; therefore this objection that a definition containing accidents cannot be a definition will not arise. In this view, the second possibility is chosen, i.e., specifying accidents will also be mentioned in the definition. And when these accidents cease, the defined also ceases. That is, the person who was the subject of the accidents of youth, when these accidents cease in the state of old age, then they say that the defined person also ceases. That is, the person of youth has ceased; now this is another person characterized by old age. Therefore, at that time, the definition's non-application is not harmful; rather it is necessary that when the defined has ceased, the previous definition should not apply at that time. This is an objection, and the true investigation in the answer is: the truth is that a particular can have a definition that gives it distinction from all others according to existence, not a definition that gives its specification. That is, a definition that can fully diagnose and specify it, such that its sharing among many is not possible rationally — this cannot be done. Because as much as you mention specifying accidents without pointing, they are all universal concepts intellectually, whose application to many is possible, even if according to external existence they do not apply to many, but intellectually their application to many is possible. For example, in answer to 'Who is Zayd?', one may say: 'The one who came to you today alone before everyone else.' So according to external existence, there cannot be two such persons, but intellectually, despite this diagnosis, multiplicity is possible for it, and application to many is not impossible intellectually. Such specification and diagnosis can only be obtained through pointing.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of definitions (حد) in usul al-fiqh, specifically whether a definition of a particular (شخص) can include accidental properties (عرضیات). The author first critiques that if a definition includes mere accidentals shared by others, it fails to distinguish. Then considers the case where specifying accidentals are included; but these may change (e.g., youth), so the definition would not apply perpetually. A counterargument that the defined person 'ceases' when accidentals change is rejected. The correct position is that a definition of a particular cannot achieve full individuation through universals; only pointing (اشارہ) can uniquely identify a particular. Thus, definitions using universal terms can only distinguish in existence, not intellectually. This is consistent with Hanafi usul that definitions in legal theory aim at جامع و مانع (comprehensive and exclusive) but for particulars, external distinction suffices.

Key Terms
حد اصولیین (hadd al-usuliyyin): A comprehensive and exclusive description (جامع و مانع) used in legal theory, which may include accidentals
عرضیات مشخصہ (aradiyyat mukhassisa): Accidental properties that are specific to a particular but not essential to its quiddity

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because accidentals are not part of the quiddity of the thing.
D) Because definitions must be based on essential properties only.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition in Hanafi usul must apply perpetually; temporary accidentals cannot ground it.

Only Pointing Can Fully Individuate a Particular
Resolution: only pointing fully individuates a particular

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why universal concepts cannot uniquely identify a particular and why pointing is necessary in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Intellect cannot uniquely pinpoint a particular through universals; only sensory pointing suffices.

The previous lesson showed that definitions relying on accidentals fail. This lesson examines the deeper reason: any description using universal terms shares the potential to apply to multiple individuals, even if only one exists at the moment. True individuation requires direct reference (اشارہ).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the limitation of universals
Any description using general terms is conceptually universal; it could apply to many, even if only one currently satisfies it in reality.
Example: 'the one who came today alone' is a universal concept.
2
Distinguish between existence-based and intellect-based application
In external existence, only one may satisfy the description, but the intellect can conceive of another possible instance.
This shows that conceptual uniqueness is not achieved.
3
Understand the role of pointing
Pointing (اشارہ) directly indicates the specific entity without relying on descriptive content, breaking the conceptual multiplicity.
Pointing can be physical (finger) or contextual (time/place).
4
Apply to legal definitions
In legal texts, general terms (e.g., 'the needy') are universal; a specific instance is identified by its particular context, not by an exclusive definition.
This is why fatwas often refer to specific individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وہ شخص محدود بھی زائل ہو جائیگا یعنی شخص شباب زائل ہو چکا ہے اب یہ دوسرا شخص ہے جو متصف بالشیب ہے لہذا اس وقت صد کا صادق نہ آنا کوئی ضرر رساں نہیں ہے بلکہ واجب ہے کہ جب محدود زائل ہو چکا ہے تو سابقہ حد اس وقت صادق نہ آئے۔ یہ ایک الزام ہے اور تحقیق حق فی الجواب یہ ہے ۔ والمحق ان الشخص الا یعنی حق بات یہ ہے کہ شخصی کی ایسی حد ہو سکتی ہے جو اس کو جمیع اختیار سے امتیاز بحسب الوجود کا افادہ کرے لا بما يفيد تعيينه الا یعنی شخصی کی ایسی عد ممکن نہین ہے جو اس کی پوری تشخیص و تعیین کردے یہاں تک کہ اس کا اشتراک بین الكثيرين بحسب العقل ممکن نہ ہو یہ نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ آپ جتنا ہی عرضیات مشخصہ اشارہ کے بغیر ذکر کریں گے تو وہ تمام عند العقل مفہومات کلیہ ہیں جن کا صدق علی الکثیرین ممکن ہے اگر چه باعتبار وجود خارجی کے صدق علی الکثیرین نہ ہو لیکن عند العقل اس کا صدق على الكثرة ممکن ہے مثلاً من زید کے جواب میں یوں کہا جائے الذى جاءك اليوم وحده قبل كل احد یعنی زید وہ شخص ہے جو آج دن آپ کے پاس سب سے پہلے اکیلا آیا تھا تو باعتبار وجود سے پہلے خارجی کے ایسے دو شخص نہیں ہو سکتے لیکن عقلا اس تشخیص کے باوجود اس میں تعدد ممکن ہے اور صدق على الكثيرين عند العقل ممتنع نہیں ہے عقلاً اس قسم کی تعیین و تشخیص صرف اشارہ کے ساتھ حاصل ہو سکتی ہے۔
The specific also applies to other human beings; then it does not count as distinction. So this type of definition cannot even give the benefit of distinguishing the defined particular from others, which is the least and lowest level of definition; therefore this definition cannot be correct. And if the specifying accidents are mentioned with it, meaning that in the definition of a particular, if along with the constitutive elements of its quiddity, specifying accidents are also mentioned, which are specific to it and beneficial for distinction, then their applying to the defined particular is not necessary perpetually due to the possibility of their cessation. For example, we define Zayd in his time of youth; then the accidents of youth that are presented at that time will cease in the state of old age, so that previous definition will not apply to him in this state of old age. Thus it will not be a definition because the application of the definition to the defined is necessary, whereas it does not apply in this state. It should be clear that what is meant here by definition is the definition of the usuliyyun, i.e., a comprehensive and exclusive description, not the definition of the logicians, which only comprises essential properties; therefore this objection that a definition containing accidents cannot be a definition will not arise. In this view, the second possibility is chosen, i.e., specifying accidents will also be mentioned in the definition. And when these accidents cease, the defined also ceases. That is, the person who was the subject of the accidents of youth, when these accidents cease in the state of old age, then they say that the defined person also ceases. That is, the person of youth has ceased; now this is another person characterized by old age. Therefore, at that time, the definition's non-application is not harmful; rather it is necessary that when the defined has ceased, the previous definition should not apply at that time. This is an objection, and the true investigation in the answer is: the truth is that a particular can have a definition that gives it distinction from all others according to existence, not a definition that gives its specification. That is, a definition that can fully diagnose and specify it, such that its sharing among many is not possible rationally — this cannot be done. Because as much as you mention specifying accidents without pointing, they are all universal concepts intellectually, whose application to many is possible, even if according to external existence they do not apply to many, but intellectually their application to many is possible. For example, in answer to 'Who is Zayd?', one may say: 'The one who came to you today alone before everyone else.' So according to external existence, there cannot be two such persons, but intellectually, despite this diagnosis, multiplicity is possible for it, and application to many is not impossible intellectually. Such specification and diagnosis can only be obtained through pointing.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of definitions (حد) in usul al-fiqh, specifically whether a definition of a particular (شخص) can include accidental properties (عرضیات). The author first critiques that if a definition includes mere accidentals shared by others, it fails to distinguish. Then considers the case where specifying accidentals are included; but these may change (e.g., youth), so the definition would not apply perpetually. A counterargument that the defined person 'ceases' when accidentals change is rejected. The correct position is that a definition of a particular cannot achieve full individuation through universals; only pointing (اشارہ) can uniquely identify a particular. Thus, definitions using universal terms can only distinguish in existence, not intellectually. This is consistent with Hanafi usul that definitions in legal theory aim at جامع و مانع (comprehensive and exclusive) but for particulars, external distinction suffices.

Key Terms
اشارہ (ishara): Pointing; a non-descriptive act that directly indicates a specific particular, breaking conceptual universality.
مفہوم کلی (mafhum kulli): A universal concept that can apply to multiple individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can no definition using words fully specify a particular in the intellect?
A) Because words are too vague.
B) Because any description uses universal concepts that can apply to multiple individuals in the mind.
C) Because Allah has forbidden complete identification.
D) Because accidentals are always changing.

Key Takeaway
Full conceptual individuation of a particular is impossible through description; only direct pointing (اشارہ) can achieve it.

The Definition of 'Surah' and the Danger of Circularity
Critique of a commentator's attempt to avoid circularity in defining 'Surah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi critique of defining 'Surah' in a general sense to avoid circularity, and explain why the technical Sharia definition must be preserved.

Core Idea
Departing from the technical Sharia meaning of 'Surah' to avoid circularity is a violation of usul principles: the zahir and haqiqah must be upheld.

This passage addresses a key dispute in the definition of the Qur'an. A commentator attempted to avoid circularity by defining 'Surah' generally as a section of revealed speech. The Hanafi critic responds that this is an unwarranted departure from the apparent meaning (zahir) and from reality (haqiqah) into metaphor (majaz). We will unpack the reasoning and identify the proper Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue: Circularity in Defining the Qur'an
If 'Surah' is defined technically as a part of the Qur'an, then defining the Qur'an as 'a collection of Surahs' becomes circular because you need knowledge of the Qur'an to know what a Surah is. The commentator sought to break this circle.
This is a classic usul problem: defining a composite by its parts when the parts themselves depend on the composite.
2
Opposing School's Argument: General Definition of Surah
The commentator defined 'Surah' in a general sense: a section of revealed speech, including Torah and Gospel. He cited Ibn al-Hajib's phrase 'by a Surah from it' and the existence of Surahs in other scriptures as evidence.
The general definition avoids circularity because 'Surah' no longer requires knowledge of the Qur'an.
3
Hanafi Critique: Departure from Zahir and Haqiqah
The critic argues that in Sharia terminology, 'Surah' has a specific technical meaning: 'a part of the Qur'an translated, with fixed beginning and end.' The commentator's general meaning is a departure from the apparent (zahir) and from haqiqah to majaz without necessity.
The critic cites al-Kashshaf and other authoritative works as witnesses to the technical definition.
4
Hanafi Response: Distinguishing General Concept from Individual Composite
Circularity only arises when defining a general concept (mufhum kulli). In contrast, defining an individual composite (majmoo' shakhsi) does not lead to circularity. The definition of the Qur'an as a particular book can be made without circularity if we specify the individual Surahs that compose it.
This distinction is crucial: the problem is not in the definition per se but in how it is framed.
5
Thamarah al-Khilaf: Practical Effect on the Definition of the Qur'an
If 'Surah' is taken generally, the definition of the Qur'an as 'a book containing Surahs' becomes independent of prior knowledge. If taken technically, the definition must be carefully phrased to avoid circularity, e.g., by referring to the specific Surahs known from revelation.
The Hanafi position preserves the technical meaning and forces a more precise formulation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور آخر توقیفا مبین ہو یعنی اس کی اول اور آخر کی تبیین من الشارع ہو اور خواہ یہ بعض حصہ قرآن منزل کا ہو یا توراۃ و انجیل کا تو اس صورت میں معرفة سورة معرفة قرآن پر موقوف نہیں ہوئی چونکہ سورۃ کا یہ عمومی مفہوم مراد تھا تو اس لئے ابن حاجب نے کہا بسورة منه ای من الكلام المنزل اگر سورۃ کے مفہوم میں خصوصیت قرآن معتبر ہوتی یعنی سورۃ کا مفہوم بعض من القرآن ہوتا تو منہ کے کہنے کی ضرورت نہیں تھی بدلیل سور الانجیل یہ سورۃ کے عموم مفہوم کی دلیل ہے یعنی سورۃ انجیل و زبور میں بھی ہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ سورۃ کے مفہوم میں خصوصیت قران مجید معتبر نہیں ہے لہذا مفہوم کلی کی اگر تعریف ہو تو بھی دور لازم نہیں آتا۔ جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ شارح نے جو سورۃ کا مفہوم عام پیش کر کے دور کو دفع کرنیکی کوشش کی ہے یہ بالکل عدول عن الظاہر ہے کیونکہ ہر اصطلاح میں اس کے اصطلاحی مفہوم معتبر ہوتے ہیں جو اہل اصطلاح کے نزدیک حقیقہ کا درجہ رکھتے ہیں تو اصطلاح شریعہ میں سورۃ کا وضعی اصطلاحی مفہوم بعض من القرآن المترجم اولہ وآخره توقیفا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ کشاف اور باقی تفاسیر معتبرہ میں سورۃ کی تعریف بایں الفاظ کی گئی ہے الطائفة من القران المترجمة الا لہذا شارح کا یہ عمومی مفہوم مراد لیتا عدوك من الظاهر الى الخفى ومن الحقيقة إلى المجاز العرنی ہے تو مفہوم کلی کی تعریف ہو تو دور لازم آتا ہے علی تعریف ابن الحاجب اگر مجموع شخصی کی تعریف و تمیز ہو تو پھر دو لازم نہیں آتا کمابینہ المصنف رحمہ اللہ تعالیٰ
And its end is clearly fixed, meaning its beginning and end are determined by the Lawgiver. And whether it is a part of the revealed Qur'an or the Torah and the Gospel, in that case, the knowledge of the Surah is not dependent on the knowledge of the Qur'an, because this general meaning of Surah was intended. Therefore, Ibn al-Hajib said: 'by a Surah from it (minhu), i.e., from the revealed speech.' If the meaning of Surah included specificity of the Qur'an, i.e., the meaning of Surah is a part of the Qur'an, then the mention of 'minhu' would not be necessary, as evidenced by the Surahs of the Gospel. This indicates the general meaning of Surah, i.e., Surahs exist in the Gospel and the Psalms. So it becomes known that the specificity of the Noble Qur'an is not considered in the meaning of Surah. Therefore, if the definition is of the general concept, then circularity does not necessarily occur. The response to this is: The commentator, by presenting the general meaning of Surah to repel circularity, has completely deviated from the apparent (zahir) because in every discipline, its technical meaning is considered, which according to the experts holds the status of reality (haqiqah). So in the terminology of Sharia, the conventional technical meaning of Surah is 'a part of the Qur'an translated, whose beginning and end are fixed.' This is why in al-Kashshaf and other authoritative commentaries, the definition of Surah is given in these words: 'a section of the translated Qur'an.' Therefore, the commentator's taking this general meaning is a departure from the apparent to the hidden, and from reality to pure metaphor. So if the definition is of the general concept, then circularity does occur according to the definition of Ibn al-Hajib. But if the definition and distinction of an individual composite (majmoo' shakhsi) is made, then circularity does not occur, as clarified by the author, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute in usul al-fiqh concerning the definition of 'Surah'. The commentator (likely the author of the sharh) attempted to define 'Surah' in a general sense to avoid circularity (dawr) in the definition of the Qur'an. He argued that if 'Surah' is defined generally as a section of revealed speech (including Torah and Gospel), then defining the Qur'an as a book containing Surahs would not require prior knowledge of the Qur'an. The critic responds that this is a departure from the apparent meaning (zahir) because in Sharia terminology, 'Surah' has a specific technical meaning: a part of the Qur'an with fixed beginning and end. Citing authoritative works like al-Kashshaf, the critic asserts that the commentator's general meaning is a metaphorical rather than real usage. The critic further distinguishes between defining a general concept (mufhum kulli) and defining an individual composite (majmoo' shakhsi), showing that circularity only applies to the former. The passage thus refines the commentator's view by insisting on adherence to the technical Sharia definition.

Key Terms
سورة (surah): A part of the Qur'an translated, with a fixed beginning and end determined by the Lawgiver.
دور (dawr): Circularity in definition where the definiendum is used to define the definiens.
عدول عن الظاهر (udool 'an al-zahir): Departure from the apparent meaning of a term without sufficient reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A section of any revealed scripture.
B) A part of the Qur'an translated, with a fixed beginning and end.
C) A synonym for the word 'book'.
D) Any speech that is beneficial.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position insists on the technical Sharia definition of 'Surah' and rejects departures from it, resolving circularity by distinguishing between general concept and individual composite.

The Four Divisions of Lafz Relative to Meaning
Introduces four divisions of lafz relative to meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four divisions of lafz according to the Hanafi usul classification and explain why the division by isti'mal precedes division by zuhur.

Core Idea
Lafz is classified by coinage, usage, clarity, and manner of indication – usage logically precedes clarity.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, lafz (speech) is analyzed through four distinct lenses: how it was coined (wad'), how it is used (isti'mal), how clear its meaning is (zuhur), and how it indicates its meaning (kayfiyyat al-dalalah). This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih explains these divisions and defends the ordering that places usage before clarity, reversing Fakhr al-Islam's sequence. Understanding this taxonomy is essential before diving into terms like 'amm, khas, haqiqah, majaz, zahir, nass, and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first division
The first division classifies lafz by its wad' (linguistic coinage) for a meaning. This yields categories: 'amm (general), khas (specific), and mushtarak (shared). Note that Fakhr al-Islam calls this the 'first regarding forms of nazm.'
This division is about the original meaning fixed by language.
2
Identify the second division
The second division classifies lafz by its isti'mal (usage): whether the word is used in its original meaning (haqiqah, literal) or in a transferred meaning (majaz, metaphorical). The commentator places this before clarity because a word must be used before we can assess its clarity.
This ordering differs from Fakhr al-Islam, who placed zuhur second.
3
Identify the third division
The third division classifies lafz by zuhur al-ma'na (clarity of meaning). Based on how apparent or hidden the meaning is, lafz is divided into zahir, nass, khafi, mushkil, etc. These categories determine how much interpretive effort is needed.
Levels of clarity are crucial for the hierarchy of proof in usul.
4
Identify the fourth division
The fourth division classifies lafz by kayfiyyat al-dalalah (the manner of indication). This leads to distinctions like mantuq (explicit) vs. mafhum (implicit), and further to haqiqah vs. majaz. Fakhr al-Islam calls this 'standing upon the rulings of nazm.'
This division is about the mode of signification, not the content.
5
Understand the ordering logic
The commentator explains why he reversed Fakhr al-Islam's order: isti'mal precedes zuhur because a word must first be used (whether literally or metaphorically) before we can judge whether its meaning is clear or hidden. Without usage, there is no basis for clarity assessment.
This logical priority is a key Hanafi methodological choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باعتبار وضعه له هذا هو التقسيم الاول یعنی تقاسیم اربعہ میں سے تقسیم اول لفظ کی باعتبار وضع للمعنی کے ہے تو کلام با عتبار وضع کے منقسم ہوتی ہے خاص اور عام مشترک کی طرف اسی کو فخر الاسلام نے اپنے اصول میں کہا الاول فی وجوه النظم صیغة ولغة ثم باعتبار استعماله فیه یعنی ثانی تقسیم لفظ کی باعتبار استعمال اللفظ في المعنی کے ہے فین قسم اللفظ یعنی لفظ باعتبار استعمال کے منقسم ہو گا اسکی طرف کہ لفظ اپنے موضوع لہ میں مستعمل ہے یا غیر موضوع لہ میں کما سیجی ثم باعتبار ظهور المعنى الخ یہ لفظ کی تیسری تقسیم ہے کہ لفظ کا معنی ظاہر ہے یا خفی اور مراتب ظہور و خفا بھی بیان کئے جائیں گے وهذا ما قال فخر الاسلام یعنی اسی تقسیم ثالث کو فخر الاسلام نے ثانی تقسم قرار دیا جس کے متعلق کہا ہے الثانی فی وجوہ البیان بذلک النظم انما جعلت هذا التقسيم ثالثا میں نے اس تقسیم کو ثالث اور باعتبار استعمال کو تقسیم ثانی قرار دیا اور فخرالاسلام کی ترتیب کا عکس اختیار کیا اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ استعمال مقدم علی الظہور والخفا ہے یعنی لفظ پہلے مستعمل فی المعنی ہوتا ہے پھر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس کا معنی ظاہر ہے يا خفى - ثم فى كيفية دلالته على المعنی یہ وہی تقسیم رابع ہے جس کے متعلق فخر الاسلام نے کہا والرابع في وجوه الوقوف علی احکام النظم تو تقیم ثانی کے لحاظ سے لفظ منقسم ہو گا الی الحقیقة والمجاز و غیر ھما اور تقسیم ثالث کے لحاظ سے منقسم ہو گا ظاہر ونص و خفی و مشکل و غیر با کی طرف
By consideration of its wad' (coining) for it — this is the first division. That is, among the four divisions, the first division of lafz is by consideration of wad' for meaning. So speech, by consideration of wad', is divided into khas (specific), 'amm (general), and mushtarak (shared). This is what Fakhr al-Islam said in his Usul: 'The first is regarding the forms of nazm: form and language.' Then by consideration of its isti'mal (usage) in it — that is, the second division of lafz is by consideration of the usage of the word in the meaning. So lafz by consideration of usage is divided into whether it is used in its original meaning or in other than its original meaning, as will come. Then by consideration of zuhur al-ma'na (clarity of meaning) — this is the third division of lafz: whether the meaning of the word is apparent or hidden, and the levels of clarity and obscurity will also be mentioned. This is what Fakhr al-Islam said, i.e., this third division he made the second division, about which he said: 'The second is regarding the aspects of bayan (clarification) by that nazm.' I made this division third and made division by isti'mal second, reversing the order of Fakhr al-Islam. The reason is that isti'mal precedes zuhur and khafa: the word is first used in the meaning, then it is known whether its meaning is apparent or hidden. Then regarding the kayfiyya (manner) of its dalalah (indication) on the meaning — this is the fourth division, about which Fakhr al-Islam said: 'The fourth is regarding the aspects of standing upon the rulings of nazm.' So by the second division (usage), lafz is divided into haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), and other than them. And by the third division (clarity), it is divided into zahir, nass, khafi, mushkil, and others.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule establishing the four divisions of lafz (word) relative to meaning. The commentator explains the first division: by wad' (linguistic coinage), lafz is classified into 'amm (general), khas (specific), and mushtarak (homonym). This is Fakhr al-Islam's first category. The second division is by isti'mal (usage), i.e., whether the word is used in its original meaning (haqiqah) or transferred meaning (majaz). The third division is by zuhur al-ma'na (clarity), i.e., how apparent or hidden the meaning is — leading to terms like zahir, nass, khafi, mushkil. The fourth division is by kayfiyyat al-dalalah (manner of indication). The commentator notes that he placed isti'mal before zuhur, reversing Fakhr al-Islam's order, because usage logically precedes knowing the clarity of meaning. Each division serves as a basis for subsequent detailed classifications in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
وضع (wad'): The original coinage of a word for a meaning in the language.
استعمال (isti'mal): The actual usage of a word in speech, either in its original meaning or not.
ظهور المعنى (zuhur al-ma'na): The degree to which the meaning of a word is clear or hidden in context.
دلالة (dalalah): The manner in which a word indicates its meaning (e.g., by context, implication).
خاص (khas): A word that indicates a specific meaning, the opposite of 'amm.
عام ('amm): A word that indicates all members of a category without restriction.
حقيقة (haqiqah): A word used in its original coined meaning.
مجاز (majaz): A word used in a meaning other than its original due to a connection.
ظاهر (zahir): A word whose meaning is clear but still admits the possibility of ta'wil (interpretation).
نص (nass): A word whose meaning is clear and does not admit ta'wil.
خفي (khafi): A word whose meaning is hidden due to some external factor (like idmar).
مشكل (mushkil): A word whose meaning is ambiguous and requires research to resolve.
منطوق (mantuq): The explicit indication of a word in its literal utterance.
مفهوم (mafhum): The implicit indication derived from a word's context (like concept of opposition).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why did he place the division by isti'mal before the division by zuhur?
A) Because Fakhr al-Islam's order was incorrect
B) Because usage is logically prior to clarity
C) Because the matn of al-Tawdih requires it
D) Because clarity is less important than usage

Key Takeaway
Lafz is analyzed through four lenses — wad', isti'mal, zuhur, and kayfiyya — with usage logically prior to clarity.

The Four Divisions of Words: An Overview
Overview of the four divisions of words in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four divisions of words in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and state the logical order preferred by the commentator over Fakhral-Islam's order.

Core Idea
Words are classified by placement, usage, clarity, and indication.

Understanding how words convey legal meanings is fundamental to usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi school divides words into four categories based on their relation to meaning: by wad' (placement), by isti'mal (usage), by zuhur (apparentness) and khafa (hiddenness), and by kayfiyat al-dalala (mode of indication). The commentator in this passage clarifies the logical sequence and addresses why the order differs from that of Fakhral-Islam al-Bazdawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four criteria for dividing words
Look at the passage: it mentions wad', isti'mal, zuhur/khafa, and kayfiyat al-dalala. These are the four bases for classification.
These are the four taqasim arba'ah referred to in the text.
2
Determine the commentator's order
The commentator presents them in the order: wad', isti'mal, zuhur/khafa, dalala. Note that he explicitly says he made the division by usage second and by apparentness third.
3
Compare with Fakhral-Islam's order
Fakhral-Islam al-Bazdawi placed the division by apparentness (zuhur) as second and usage as something else? The commentator reverses this, placing usage before apparentness.
The text states: 'I have made this division [by zuhur] the third and made the division by usage the second, and I adopted the opposite of Fakhral-Islam's order.'
4
Understand the justification for the order
The commentator explains that usage logically precedes determining clarity: a word is first used in a meaning, then we can assess whether its meaning is apparent or hidden.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the natural sequence of speech acts.
5
Note the subcategories of each division
Each division yields distinct classification pairs: wad' → khass, 'amm, mushtarak; isti'mal → haqiqah, majaz; zuhur/khafa → zahir, nass, khafi, mushkil; dalala → 'ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, iqtida' al-nass.
These subcategories are detailed in subsequent lessons.

باعتبار وضعه له هذا هو التقسيم الاول یعنی تقاسیم اربعہ میں سے تقسیم اول لفظ کی باعتبار وضع للمعنی کے ہے تو کلام با عتبار وضع کے منقسم ہوتی ہے خاص اور عام مشترک کی طرف اسی کو فخر الاسلام نے اپنے اصول میں کہا الاول فی وجوه النظم صیغة ولغة ثم باعتبار استعماله فیه یعنی ثانی تقسیم لفظ کی باعتبار استعمال اللفظ في المعنی کے ہے فین قسم اللفظ یعنی لفظ باعتبار استعمال کے منقسم ہو گا اسکی طرف کہ لفظ اپنے موضوع لہ میں مستعمل ہے یا غیر موضوع لہ میں کما سیجی ثم باعتبار ظهور المعنى الخ یہ لفظ کی تیسری تقسیم ہے کہ لفظ کا معنی ظاہر ہے یا خفی اور مراتب ظہور و خفا بھی بیان کئے جائیں گے وهذا ما قال فخر الاسلام یعنی اسی تقسیم ثالث کو فخر الاسلام نے ثانی تقسم قرار دیا جس کے متعلق کہا ہے الثانی فی وجوہ البیان بذلک النظم انما جعلت هذا التقسيم ثالثا میں نے اس تقسیم کو ثالث اور باعتبار استعمال کو تقسیم ثانی قرار دیا اور فخرالاسلام کی ترتیب کا عکس اختیار کیا اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ استعمال مقدم علی الظہور والخفا ہے یعنی لفظ پہلے مستعمل فی المعنی ہوتا ہے پھر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس کا معنی ظاہر ہے يا خفى - ثم فى كيفية دلالته على المعنی یہ وہی تقسیم رابع ہے جس کے متعلق فخر الاسلام نے کہا والرابع في وجوه الوقوف علی احکام النظم تو تقیم ثانی کے لحاظ سے لفظ منقسم ہو گا الی الحقیقة والمجاز و غیر ھما اور تقسیم ثالث کے لحاظ سے منقسم ہو گا ظاہر ونص و خفی و مشکل و غیر با کی طرف
اور تقسیم رابع کے لحاظ سے منقسم ہو گا دلالتہ النص وعمارة النص وغير معما کی طرف . قال الشارح في التلويح قوله لما كان القران يريد ان اللفظ الم مصنف نے قسم اللفظ بالنسبة إلی المعنی کہا اگر لفظ معنی سے مراد موضوع لہ ہو تو پھر مجاز کو ہی تقسیم سے خالج ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ مجاز میں معنی موضوع لہ مراد نہیں ہوتا اس لئے شارح نے تشریح کرتے ہوئے کہا یرید ان اللفظ الدال على المعنى بالوضع لا بد له من وضع للمعنی تو اس عبارت میں شارح نے من وضع کے اندر لفظ وضع کو نکرہ کر دیا تاکہ لفظ وضع شخصی اور نوشی کو شامل ہو جائے اور من وضع للمعنی میں المعنی سے عام معنی مراد ہے جو موضوع لہ اور غیر موضوع لہ کو شامل ہے تو اس لحاظ سے تقسیمات اربعہ اس میں مندرج ہو سکتی ہیں یا یوں بھی کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ معنی سے مراد معنی موضوع لہ ہو اور باعتبار وضعہ کے اندر با ملابستہ کی ہو اور تقسیم متلبس باعتبار الاستعمال مجاز کو شامل ہو جائے گی اور تلبس باعتبار الوضع تقسیم رابع جو عبارة النص اور اشارہ وغیرہ کی طرف ہے اس کو بھی شامل ہو جائے گی جیسے دلالتہ لفظیہ وضعیہ تضمنی اور التزامی کو شامل ہے حالانکہ معنی تضمینی اور التزامی لفظ کا موضوع لہ نہیں ہے صرف اعتبار وضع کے ساتھ ان کو تلبس ہو سکتا ہے بہر حال لفظ جو دال علی المعنى بالوضع ہوتا ہے اس کے لئے ایک تو وضع برائے معنی کا ہونا ضروری دوسرا اس معنی میں لفظ کی استعمال تیسرا اس معنی پر دلالتہ لفظ اگر تقسیم باعتبار وضع للمعنی کے ہو تو یہ تقسیم اول ہے اگر باعتبار استعمال في المعنی کے لحاظ سے ہے تو یہ تقسیم ثانی ہے اگر تقسیم لفظ باعتبار دلالات على المعنی کے ہے اگر اس کے اندر ظہور معنی اور اس کے خفا کا لحاظ ہے تو یہ ہے والا فهو الرابع - وجعل الدمام في الاسلام یعنی امام فخرالاسلام نے ان تمام اقسام کو اقسام نظم اور معنی قرار دیا ہے اور انھوں نے پہلی تقسیمات ثلثہ کے اقسام یعنی خاص وعام وغیرہ حقیقت و مجاز وغیرہ اور ظاہر و حفی وغیرہ کو صفہ لفظ قرار دیا اور وہ اقسام جو تقسیم رابع سے برآمد ہوئے یعنی عبارة النص واشارة النص وغیرہ کو ایک بار تعبیر کیا استدلال بالعبارة وبالاشارة وبالدلالة و بالاقتضا اور کبھی یوں تعبیر کی استدلال بالعباره و بالاشارہ یعنی ان کے ساتھ لفظ استدلال استعمال کیا اور ثابت بالدلالہ والاقتضا یعنی ان کے ساتھ لفظ ثابت استعمال کیا دتار چاروں کے ساتھ لفظ وقوف کا استعمال کیا جو واقفیت سے ماخوذ ہے کہا الوقوف بعبارة النصل الى آخره
Rather, they considered the meaning alone sufficient for the permissibility of prayer regarding the fulfillment of the obligation of reciting the Qur'an, so much so that if a person recites in non-Arabic without an excuse during prayer, the prayer would be valid. And he [the author] said 'especially' meaning he specified the permissibility of prayer because in other rulings besides prayer, the [Arabic] wording is deemed necessary, such as the recitation of a junub or a menstruating woman—meaning the recitation of the Qur'an that is prohibited for them is the recitation of the Arabic wording; if they read a verse of the Qur'an in Persian, it is permissible for them because it is not truly the Qur'an, since the Arabic wording is not included. Therefore, a translation in the Persian language will not be called Qur'an. But the more correct view is that Imam [Abu Hanifa] has retracted from this statement—that wording is not a necessary pillar for the permissibility of prayer—so the text of al-Tanqih did not mention this statement. Rather, I say: rather, the text said that the Noble Qur'an is expression and interpretation from the wording indicating the meaning. The mashayikh who said that the Qur'an is the name of wording and meaning, their intention is also wording indicating meaning.

By its placement (wad') for it: this is the first division. That is, among the four divisions, the first division of the word is according to the placement for meaning. So speech is divided by placement into specific, general, and common. Fakhral-Islam said in his Usul: 'The first is regarding the aspects of wording: form and language.' Then according to its usage in it: that is, the second division of the word is according to the usage of the word in meaning. So the word is divided according to usage: whether the word is used in its assigned meaning or not, as will come. Then according to the manifestation of meaning, etc.: this is the third division of the word: whether the meaning of the word is apparent or hidden, and the levels of manifestation and concealment will also be explained. And this is what Fakhral-Islam said: that is, he considered this third division as the second division, regarding which he said: 'The second is regarding the aspects of clarification by that wording.' I have made this division the third and made the division by usage the second, and I adopted the opposite of Fakhral-Islam's order. The reason is that usage precedes manifestation and concealment: the word is first used in a meaning, then it is known whether its meaning is apparent or hidden. Then regarding how it indicates the meaning: this is the fourth division, regarding which Fakhral-Islam said: 'The fourth is regarding the aspects of understanding the rulings of the wording.' So with respect to the second division, the word is divided into real, metaphorical, and others. With respect to the third division, it is divided into apparent, explicit, hidden, difficult, and others. And with respect to the fourth division, it is divided into indication of the text, implication of the text, and others. The commentator said in al-Talwih: 'His statement: since the [author] intended...' The author said the division of the word with respect to meaning: if by meaning the assigned meaning is intended, then metaphor should be excluded from the division because in metaphor the assigned meaning is not intended. Therefore, the commentator clarified by saying: 'He intends that the word indicating the meaning by placement must have a placement for the meaning.' So in this expression, the commentator made 'placement' indefinite in the phrase 'from placement' so that it includes specific placement and generic placement. And in 'from placement for meaning', the word 'meaning' is general, encompassing the assigned and non-assigned meaning. Thus, from this perspective, the four divisions can be included in it. Or it can also be said that by meaning, the assigned meaning is intended, and in 'by its placement' there is an association, and the division adorned by usage will include metaphor, and the division adorned by placement will include the fourth division which is text expression, indication, etc. For example, it includes verbal, placed, implied, and necessary indications, even though the implied and necessary meanings are not the assigned meanings of the word; they can only be adorned with the consideration of placement. In any case, a word that indicates a meaning by placement needs: first, a placement for the meaning is necessary; second, usage of the word in that meaning; third, the indication of the word for that meaning. If the division is according to placement for meaning, this is the first division; if according to usage in meaning, this is the second division; if the division of the word is according to indication of meaning, and if within it there is consideration of manifestation of meaning and its concealment, then this is the third, and the remaining is the fourth. And Imam Fakhral-Islam made all these divisions as divisions of wording and meaning. He considered the divisions of the first three types—specific, general, etc.; real, metaphorical, etc.; and apparent, hidden, etc.—as attributes of the word. And the divisions that emerged from the fourth division, i.e., text expression, text indication, etc., he sometimes expressed as inference by expression, by indication, by implication, and by requirement; and sometimes he expressed as inference by expression and by indication, i.e., he used the word 'inference' with them, and 'established' by implication and requirement, i.e., he used the word 'established' with them. The author used the word 'understanding' with all four, derived from 'familiarity', saying: 'the understanding by text expression... etc.'
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage from a commentary on al-Tawdih (by Sadr al-Shariah) and al-Talwih (by al-Taftazani) discusses the classification of words (alfaz) in usul al-fiqh according to their relation to meaning. The author presents four divisions (taqasim arba'ah): (1) by wad' (linguistic placement) — this yields words like khass (specific), 'amm (general), and mushtarak (common); (2) by isti'mal (usage) — whether the word is used in its assigned meaning (haqiqah) or not (majaz); (3) by zulur (apparentness) and khafa (hiddenness) — categories like zahir, nass, khafi, mushkil; and (4) by kayfiyat al-dalala (mode of indication) — such as 'ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. The commentator notes that Fakhral-Islam (al-Bazdawi) presented these in a different order, making the division by usage second and by apparentness third. The commentator justifies his order by explaining that usage logically precedes knowing whether the meaning is apparent or hidden. The passage also addresses a potential objection: if the first division is by wad', then majaz (metaphor) would be excluded because it is not used in its assigned meaning. The commentator resolves this by interpreting the phrase 'al-lafz al-dall 'ala al-ma'na bi al-wad'' broadly: 'ma'na' can include both assigned and non-assigned meanings, or the division by wad' can be understood to include an association (bi al-mulabasah) that encompasses majaz. This shows the Hanafi method of careful definition to include all legal categories.

Key Terms
وضع (wad'): The linguistic assignment of a word to a specific meaning.
استعمال (isti'mal): The usage of a word in a meaning, whether in its assigned meaning or not.
ظهور (zuhur): The clarity or apparentness of the meaning of a word.
دلالة (dalala): The indication of a word towards its meaning, including 'ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the division by usage (isti'mal) placed before the division by apparentness (zuhur)?
A) Because usage is more frequently invoked in legal reasoning.
B) Because a word must first be used before its clarity can be assessed.
C) Because Fakhral-Islam made a mistake.
D) Because the division by apparentness is less important.

Key Takeaway
The four divisions of words provide a comprehensive framework for analyzing legal texts in Hanafi usul, and their order reflects the logical sequence of linguistic operations.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Four Types of Textual Indication in Hanafi Usul
Explains the fourth division of words and its four types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and differentiate the four types of textual indication ('ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida') and state the Hanafi position on each.

Core Idea
A text reveals its ruling through four channels: explicit words, implied context, inferred ratio, and necessary presupposition.

This lesson unpacks the fourth division of words in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh. The commentator explains how the same text can yield multiple legal implications through different analytical lenses. Understanding these four modes is essential for deriving rulings beyond the surface meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Types
Extract the four Arabic terms for textual indication from the passage: 'ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida'. Note each is defined in the key terms.
These are the four components of the fourth division.
2
Define Each Type
For 'ibarah: the explicit meaning from wording. isharah: implied meaning from context. dalalah: inferred meaning by ratio legis (illah). iqtida: a meaning necessary for coherence.
The text gives examples: 'ibarah and isharah are direct; dalalah and iqtida are secondary.
3
Understand the Role of Wad' (Convention)
The word must have a conventional placement (wad') for a meaning. This conditions all four types—even iqtida requires the text to be valid.
Metaphor (majaz) is excluded when meaning is restricted to wad'.
4
Distinguish from Earlier Divisions
The first three divisions (amm/khass, haqiqah/majaz, zahir/khafi) concern the word itself. The fourth concerns the word's indication of meaning beyond the literal.
This is why the fourth division is about 'indication of the text' (dalalat al-nass).

پر دلالتہ لفظ اگر تقسیم باعتبار وضع للمعنی کے ہو تو یہ تقسیم اول ہے اگر باعتبار استعمال في المعنی کے لحاظ سے ہے تو یہ تقسیم ثانی ہے اگر تقسیم لفظ باعتبار دلالات على المعنی کے ہے اگر اس کے اندر ظہور معنی اور اس کے خفا کا لحاظ ہے تو یہ ہے والا فهو الرابع - ثالث وجعل الدمام في الاسلام یعنی امام فخرالاسلام نے ان تمام اقسام کو اقسام نظم اور معنی قرار دیا ہے اور انھوں نے پہلی تقسیمات ثلثہ کے اقسام یعنی خاص وعام وغیرہ حقیقت و مجاز وغیرہ اور ظاہر و حفی وغیرہ کو صفہ لفظ قرار دیا اور وہ اقسام جو تقسیم رابع سے برآمد ہوئے یعنی عبارة النص واشارة النص وغیرہ کو ایک بار تعبیر کیا استدلال بالعبارة وبالاشارة وبالدلالة و بالاقتضا اور کبھی یوں تعبیر کی استدلال بالعباره و بالاشارہ یعنی ان کے ساتھ لفظ استدلال استعمال کیا اور ثابت بالدلالہ والاقتضا یعنی ان کے ساتھ لفظ ثابت استعمال کیا دتار چاروں کے ساتھ لفظ وقوف کا استعمال کیا جو واقفیت سے ماخوذ ہے کہا الوقوف بعبارة النصل الى آخره وذكر في تفسيرها اور ان کی تفسیر میں ایسے امور ذکر کئے جو صفہ للمعنی ہونے پر دال ہیں کا لثابت بالنظم مقصوراً یعنی ان کا اثبات نظم سے بالقصد وبالذات ہو یا وہ مقصود بالذات نہیں بلکہ ان کا اثبات بالتبع ہے یہ عبارة النص واشارۃ النص کی طرف اشارہ ہے والثابت بمعنى النظم یہ دلالة النص ہے والثابت زيادة على النص یعنی بعض احکام کے اثبات کے لئے زیادہ علی النص کرنی پڑتی اور یہ زیادتی صحت نص کے لئے شرط کے درجہ میں ہوتی ہے اس کے بغیر مفہوم نص صحیح نہیں ہو سکتا یہ اقتضاء النص ہوتا ہے نذهب بعضهم اس لئے بعض حضرت کا یہ خیال ہے کہ تقسیم رابع کے اقسام معنی کے اقسام ہیں۔ اور ہوائی اقسام ثلثہ نظم کے اقسام ہیں اور بعض کا خیال یہ تھا کہ صرف دلالة النص اور اقتضا النص اقسام معنی ہیں اور بواقی اقسام نظم ہیں وصرح المصنف مصنف نے تصریح فرمادی ہے کہ یہ تمام اقسام نظم بالنسبة الى المعنی کے اقسام ہیں۔ . اخذ أبا الحاصل الم یعنی ایک تو مشائخ کی عبارات کا جوالحاصل اور خلاصہ تھا اس کو لے لیا و میلاً الى الضبط اور اس صورت میں چونکہ ضبط اقسام درست ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے میلان الی الضبط کیا اور جمیع کو اقسام نظم قرار دیا لیکن چونکہ تقسیم رابع کے اقسام میں ثابت بالنص يا وقوف بعبارۃ وغیرہ کے الفاظ ذکر کئے گئے ہیں یہ تو اقسام نظم نہیں ہو سکتے کیونکہ ثبوت یا وقوف بالعبارة یہ تو اوصاف معنی ہیں اوصاف نظم نہیں ہیں تو شارح نے اس سوال کو مرتفع کرتے ہوئے کہا خاقسام التقسم الرابع هو الم یعنی تقسیم الرابع کے اقسام کی یہ تعبیر اختیار کرلی الدال بطريق العبارة والاشارہ اور دلالۃ صفہ لفظ ہے اس لئے ان اقسام کا تعلق نظم سے ہو سکتا ہے مشائخ کی عبارات مختلفہ کی طرف التفات نہیں کی بلکہ حاصل معنی کو لے لیا کیونکہ اختلاف عبارات یہ مشائخ کی عادت ہے لیکن مقصود ایک ہوتا ہے اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ اختلاف عبارات کو ترک کر کے وحدہ مقصود کی طرف التفات ہونی چاہتے توان عبارات مختلفہ کا حاصل یہی ہے کہ یہ نظم بالنسبتہ الی المعنی کی تقسیم اور اقسام ہیں۔ بحمل قولهم آل یعنی مشائخ کے اس قول سے کہ یہ نظم اور معنی کے اقسام ہیں یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ بعض اقسام نظم ہیں اور بعض اقسام معنی بلکہ اس قول کی مراد بھی یہی ہے کہ یہ نظم دال علی المعنی کے اقسام ہیں ۔ کما قالو القران هو النظم والمعنی جیسے اس قول میں النظم والمعنی سے دو الگ الگ چیزیں معتبر نہیں ہے بلکہ مراد و سی نظم دال علی المعنی ہے اسی طرح اقسام
And according to the fourth division, it will be divided into: indication of the text, construction of the text, and other than that. The commentator said in al-Talwih: 'His statement: since the Qur'an intends that the word...' The author divided the word in relation to meaning. If by meaning is intended the meaning for which it is placed, then metaphor should be excluded from the division because in metaphor the meaning for which it is placed is not intended. Therefore the commentator clarified saying: 'He intends that the word that indicates the meaning by convention must have a convention for the meaning.' In this expression the commentator made 'wad'' indefinite so that it includes specific and generic convention. And 'convention for the meaning' includes general meaning which covers both the meaning for which it is placed and other than that. In this respect, the four divisions can be included in it. Or it can be said that by meaning is intended the meaning for which it is placed, but with respect to its convention and connection, and the division of 'mutalabbis' by consideration of usage will include metaphor, and 'mutalabbis' by consideration of convention will include the fourth division which is expression of the text and indication etc., just as verbal conventional indication includes implicit and concomitant, even though the implicit and concomitant meanings are not the original meanings of the word, they can only be connected with it by consideration of convention. In any case, the word that indicates the meaning by convention requires: first, a convention for the meaning; second, usage of the word in that meaning; third, indication of the word upon that meaning. If the division is by consideration of convention for the meaning, this is the first division; if by consideration of usage in the meaning, this is the second division; if the division of the word is by consideration of indications upon the meaning, and if within it there is consideration of the clarity and obscurity of the meaning, then this is the third, and the one that is this, that is the fourth. And he made al-Imam, meaning Imam Fakhr al-Islam, considered all these divisions as divisions of text and meaning. And he considered the divisions of the first three categories, i.e., specific and general etc., reality and metaphor etc., clear and obscure etc., as attributes of the word. And the divisions that came from the fourth division, i.e., expression of the text, indication of the text etc., he sometimes expressed as 'inference by expression, by indication, by implication, and by requirement', and sometimes expressed as 'inference by expression and by indication', i.e., he used the word 'inference' with them, and 'established by implication and requirement', i.e., he used the word 'established' with them; then he used the word 'pause' with all four, which is derived from acquaintance, he said: 'the pause at the expression of the text... to the end.' And he mentioned in its explanation matters that indicate that they are attributes of meaning, such as 'established by the text restrictively', meaning their establishment from the text is intentional and essential, or they are not intended essentially but their establishment is incidental; this refers to expression of the text and indication of the text. And 'established by meaning of the text' is implication of the text. And 'established as additional to the text' means for the establishment of some rulings one must go beyond the text, and this additional element is in the position of a condition for the validity of the text, without which the meaning of the text is not correct; this is requirement of the text. Some went so far as to hold the opinion that the divisions of the fourth division are divisions of meaning, and the three other categories are divisions of text. And some held the opinion that only implication of the text and requirement of the text are divisions of meaning, and the remaining are divisions of text. And the author explicitly stated that all these divisions are divisions of text in relation to meaning. He took the summary and essence of the statements of the early scholars and leaned toward organization, and because in this way the organization of divisions becomes correct, he leaned toward organization and made all of them divisions of text. But since in the divisions of the fourth division phrases like 'established by the text' or 'pause at expression' etc. are mentioned, these cannot be divisions of text because establishing or pausing at expression are attributes of meaning, not attributes of text. So the commentator, removing this objection, said: 'the divisions of the fourth division are that he adopted this expression: indicating by way of expression and indication', and indication is an attribute of the word, therefore these divisions can be related to text. He did not pay attention to the various expressions of the early scholars but took the essential meaning, because difference in expressions is the habit of the early scholars but the purpose is one. Therefore it is necessary to abandon difference in expressions and pay attention to the unity of purpose. So the summary of these various expressions is that this is a division of text in relation to meaning. And by interpreting their statement that these are divisions of text and meaning, it is not meant that some divisions are text and some are meaning, rather the meaning of that statement is also that these are divisions of text that indicate meaning, just as they said 'the Qur'an is the text and the meaning', in this statement text and meaning are not considered two separate things, rather what is meant is the text that indicates meaning, similarly the divisions.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih addresses the classification of words (alfaz) in Usul al-Fiqh according to the Hanafi school. The author explains that words can be divided in relation to meaning, and the fourth division concerns the types of indication derived from the text: 1) 'Ibarat al-nass (explicit expression), 2) Isharat al-nass (implicit indication), 3) Dalalat al-nass (inferred meaning), and 4) Iqtida' al-nass (required meaning). The passage clarifies that the word 'wad'' (convention) is used in a general sense to include both specific and generic placements. The early Hanafi scholar Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi considered the first three divisions (specific/general, reality/metaphor, clear/obscure) as attributes of the word (sifat al-lafz), and the fourth division as attributes of meaning. However, the author of the text under commentary (probably Sadr al-Shari'ah) explicitly states that all these are divisions of the text (nazm) in relation to meaning. The commentator resolves an apparent contradiction: the phrases used by earlier scholars, such as 'established by the text' or 'pause at expression', seem to describe meanings, not words. The commentator argues that these should be understood as divisions of the word's indication (dalalah), which is an attribute of the word. Therefore, the fourth division pertains to the word's function in conveying meaning, making them divisions of the text as indicator. The passage concludes that differing expressions among scholars should not obscure the unified purpose: all these divisions concern the word as a signifier of meaning, just as the Qur'an is both text and meaning but considered as a single entity.

Key Terms
عبارة النص ('Ibarat al-nass): The explicit meaning directly from the wording of the text
اشارة النص (Isharat al-nass): A meaning that is implied by the text but not directly stated, usually from context
دلالة النص (Dalalat al-nass): A meaning derived by analogy from the ratio legis of the text
اقتضاء النص (Iqtida' al-nass): A meaning that must be assumed for the text to be coherent, even if not explicitly stated
نظم (Nazm): The composed text or wording itself

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of textual indication applies when a ruling is derived from understanding that the text cannot be literally true without assuming an unstated condition?
A) 'Ibarat al-nass
B) Isharat al-nass
C) Dalalat al-nass
D) Iqtida' al-nass

Key Takeaway
The fourth division ('ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida') classifies how a text indicates rulings beyond its explicit words.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Are the Four Dalaalat Divisions of Nazm or Ma'na?
Resolving dispute over whether the four dalaalat are divisions of nazm or ma'na

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the classification of the four dalaalat and apply the principle that nazm indicates meaning, distinguishing it from ma'na as a separate entity.

Core Idea
All four dalaalat are divisions of nazm indicating meaning — the text's form governs its implication.

This passage addresses a foundational question in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: are the four types of textual indication (ibarah, isharah, dalaalah, iqtidaa) attributes of the wording (nazm) or of the meaning (ma'na)? The discussion is not merely terminological; it affects how we derive rulings from the primary sources. By understanding the Hanafi resolution, you will grasp why the school treats the text's structure as determinative for legal inference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State whether the four dalaalat are divisions of nazm or ma'na according to different scholars. Note the three views: (1) fourth division is ma'na, rest are nazm; (2) dalaalah and iqtidaa are ma'na; (3) all are nazm.
The 'fourth division' likely refers to a specific category among the four dalaalat, possibly iqtidaa.
2
Analyze the Hanafi argument
Examine the proof: expressions like 'established by text' refer to nazm's function. The mashayikh's phrase 'divisions of nazm and meaning' means nazm that indicates meaning—not two separate entities.
Analogous to saying 'the Quran is nazm and meaning' meaning nazm-bearing-meaning.
3
Address the objection
Some object that attributes like 'stopping at expression' are qualities of ma'na. The sharh responds by showing that these terms describe how nazm conveys meaning; they are still functions of nazm.
The sharh does not rely on conflicting mashayikh statements but takes the essential meaning.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If dalaalat are attributes of nazm, rulings are textually fixed; if of ma'na, ijtihad becomes more flexible. The Hanafi position restricts derivation to the text's form.
This affects the scope of qiyas and istihsan in practice.
5
Conclude the tarjih
The musannif explicitly states all are divisions of nazm relative to meaning, and this is the relied-upon position.
The text endorses this as the sound view, aligned with the Hanafi emphasis on nazm.
